فيقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب، ثم ليسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبها فإذا بطل الأصل الذي به العالم وهلك، مع الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلاكه انقلاب غير وقيامه، مع ما يكون في الهيولى تلفها، فتصير هي بلا قوة التقليب، فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما، فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما في الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث لم يكن يصلح إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك، فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض كان كذلك، كل على جعله يصلح لشيء كذلك و بعد، فإن القوة إذ هي قلبته بالطبع فهي غير مفارقة عنه، فما بالها خلت عن عملها في القدم، وذو الطبع لا يخلو عن عمله في الشاهد. على أن الأعراض التي أحدثت إما أن كانت في الهيولى فيبطل قوله: كانت خالية عنها حتى حدثت، أو لم يكن فحدثت من غير شيء؛ إذ وصف القوة بما وصف به الهيولى، ولم يكن فيه أعراض، فثبت أيضا كونها لا عن من باب العدد، فلم يكن فلم يكن ثمة حدث، وقد أوجب هنالك، أو هي هيولى. فيبطل قوله: هي مع الهيولى، أو هي التي قلبت الهيولى، وكأنها قلبت نفسها لا الهيولى. مع ما زعم أن تلك الأعراض اعترضت في الهيولى فحركته وسكنته ودفعته وخفضته من غير أن كان ثمة غير إليه تتحرك أو فيه يسكن أو إليه يرتفع وينحط، ووجود أمثال فاسد فما عنه تولده، فهي في أصله أشد فسادا. وزعم محمد بن شبيب أنه يسمى القوة حركة، وفي روايته أنها لا توصف بما لا توصف به الهيولى، وقد ذكر عنهم الآراء في الهيولى، فلا أدري أيصح ذا أو لا؟ إلا أن سمى القوة حركة وهي فيه، فيبطل قوله: إن الهيولى لا يوصف بحركة إذ قد وصفه بها. لا يتجلو من أن يكون مماسة له أو مباينة عنه، وأيهما قال، فيه إثبات الجسمية والعرضية؛ إذ البينونة والمماسة غير الذي يماس ويباين. ثم قول هؤلاء أن حدثت الجواهر من حركات الأصل، وكذلك قول المنجمة، ومعلوم وجود جواهر من علو وسفل ومن كل Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist theory that an inherent power (quwwa) in primordial matter (hayula) causes change and the generation of the world. Imam al-Maturidi systematically dismantles this claim by showing its internal contradictions. First, he argues that if the world is composed of a power that turns matter, then the world would be subject to perpetual destruction and change, but its actual existence indicates a wise maker, not a blind power. Second, he questions why the power, if it is inseparable from matter by nature, did not act from eternity—since in the observed world, a natural power never remains idle. Third, he examines the production of accidents: either they existed in matter from eternity (contradicting the claim that matter was originally devoid of them) or they occurred from nothing (which implies creation ex nihilo, something the materialists deny). He then turns the argument against them: if power is described as matter is, it becomes a second entity, leading to an infinite regress or to the absurdity that power turns itself. Next, he addresses Muhammad ibn Shabib's identification of power with motion, showing that if motion is in matter, then matter becomes subject to motion, contradicting the claim that matter is not described by motion. He concludes that matter either is contiguous to motion or separate, both of which imply corporeality and accidentality. Finally, he cites al-Nazzām's objection: if turning power causes diverse accidents like color, taste, etc., they would all occur at once from a single motion, but observation shows they differ and come from multiple directions. Muhammad ibn Shabib also argues that matter and accidents are not long individually, yet combined they become long—this absurdity shows the theory fails. The overall point is that the materialist explanation is incoherent, and the existence of the world points to a wise Creator.

What does Maturidi argue would happen if power is described as matter is described?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused your own moral failures by thinking 'it's just my nature' or 'my circumstances made me do it'? This lesson shows that attributing power to matter leads to infinite regress of excuses. What would it mean for you to instead see your power to choose as a direct gift from Allah, holding you accountable? Can you identify one area where you have been using a materialist excuse, and commit to taking responsibility starting today?
?
Maturidi exposes the absurdity of thinking that diverse effects can come from a single, undifferentiated cause. In your own life, do you sometimes treat Allah's actions as if they were the product of blind, uniform forces? How does recognizing the infinite wisdom and power behind every diversity in creation change the way you experience pain, joy, or hardship? Will you begin to see each unique event as a direct sign from the Creator?
?
The argument shows that matter cannot produce motion or length without external cause. Consider your own spiritual deadness: have you been waiting for 'matter' (habits, environment, time) to change you? This lesson demands that you stop expecting the physical world to revive your soul. Instead, will you turn directly to the One who gives power and motion, and ask Him to move your heart today?

The Example of Quicklime and the Principle of Inference
Example and methodological principle for inferring the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the interaction of quicklime and arsenic illustrates the need for a cause beyond mere natures, and the methodological principle of inferring the unseen from the observed.

Core Idea
Observed effects point beyond themselves to a cause that is not directly seen.

Maturidi begins with a concrete example: quicklime and arsenic alone do not burn, but together they do. This raises the question: what changes? He then introduces a foundational principle for discussing the unseen—either rely on revelation or infer from the observed. This lesson unpacks that example and its methodological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the example carefully
Read the Arabic about quicklime and arsenic. Notice that each alone does not burn, but together they do. Ask yourself: why?
The example is not about chemistry but about causal reasoning.
2
Identify the question posed
Maturidi poses a hypothetical: what if one substance actually burns but has an internal preventer? This shows the complexity of explaining effects solely by natures.
3
Understand the methodological principle
After the example, Maturidi states the principle: in matters of the unseen (like stars and natures), one must either use revelation (sam') or infer from the observed to the unseen (al-hadir 'ala al-gha'ib).
This principle is key to Islamic theology.
4
See how this invalidates materialist claims
The observed world is in a certain state; by existence, its cause must have that quality. This refutes claims that the world is eternal through mixture or movement.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأجاب بالنورة والزرنيخ، أن كل واحد منهما على الانفراد لا يحرق ، يمنع عنهم وعند الاجتماع يحرق . فيقال : ما يبعد أن يكون أحدهما يحرق لكن فيه ما عن الإحراق ، وفى الآخر ما يمنع هذا المانع عن المانع فيحرق ، لا أن لم يكن فيه إحراق ، أو كلاهما كانا كذلك ، وأمر الأعراض عندك على ما ذكرنا ، ومحال حلول المانع فيه لو كان طويلا أو سوادا وكذا في الهيولى ؛ لذلك اختلفا قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل فى هذا عندنا وفيما ذكر من النجوم والطبائع أن لا يخلو من أن يرجع في ذلك إلى السمع، وفيهم سماع أهل التوحيد أثبت براهين الصدق أو يستدل بالحاضر الموجود على الغائب ، فإن كان هذا معهم طريقه فيجب ؛ إذ الموجود على حال وبالوجود اعتباره - أن يكون الذي به وجد بهذه الصفة ، فيبطل قولهم فى حدوث العالم فيبطل قولهم فى حدوث العالم بالامتزاج ويتحرك النجوم ، وتقليب القوة الهيولى ، والهيولى والقوة جميعا ، وإن كان على اعتبار معان في الموجود يدل عليه فان الأصل أن كل ذي طبع لا يتغير عما عليه إلى خلاف إلا بمغير حكيم أو سفيه ، لكن يظهر أمرهما بالعواقب ، فمثله الأصل الذي أشاروا إليه إنه لا يصير على غير تلك الحال مما يصلح عواقبه إلا بحكيم ؛ إذ هي وذلك يبطل أصلهم ويثبت أن الأصل احتمل ما احتمل يجعل غيره كذلك ، وفى ذلك حدثه بمحدث حكيم ، وبالله التوفيق وأيضا أن المعلوم فيما كان طبعه الإحراق أنه لا يحرق إلا المطبوع لاحتمال الإحتراق، وكذا التسويد وكل حال وجوهر ، ثم ليس في طبع المحتمل الرفع إلى [؟] القابل فيه بالطبع ، ولا في طبع المحرق أن إلى من يحتمل ذلك ، ومن أراد في الشاهد ذلك لا يتهيأ له دون العلم بالوجود والجمع بينهما ، فعلى ذلك أمر ذلك يصير كذلك ، فيه ، والله الموفق . هم تلك الأصول التى قالوها في موات لا تدبير لهن الغائب ، فيبطل الذى راموا إثباته ويصير هو بمعنى ما ما إذا كان مع جميع ويعملن بالطبع لا اختيار لمن لم يجز أن يكون فيما منه وجود به يحيى عالما سميعا بصيرا قادرا حيا ميتا محتملا لجهات ذلك ، خارجا من احتمال ذلك ، ثبت كون ذلك كله بالمكون العليم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
He responded with [an example of] quicklime and arsenic: that each one of them alone does not burn, [but] it prevents [burning] from them, and when combined they burn. So it is said: what is improbable that one of them burns but there is in it that which prevents burning, and in the other that which prevents this preventer from preventing, so it burns, not that there was no burning in it, or both were like that. And the matter of accidents according to you is as we mentioned, and it is impossible for the preventer to inhere in it, whether it be long or black, and likewise in the hyle; therefore they differed. The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The principle in this according to us, and in what has been mentioned of the stars and natures, is that it cannot be free from either referring back in that to hearing (sam'), or among them the hearing of the people of tawhid establishes proofs of truth, or using the present existing to infer the absent (gha'ib). If this is their way, then it is necessary; for the existent is in a state, and by existence its consideration—that which by it exists with this description—so their statement about the temporality of the world is invalidated, their statement about the temporality of the world through mixture and the movement of the stars, and the turning of the power of the hyle, and the hyle and power together is invalidated. And if it is based on considering meanings in the existent that indicate it, then the principle is that every possessor of a nature does not change from its state to contrary except by a wise or foolish changer, but their outcome is made manifest by consequences. So similar to this is the principle they referred to: that it does not become upon other than that state such that its consequences are sound except by a wise [agent]; since that invalidates their principle and establishes that the principle which admitted what it admitted, makes another like it. And in that is its being temporally originated by a wise originator. And with Allah is success. And also that it is known that what has the nature of burning only burns what is predisposed to burning due to possibility of combustion, and likewise blackening and every state and substance. Then it is not in the nature of the one that receives to be raised to the [؟] receiver by nature, nor in the nature of the burner to [go] to the one that receives that. And whoever intends that in the witnessed realm cannot accomplish it without knowledge of existence and combination between them. So upon that the matter becomes likewise. And Allah is the Grantor of success. Those are the principles they mentioned about lifeless things that have no management for the absent, thus what they sought to prove is invalidated, and it becomes meaning that which is with all? and they act by nature, no choice for one who does not allow that from that which has existence by which He gives life, knowing, hearing, seeing, powerful, living, dead, subject to aspects of that, outside of possibility of that, the existence of all that is established by the All-Knowing Maker, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 750

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument for the existence of a wise Creator. It begins by recounting an example: quicklime and arsenic—when combined, they produce burning, but individually they do not. This prompts the question of whether the effect is due to a change in the substances themselves or to an external agent. The author then states the fundamental principle: in matters of the unseen (like the nature of stars and elements), one must either rely on revelation (sam') or infer from the observed to the unobserved (al-hadir 'ala al-gha'ib). If the latter method is used, the observed existent is taken as a sign: it is in a certain state, and by its existence we consider that whatever brought it into existence must possess that quality. This invalidates materialist claims about the temporal origination of the world through mixture, movement of stars, etc. Next, the author argues on the basis of stability and change: every natural thing that changes requires a changer—either wise or foolish—and the eventual outcomes reveal which. Consistently beneficial outcomes point to a wise changer. He further refutes the idea that natures alone produce effects, because for an effect to occur, the agent must have knowledge of the combination and the subject must be receptive. Therefore, all things—including the life, knowledge, power, etc. mentioned—are created by the All-Knowing Maker, establishing that there is no power except through Him.

Key Terms
النورة
الزرنيخ
السمع
الحاضر على الغائب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The example of quicklime and arsenic is about chemical interaction and can be explained by natural properties alone.
Correction: Maturidi uses the example to show that the combination produces a new effect not attributable to either substance alone, implying an external agent beyond natures.

Checkpoint
What is the main methodological principle Maturidi presents after the example of quicklime and arsenic?
A) All knowledge comes from revelation alone.
B) One must either rely on revelation or infer the unseen from the observed.
C) Natures themselves are sufficient to explain all phenomena.
D) The observed world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The example of quicklime and arsenic leads to the principle that effects require a cause beyond mere natures, and we must use sound methods to infer the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that observed effects demand a cause beyond the things themselves. Look at your own existence—your breath, your heartbeat, your thoughts. Are you willing to accept that these are mere accidents of matter, or do they force you to recognize a Causer? What keeps you from fully surrendering to that recognition?
?
The passage teaches that we must rely either on revelation or on sound inference to know the unseen. Which one do you lean on more? If you were stripped of both, would your certainty in Allah remain? Why or why not?
?
Consider a moment when you assumed something 'just happened'—a coincidence, a stroke of luck, a natural process. After this lesson, can you honestly still call it that? Or must you now see it as a sign pointing to its author? What will you change in how you view everyday events?

intermediate
6 min
Argument from Change for a Wise Creator
Argument from change requiring a wise changer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that every change in nature requires a changer, and that beneficial outcomes point to a wise changer.

Core Idea
Change demands a changer; consistent good outcomes reveal a wise one.

After establishing the methodological principle, Maturidi builds an argument based on the observation that natural things change. He argues that any change from a nature requires an external agent, and that the wisdom seen in outcomes points to a wise creator. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument about change
Read the Arabic that begins with 'وإن كان على اعتبار معان...' Focus on the statement that every possessor of a nature does not change except by a wise or foolish changer.
2
Understand the two types of changers
Maturidi says changes can be caused by a wise or a foolish agent. The outcome (consequences) reveals which one it is.
This is a teleological argument.
3
See how this refutes materialist claims
If things changed only by blind forces, outcomes would not be consistently beneficial. But we see order, so the changer must be wise.
4
Note the conclusion
The argument proves that the world is temporally originated by a wise originator (muhdith hakim).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument for the existence of a wise Creator. It begins by recounting an example: quicklime and arsenic—when combined, they produce burning, but individually they do not. This prompts the question of whether the effect is due to a change in the substances themselves or to an external agent. Therefore, all things—including the life, knowledge, power, etc. mentioned—are created by the All-Knowing Maker, establishing that there is no power except through Him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Change can occur spontaneously without an external cause.
Correction: Maturidi argues that every change requires a changer, and the quality of the change (wise or foolish) is revealed by its consequences.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the soundness of consequences indicate about the changer?
A) That the changer is powerful.
B) That the changer is wise.
C) That the changer is eternal.
D) That the change is accidental.

Key Takeaway
Every change in nature requires a changer; consistent beneficial outcomes prove that changer is wise, establishing a wise originator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one area in your life where you resist change. Does your resistance imply you distrust the Changer behind it? How does this lesson invite you to surrender to His wisdom today?
?
Look at the outcomes of your daily choices—do they reveal a wise changer (submission to Allah’s guidance) or a foolish one (following your whims)? What will you change starting tonight?
?
The source states: 'outcomes manifest the changer.' If someone examined the consequences of your actions this past week, what would they conclude about who—or what—is changing you? Are you satisfied with that verdict?

Allah's Existence

Natures Require Knowledge: The All-Knowing Maker
Argument that natures alone cannot produce effects without knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that natural properties alone cannot produce effects without knowledge of the combination and receptivity, leading to the necessity of an all-knowing maker.

Core Idea
Effects require knowledge; blind natures cannot coordinate themselves.

Maturidi deepens the argument by examining the relationship between natural agents and their effects. He shows that for a cause to produce its effect, both the agent and the recipient must be appropriately matched—and that match requires knowledge. This points to a creator who is all-knowing and all-powerful. This lesson covers that final argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the final argument
Read the Arabic starting with 'وأيضا أن المعلوم...' Focus on the claim that what has the nature of burning only burns what is susceptible to burning.
2
Understand the need for knowledge
Maturidi argues that it is not in the nature of the burner to automatically go to the receptive subject, nor in the receptive subject to attract the burner. Someone who wants to achieve burning in the witnessed world must have knowledge of existence and the combination.
3
Apply to the materialist position
Materialists claim that natures act by themselves without choice. But this cannot produce the complex order we see, because they lack knowledge.
4
See the conclusion
All things—life, knowledge, power, etc.—are from the All-Knowing Maker (al-mukwin al-'alim). This establishes the necessity of a creator with attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأجاب بالنورة والزرنيخ، أن كل واحد منهما على الانفراد لا يحرق ، يمنع عنهم وعند الاجتماع يحرق . فيقال : ما يبعد أن يكون أحدهما يحرق لكن فيه ما عن الإحراق ، وفى الآخر ما يمنع هذا المانع عن المانع فيحرق ، لا أن لم يكن فيه إحراق ، أو كلاهما كانا كذلك ، وأمر الأعراض عندك على ما ذكرنا ، ومحال حلول المانع فيه لو كان طويلا أو سوادا وكذا في الهيولى ؛ لذلك اختلفا قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل فى هذا عندنا وفيما ذكر من النجوم والطبائع أن لا يخلو من أن يرجع في ذلك إلى السمع، وفيهم سماع أهل التوحيد أثبت براهين الصدق أو يستدل بالحاضر الموجود على الغائب ، فإن كان هذا معهم طريقه فيجب ؛ إذ الموجود على حال وبالوجود اعتباره - أن يكون الذي به وجد بهذه الصفة ، فيبطل قولهم فى حدوث العالم فيبطل قولهم فى حدوث العالم بالامتزاج ويتحرك النجوم ، وتقليب القوة الهيولى ، والهيولى والقوة جميعا ، وإن كان على اعتبار معان في الموجود يدل عليه فان الأصل أن كل ذي طبع لا يتغير عما عليه إلى خلاف إلا بمغير حكيم أو سفيه ، لكن يظهر أمرهما بالعواقب ، فمثله الأصل الذي أشاروا إليه إنه لا يصير على غير تلك الحال مما يصلح عواقبه إلا بحكيم ؛ إذ هي وذلك يبطل أصلهم ويثبت أن الأصل احتمل ما احتمل يجعل غيره كذلك ، وفى ذلك حدثه بمحدث حكيم ، وبالله التوفيق وأيضا أن المعلوم فيما كان طبعه الإحراق أنه لا يحرق إلا المطبوع لاحتمال الإحتراق، وكذا التسويد وكل حال وجوهر ، ثم ليس في طبع المحتمل الرفع إلى [؟] القابل فيه بالطبع ، ولا في طبع المحرق أن إلى من يحتمل ذلك ، ومن أراد في الشاهد ذلك لا يتهيأ له دون العلم بالوجود والجمع بينهما ، فعلى ذلك أمر ذلك يصير كذلك ، فيه ، والله الموفق . هم تلك الأصول التى قالوها في موات لا تدبير لهن الغائب ، فيبطل الذى راموا إثباته ويصير هو بمعنى ما ما إذا كان مع جميع ويعملن بالطبع لا اختيار لمن لم يجز أن يكون فيما منه وجود به يحيى عالما سميعا بصيرا قادرا حيا ميتا محتملا لجهات ذلك ، خارجا من احتمال ذلك ، ثبت كون ذلك كله بالمكون العليم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله

Source pages p. 750

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument for the existence of a wise Creator. It begins by recounting an example: quicklime and arsenic—when combined, they produce burning, but individually they do not. This prompts the question of whether the effect is due to a change in the substances themselves or to an external agent. The author then states the fundamental principle: in matters of the unseen (like the nature of stars and elements), one must either rely on revelation (sam') or infer from the observed to the unobserved (al-hadir 'ala al-gha'ib). If the latter method is used, the observed existent is taken as a sign: it is in a certain state, and by its existence we consider that whatever brought it into existence must possess that quality. This invalidates materialist claims about the temporal origination of the world through mixture, movement of stars, etc. Next, the author argues on the basis of stability and change: every natural thing that changes requires a changer—either wise or foolish—and the eventual outcomes reveal which. Consistently beneficial outcomes point to a wise changer. He further refutes the idea that natures alone produce effects, because for an effect to occur, the agent must have knowledge of the combination and the subject must be receptive. Therefore, all things—including the life, knowledge, power, etc. mentioned—are created by the All-Knowing Maker, establishing that there is no power except through Him.

Key Terms
الطبع
المكون العليم
الإحراق
المحتمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Natures alone, without any external intelligence, can produce the ordered effects we see.
Correction: Maturidi argues that natures lack knowledge and will; therefore, they cannot bring about coordinated effects without an external knowing agent.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say is necessary for an effect like burning to occur in the witnessed world?
A) The nature of fire alone.
B) The receptivity of the object alone.
C) Knowledge of existence and combination between agent and recipient.
D) Chance.

Key Takeaway
Natural properties alone are insufficient to produce order; the need for knowledge and combination points to an All-Knowing Maker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the intricate coordination in your life—your heartbeat, the seasons, the paths of people crossing—do you ever attribute it to mere chance or your own planning? How can you train yourself to see the All-Knowing's hand in every detail, and will you thank Him for a specific instance today?
?
Think of a goal you desperately wanted to achieve but couldn't make happen despite your best efforts. Did you realize that even bringing together the right conditions requires knowledge beyond yours? Will you now surrender that goal to the One who knows how to combine all things perfectly, and trust His timing rather than your own frustration?
?
The argument shows that without knowledge, even fire and wood cannot come together. In your relationships, do you try to force harmony through your own efforts, or do you turn to the All-Knowing who alone can unite hearts? What is one relationship you will commit to entrusting to Him this week, asking Him to 'bring together' what you cannot?

The Impossibility of Two Eternal Principles Coexisting
Maturidi presents a dilemma on mixture origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that two eternal principles cannot coexist or mix without contradiction.

Core Idea
Two eternal principles cannot mix without one originating from the other.

Maturidi begins his refutation by forcing the dualist into a dilemma. If light and darkness are both eternal, how can they mix? The answer leads to an absurdity that undermines the claim of dualism. This passage sets up the key logical trap.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Notice the opening question: Did mixture occur after it was not? The answer forces either pre-eternal mixing or later origination.
The dualist cannot consistently say 'by the first two' without absurdity.
2
Identify the key alternative
The dualist must say whether the mixture was from light or darkness. If both exist together, they cannot be separate principles.
Maturidi cuts off the option of coexistence without mixing.
3
Understand the conclusion
The impossibility of coexistence leads to the clear conclusion that the dualist position is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أليس بعد أن لم يكن ؟ أو غيرهما ؟ فإن قال : بالأولين ، أحال ؛ لأنه أثبت الامتزاج والتباين لنفسه لا بد من : بلى . قيل : آكان هو النور أو الظلمة . ولو جاز ذلك الجاز وجودهما معا ، وهو بين ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم إثباتهم الحد من حيث الالتقاء ، إما إن كانا متماسين في الأزل أو [غير] متماسين ، فإن كانا متباينين قال : إن تماما حدثا ، فحدث الجزء يوجب الكل بحق الاستدلال بالشاهد على الغائب ، وإن كانا متماسين فلا بد من أن أحدهمها حتى يمتزج بالآخر أو يجيد من الآخر حتى يدخل في نفسه ، وأيهما كان / ففيه زيادة لم يكن أو قطع وإدخال في جوهر ، فيبطل القول بأنه غير متناه ؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن لأجزائه تناه لم يكن للآخر فيه تداخل ليمتزج به ، ثبت أنه متناه إذا احتمل الامتزاج ، مع البعد أن تبقى الظلمة كثافتها على النور مع رقته فيقتطع منها ؛ إذ كل ممتلى بما يلطف من الأشياء لا يتمكن فيه ما يكثف ولو كان ذلك من النور فقد اكتسب الشر وألقى نفسه في الحبس مع ثبات الكيف جوهرا واحدا ، وإنما بحد اللطف المنفذ فى الكثيف إذا كان من جواهر مختلفة يبقى بينها الفرج " ، وأما الذى سبيله ما ذكر فلا، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإن سبقت بما حدث من الامتزاج بعد أن لم يكن فإما أن كان بأحدهما أو بهما ، وفيه احتمال الحدوث ، فمثله الكل، أو ليس بها ، ففى ذلك تثبيت ثالث ، أو لأنفسهما كان ، فلزم نفى التباين ، أو تبقى الظلمة بنفسها فلم يكن ذلك الوقت بأولى مما قبله ، وإذا لم يحدث في الجزئين اللذين لم يمتزجا شيء ، وقد وجد ، لم لا كان كذلك فى الكل ؟
Is it after it was not? Or other than them? If he says: by the first two, he makes impossible; because he affirmed mixing and separation for itself, it must be: yes. It was said: Was it light or darkness? If that were permissible, their existence together would be permissible, and it is clear, and there is no power except with Allah. Then their affirmation of limit from the aspect of meeting: either they were touching in pre-eternity or not touching. If they were separate, he said: the two parts came into existence, so the occurrence of the part necessitates the whole by the right of inference from the witnessed to the absent. And if they were touching, then it is inevitable that one of them penetrates the other or separates from the other until it enters into itself. Whichever it is, in it is an increase that was not, or a cutting and insertion into a substance. So the statement that it is infinite is invalidated; because if its parts have no end, there would be no interpenetration of the other into it to mix with it. It is established that it is finite when it admits mixing. With the remoteness that darkness retains its density upon light despite its subtlety so that it cuts from it; since everything filled with subtle things cannot contain what is dense, and if that were from light, then it has acquired evil and thrown itself into imprisonment with the stability of quality as one substance. And it is only by the limit of the subtle penetrating into the dense if they are different substances, voids remain between them. As for that which is such as mentioned, no. And there is no power except with Allah. And if the mixture occurred after it was not, then either it was from one of them or from both, and in it is the possibility of origination, so the whole is like it. Or not from them, then in that is the affirmation of a third. Or from themselves, then the negation of separation is necessary. Or darkness remains by itself, then that time was not more appropriate than before it. And if nothing occurred in the two parts that did not mix, and it existed, why would it not be so in the whole?
Source pages p. 759

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the dualist claim that light and darkness are two eternal principles that mix. Maturidi first poses a dilemma: if the questioner says that mixture occurred after not existing, or something else, he is forced into contradictions. He then examines the possibility of the two being in contact or separate in pre-eternity. If separate, their coming into existence as parts would imply the whole is also originated, which is invalid for eternal principles. If in contact, one must penetrate the other, which requires finitude—if the parts are infinite, no interpenetration can occur. Thus, if mixture is possible, they must be finite, contradicting the claim of eternity. Maturidi then considers the scenario of mixture occurring after non-existence, tracing whether it comes from one, both, or a third, each leading to absurdities. He concludes that if no change occurred in the parts that did not mix, the whole should also be unchanged, undermining the dualist thesis.

Key Terms
امتزاج (mixing)
تباين (separation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two eternal principles can mix without one being derived from the other.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if both exist together, they would coexist as a mixture, contradicting their separate eternal natures.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say would be permissible if mixture could be from both light and darkness?
A) Their existence together
B) Their eternal separation
C) Their non-existence
D) Their finitude

Key Takeaway
Two eternal principles cannot coexist without contradiction; mixture implies origination or absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed any power or existence to something alongside Allah, even in a subtle way? What 'eternal principles' have you unconsciously elevated to compete with Him in your heart? Today, will you consciously reject that and affirm with certainty that nothing shares in His lordship?
?
The dualist believes light and darkness are both eternal and separate. What 'lights' (success, health, wealth) and 'darknesses' (failure, illness, poverty) have you mentally treated as independent forces outside Allah's control? How does the logical impossibility in this lesson expose the falsehood of that mindset?
?
Consider the logical contradiction of two eternal principles mixing: is there any area of your life where you are trying to serve two masters, trying to mix devotion to Allah with loyalty to something else? What concrete step will you take today to remove that mixture and purify your tawhid?

The Finitude Argument from Contact and Separation
Maturidi argues from contact/separation to finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the concepts of touch and separation to prove that eternal principles cannot be infinite.

Core Idea
If two eternal principles touch, one must penetrate the other, requiring finitude.

Maturidi now examines the possibility that light and darkness are in contact or separate in pre-eternity. Both scenarios lead to the conclusion that they must be finite, contradicting their claim to be eternal and infinite. This is a key move in showing the incoherence of dualism.

Guided Path
1
Consider the two possibilities
The dualist must say whether light and darkness are in contact (touching) or separate in pre-eternity. Each leads to a contradiction.
Maturidi systematically eliminates both options.
2
Analyze the 'separate' case
If they are separate, their parts came into existence, implying the whole is originated—not eternal.
This uses the principle that the part's origination points to the whole's origination.
3
Analyze the 'touching' case
If they touch, one must penetrate the other. Penetration requires a limit, so the parts cannot be infinite. Mixture implies finitude.
Infinite parts cannot interpenetrate, so mixture is impossible if infinite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Origination of Mixture and Its Impossibility
Maturidi examines originated mixture scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's analysis of the scenario where mixture originates after non-existence, leading to further contradictions.

Core Idea
If mixture occurs after non-existence, it must come from one principle, both, or a third—all impossible.

Maturidi now considers the possibility that the dualist concedes mixture is originated (not eternal). He then traces the origin of this mixture, showing that each possible source leads to an absurdity. This final argument seals the refutation of dualism by demonstrating that no coherent account of mixture is possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four possibilities
If mixture occurred after non-existence, it could come from one principle, from both, from neither (a third), or from themselves. Each is examined.
Maturidi systematically lists and refutes each.
2
Refute each possibility
From one or both implies the mixture is originated, so the whole is originated; from a third affirms a new principle; from themselves negates separation; darkness remaining itself makes time irrelevant.
Each leads to a contradiction with dualist claims.
3
Conclude with analogy
If no change occurred in the parts that did not mix, the whole should also be unchanged, showing mixture is impossible.
This final analogy closes the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Maturidi argues that every possible origin for mixture fails. Consider: are there areas in your life where you are trying to 'mix' your worship of Allah with something else—like status, comfort, or relationships—as if they could coexist eternally? How does this argument reveal the impossibility of such a partnership? What step will you take today to purify your intention?
?
The passage shows that any attempt to make a second eternal principle leads to contradictions. In your heart, do you ever act as if something besides Allah has permanence—like a grudge, a desire, or a fear? How can the logical conclusion that only Allah is eternal free you from idolizing created things?
?
Dualists believed in two origins. Maturidi dismantles that. Think of a habit or thought pattern that feels 'eternal' in your life—something you think you can't change. Does this passage help you see that everything besides Allah is originated and therefore can be changed with His help? What is one thing you will submit to His power today?

Self-Contradiction in Dualism
Maturidi shows how the dualists' own account makes light ignorant and darkness powerful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi exposes the internal contradiction in the dualist position by analyzing their own narrative.

Core Idea
Dualism collapses when its own story makes light ignorant and darkness powerful.

The dualists wanted to separate good and evil into two independent origins. But as Maturidi shows, their own account of light and darkness forces them to attribute both good and evil to one source. This passage reveals the self-refuting nature of their claim, using logic grounded in divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the theological principle
Start with Maturidi's opening principle: God punishes through the very pretexts people use to deny Him. This frames the refutation.
This sets the stage for why dualism is a false pretext.
2
Identify the dualist claim
The dualists say good cannot come from evil, so they posit two separate origins: light (good) and darkness (evil).
3
Trace the contradiction
Maturidi then shows how their narrative makes light ignorant of consequences, unable to repel harm, and even imprisoned by darkness.
Light loses the very attributes of good—knowledge and power.
4
See the final reversal
The dualists end up attributing both good and evil to darkness, thereby making their separation pointless and their position self-refuting.
This is the core of the internal contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل أن الله عز وجل يجعل هلاك عبده بالذي به يدعى جحوده ، ويعدل عن طاعته خوفا عن أمر يلزمه بأن يهلكه بلزومه فيما طمع الخلوص عنه . فهؤلاء أن الذي يكون منه الخير لا يحتمل كون الشر منه صاروا إلى القول باثنين ، ويجعل أصل كل غير الذي هو أصل الآخر ، ثم صيروا الذي أصل الخير عندهم هو النهاية في الشر ، والذي هو أصل الشر عندهم في الخير ; لأن هؤلاء صيروا النور جاهلا بعواقب ما إليه يصير ، حتى كان على أحد القولين أراد دفع أذاه فبقى فيه ، لا يعلم أنه لا يقدر عليه ، ولا أنه يبقى في غاية ما رام دفعه ، ولا قدر على التخلص ، إذ بلي به ، والأول صار إليه ليلين خشونته ويدفع أذاه جهلا منه أنه لا يقدر عليه ، وعجزا أن يتخلص عنه . وكذلك على قول الماني إن الظلمة هي التي بغت على النور وألقته في حبسها وأوثقته بوثاقها حتى جهل مأتاه وعجز عن النجاة ، وبدوء كل خير ، ونهاية العلم ، والإحاطة بكل خير ، والبلوغ إليه إنما هو بالقدرة عليه ، فأزالوا الأمرين جميعا عن النور ، وحققوا للظلمة ، فصاروا إلى نقض جميع ما بنوا : إن الخير لكل ذلك ، فصيروا النور خارجا عن أعظم الخير ، والآخر عن أعظم الشر ، ثم حققوا الأمرين لواحد ، فيبطل قولهم من حيث راموا اثباته.
And the principle is that God, mighty and majestic, makes the destruction of His servant happen by that through which he pretends to deny Him, and he turns away from His obedience for fear of something that binds him, so that He destroys him by his adherence to what he hoped to escape from. So these people, because that from which good comes cannot have evil come from it, they resorted to saying two (principles), and they made the origin of each other than the origin of the other. Then they made that which they considered the origin of good to be the ultimate in evil, and that which they considered the origin of evil to be (the ultimate) in good. For these people made light ignorant of the consequences of what it would become, such that according to one of the two sayings, it intended to repel its harm but remained in it, not knowing that it cannot overcome it, nor that it remains in the utmost of what it aimed to repel, nor could it free itself, since it was afflicted with it. And the first (origin) turned to it to soften its harshness and repel its harm, out of ignorance that it cannot overcome it, and inability to escape from it. Similarly, according to the saying of Mani, darkness it was that attacked light and cast it into its prison and bound it with its bonds until it became ignorant of its way and unable to escape. And the beginning of every good, the ultimate of knowledge, encompassing every good, and attaining it, is only through power over it. So they removed both matters from light and attributed them to darkness, and thus they came to negate everything they had built: that good is for all that, and they made light outside the greatest good, and the other (outside the greatest evil). Then they attributed both matters to one, so their saying is invalid from the aspect they sought to establish it.
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of dualism by exposing inner contradiction. Maturidi begins with a theological principle: God punishes a servant by means of his own false pretexts. The dualists, assuming good cannot originate evil, posited two principles: one for good (light) and one for evil (darkness). However, their own narrative turns light into something ignorant and powerless—it cannot escape darkness, does not know the outcome, and fails to repel harm. Similarly, in Mani's account, darkness overpowers light and imprisons it. Thus light loses all attributes of goodness and power, while darkness gains them. The dualists end up attributing both good and evil to one source (darkness or the mixture), contradicting their initial claim. Therefore their position is self-refuting.

شر

ظلمة

ماني

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dualists consistently separate good and evil into two independent principles.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their own narrative makes light weak and ignorant, so it cannot be the source of good; they end up attributing both to one principle.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's refutation, what do the dualists end up doing to the two principles they posited?
A) They keep them strictly separate
B) They attribute both good and evil to one principle
C) They deny the existence of evil
D) They make light all-powerful

Key Takeaway
The dualist claim that good and evil have separate origins collapses when their own narrative reveals light to be ignorant and powerless, ultimately attributing both good and evil to one source.

?

?
The dualists attributed both good and evil to one source ultimately. Do you ever find yourself attributing blessings to your own efforts and hardships to external circumstances, forgetting that all comes from Allah? How can you train yourself to see His hand in everything?

The Regress Argument Against Dualism
Maturidi enumerates steps forcing dualism into absurd multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi demonstrates that dualism logically leads to an infinite regress of principles.

Core Idea
Dualism cannot stop at two; consistency forces ever more principles.

This passage begins Maturidi's refutation of the dualist claim that the world originates from two eternal principles. He shows that if duality is granted, reason demands additional principles, each step leading to absurdity. The argument exposes the instability of any finite polytheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical progression from two to four, then to six, then to seven or five.
This is a condensed logical argument; read slowly.
2
Identify the numerical chain
List the numbers mentioned: 2, 4, 6, 7 (or 5). Understand why each step is taken: for example, if two aspects, then four opposing; if four like natures, then six directions.
The argument assumes that each step is required to be consistent.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Ask yourself: what does this regress show about dualism? It shows that dualism cannot be self-consistent; it either leads to an infinite number of principles or arbitrary endpoints.
Maturidi uses this to clear the ground for tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع ما لو كان لذينك الوجهين يجب القول بالاثنين ليجب القول بالأربع متضادة ، كل يضر الكل ، ولو كان بهذا يقول بالأربع : نحو الطبائع ; إذ هي ليجب القول بالست ; بما لا يخلو شيء قائم عن جهات ست ، وذلك يوجب القول بالسابع ; لما كان حامل تلك الجهات لا يوصف بجهة سابتها ، أو بالخمس بما كان الذي فيه اجتماع تلك الطبائع هو الخامس ، لا يوصف بحر ولا يرد. ولو كان كما تقول الثنوية ليجب القول بالثالث ; لما كانا ولم يكن العالم ، ولا شر ، ومحال كون متبائن بنفسه ، ممتزجا بنفسه لا يوجب الاجتماع والتناقض ثبت كون ذلك بغيرهما ، وبه كان كل خير وشر ، فيبطل قولهم من حيث راموا اثباته. ثم القول بالواحد لا يضطر صاحبه إلى القول بآخر بوجه . وأصل ذلك أن هؤلاء قوم لم تبلغ تقولهم المبلغ الذي يدرك به حكمة الربوبية في الأشياء ، وظنوا أن يكون الرب على صفتهم من الحاجات والشهوات واحتمال الآفات وشوائب العاهات ، فقدروا أفعاله بالذي علموا الحكمة بأفعال أنفسهم ، ولو تأملوا ما فيه من الضرورات السواتر المانعة عن الإحاطة بالأشياء ، ثم بمصالح أنفسهم التي في ذلك جل كدهم ، وجهدوا لعلموا أن الجهل هو الذي سدهم عن إدراك الحكمة في ذك ، وأحق الناس بهذا هم ; إذ زعموا أن العالم إنما هو امتزاج النور والظلمة ، فما من جزء من أجزاء النور إلا هو مشوب بجزء من أجزاء الظلمة ، والظلمة هي الساترة ثم هي القاهرة للنور ، فما من خير يرجى بدوه منه إلا والظلمة تقهره وتستره عن التجلي لأهل المذهب ، فأنى لهم والعلم والوقوف على طريق الحكمة ، حتى يدعون في الآخر دعوى بشر.
Moreover, if for those two aspects duality must be affirmed, then it would necessitate affirming four mutually opposing (principles), each harming the whole. And if one says four, like the natures, then it necessitates affirming six, because no existent thing is free from six directions; and that necessitates affirming a seventh, because the bearer of those directions cannot be described by a seventh direction; or five, because that in which these natures gather is the fifth, not described by movement or rest. And if it were as the dualists claim, then it would necessitate affirming a third, because they (the two) and the world did not exist, nor evil; and it is impossible for two things that are separate by themselves to mix by themselves without necessitating combination and contradiction; so it is established that their coming to be is from something other than them, and through that every good and evil came to be; thus their saying is invalid from the aspect they sought to establish it. Then, belief in the One does not compel its adherent to affirm another in any respect. The origin of this is that these are people whose intellects have not reached the level by which the wisdom of lordship in things is perceived; they thought that the Lord should be like them, possessing needs, desires, susceptibility to afflictions and blemishes; so they measured His actions by what they knew of wisdom from their own actions. Had they reflected on the inherent necessities that prevent encompassing things, and then on the interests of their own selves which constitute the bulk of their effort and toil, they would have known that ignorance is what blocked them from perceiving wisdom in that. And the most entitled to this (ignorance) are they, for they claim that the world is merely a mixture of light and darkness; there is no part of light except it is mixed with a part of darkness, and darkness is the covering and then the vanquisher of light; so no good can be hoped to appear from it without darkness vanquishing it and concealing it from manifestation to the people of the sect. So how can they have knowledge and insight into the way of wisdom, when at the end they claim the claim of a human being?
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage is a logical and philosophical refutation of dualism and a positive argument for tawhid (divine unity). Maturidi first argues ad absurdum: if duality is accepted, consistency demands more principles—four, six, seven, or five—as in the natures (elemental qualities) or directions, leading to an infinite regress. Moreover, if the two principles were originally separate, their mixture requires a third cause. Thus dualism collapses. He then presents the alternative: belief in the One (al-wāḥid) does not force one to posit another principle. The root error of the dualists is that they judge God by human limitations (needs, desires, susceptibility to harm). They fail to grasp divine wisdom because their own doctrine holds that all light is mixed with darkness, making true knowledge impossible. Hence their claim to know ultimate reality is self-defeating.

Key Terms
اثنين
أربع
طبائع
جهات
سابع
خمس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism (belief in two eternal principles) is a simple and coherent worldview.
Correction: Maturidi shows that dualism cannot stop at two; it logically requires an infinite regress of additional principles, making it incoherent.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, if one affirms two principles, what does consistency require next?
A) Four mutually opposing principles
B) Six directions
C) Seven principles
D) Five principles

Key Takeaway
Dualism cannot be logically contained; it leads to absurd multiplicity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes act as if there are multiple independent forces controlling your life—luck, people's opinions, your own strength—while mentally affirming Allah's oneness? Maturidi's argument shows that dualism logically collapses into absurdity. Will you examine your heart today and repent from any hidden shirk in your reliance?
?
When you face a conflict between your desires and Allah's command, do you treat those desires as a separate, self-existing power? This lesson proves that two opposing principles cannot coexist coherently. Will you consciously submit your will to Allah alone, acknowledging that He is the sole Sovereign over your choices?
?
You may never have considered the logical flaws in dualism, but do you live as though your life is split between sacred and secular, as if Allah rules only in the mosque? The regress argument shows that dividing reality into independent domains leads to absurdity. Will you integrate your faith into every aspect of your life starting today, recognizing that Allah's oneness demands total allegiance?

Dualism Self-Destructs and Points to the One
Maturidi argues that dualism necessitates a third principle and then affirms tawhid.

Learning Objective
Understand why dualism cannot explain the world's existence without a third principle, and why belief in one God avoids this problem.

Core Idea
The dualists' own reasoning forces them to admit a third cause, undermining their position.

Maturidi now tightens the logical noose. If the two principles were originally separate, how could they mix without a third agent? And if they always coexisted, why is there evil? The argument culminates in affirming the necessity of a single Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the logical steps: the two principles are separate, so they cannot mix by themselves; a third is needed to cause their union and the world's existence.
The phrase 'it is impossible for two separate things to mix by themselves' is key.
2
Consider the implications for good and evil
If the two principles are good and evil, their mixture would require an external cause for both. This shows dualism cannot account for moral dualism.
3
Contrast with tawhid
Belief in one God does not force one to posit another principle. This is the positive conclusion of the argument.

Why Dualists Fail to Grasp Divine Wisdom
Maturidi critiques the dualists' anthropomorphism and epistemological self-defeat.

Learning Objective
Recognize that the dualists' mistake stems from projecting human limitations onto God and from their own epistemologically self-defeating worldview.

Core Idea
Dualists measure God by themselves, and their own doctrine makes knowledge impossible.

Having dismantled the logical structure of dualism, Maturidi now diagnoses its psychological and philosophical roots. The dualists conceive of God as having human needs and flaws, and their own belief that light is always mixed with darkness makes it impossible for them to attain true wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Notice the two main criticisms: (1) dualists anthropomorphize God, (2) their own cosmology prevents true knowledge.
The phrase 'they thought that the Lord should be like them' is central.
2
Understand the anthropomorphic error
Dualists assume God has needs, desires, and susceptibility to harm, just like humans. This leads them to measure divine actions by human standards.
Maturidi implies that true wisdom requires recognizing God's transcendence.
3
Grasp the self-refutation
If light (source of good) is always mixed with darkness, then no perfect knowledge can be attained. Hence, dualists cannot claim to know ultimate reality.
The argument is that their own principles make knowledge of wisdom impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع ما لو كان لذينك الوجهين يجب القول بالاثنين ليجب القول بالأربع متضادة ، كل يضر الكل ، ولو كان بهذا يقول بالأربع : نحو الطبائع ; إذ هي ليجب القول بالست ; بما لا يخلو شيء قائم عن جهات ست ، وذلك يوجب القول بالسابع ; لما كان حامل تلك الجهات لا يوصف بجهة سابتها ، أو بالخمس بما كان الذي فيه اجتماع تلك الطبائع هو الخامس ، لا يوصف بحر ولا يرد. ولو كان كما تقول الثنوية ليجب القول بالثالث ; لما كانا ولم يكن العالم ، ولا شر ، ومحال كون متبائن بنفسه ، ممتزجا بنفسه لا يوجب الاجتماع والتناقض ثبت كون ذلك بغيرهما ، وبه كان كل خير وشر ، فيبطل قولهم من حيث راموا اثباته. ثم القول بالواحد لا يضطر صاحبه إلى القول بآخر بوجه . وأصل ذلك أن هؤلاء قوم لم تبلغ تقولهم المبلغ الذي يدرك به حكمة الربوبية في الأشياء ، وظنوا أن يكون الرب على صفتهم من الحاجات والشهوات واحتمال الآفات وشوائب العاهات ، فقدروا أفعاله بالذي علموا الحكمة بأفعال أنفسهم ، ولو تأملوا ما فيه من الضرورات السواتر المانعة عن الإحاطة بالأشياء ، ثم بمصالح أنفسهم التي في ذلك جل كدهم ، وجهدوا لعلموا أن الجهل هو الذي سدهم عن إدراك الحكمة في ذك ، وأحق الناس بهذا هم ; إذ زعموا أن العالم إنما هو امتزاج النور والظلمة ، فما من جزء من أجزاء النور إلا هو مشوب بجزء من أجزاء الظلمة ، والظلمة هي الساترة ثم هي القاهرة للنور ، فما من خير يرجى بدوه منه إلا والظلمة تقهره وتستره عن التجلي لأهل المذهب ، فأنى لهم والعلم والوقوف على طريق الحكمة ، حتى يدعون في الآخر دعوى بشر.
Moreover, if for those two aspects duality must be affirmed, then it would necessitate affirming four mutually opposing (principles), each harming the whole. And if one says four, like the natures, then it necessitates affirming six, because no existent thing is free from six directions; and that necessitates affirming a seventh, because the bearer of those directions cannot be described by a seventh direction; or five, because that in which these natures gather is the fifth, not described by movement or rest. And if it were as the dualists claim, then it would necessitate affirming a third, because they (the two) and the world did not exist, nor evil; and it is impossible for two things that are separate by themselves to mix by themselves without necessitating combination and contradiction; so it is established that their coming to be is from something other than them, and through that every good and evil came to be; thus their saying is invalid from the aspect they sought to establish it. Then, belief in the One does not compel its adherent to affirm another in any respect. The origin of this is that these are people whose intellects have not reached the level by which the wisdom of lordship in things is perceived; they thought that the Lord should be like them, possessing needs, desires, susceptibility to afflictions and blemishes; so they measured His actions by what they knew of wisdom from their own actions. Had they reflected on the inherent necessities that prevent encompassing things, and then on the interests of their own selves which constitute the bulk of their effort and toil, they would have known that ignorance is what blocked them from perceiving wisdom in that. And the most entitled to this (ignorance) are they, for they claim that the world is merely a mixture of light and darkness; there is no part of light except it is mixed with a part of darkness, and darkness is the covering and then the vanquisher of light; so no good can be hoped to appear from it without darkness vanquishing it and concealing it from manifestation to the people of the sect. So how can they have knowledge and insight into the way of wisdom, when at the end they claim the claim of a human being?
Source pages p. 763

Commentary
This passage is a logical and philosophical refutation of dualism and a positive argument for tawhid (divine unity). Maturidi first argues ad absurdum: if duality is accepted, consistency demands more principles—four, six, seven, or five—as in the natures (elemental qualities) or directions, leading to an infinite regress. Moreover, if the two principles were originally separate, their mixture requires a third cause. Thus dualism collapses. He then presents the alternative: belief in the One (al-wāḥid) does not force one to posit another principle. The root error of the dualists is that they judge God by human limitations (needs, desires, susceptibility to harm). They fail to grasp divine wisdom because their own doctrine holds that all light is mixed with darkness, making true knowledge impossible. Hence their claim to know ultimate reality is self-defeating.

Key Terms
حكمة
ربوبية
حاجات
ظلمة
نور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualists are rational and objective in their theology.
Correction: Maturidi shows they project human limitations onto God and their own worldview makes knowledge impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what prevents the dualists from attaining wisdom?
A) Lack of effort
B) Their own doctrine that light is mixed with darkness
C) Their belief in one God
D) Their use of logic

Key Takeaway
True knowledge of God requires recognizing His transcendence and avoiding self-projection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you found yourself measuring God's actions by your own standards of fairness or wisdom? What does that reveal about the condition of your heart, and how will you repent now?
?
Your intellect, like that of the dualists, has limits that prevent you from encompassing all divine wisdom. In what area of your life are you most prone to claim you 'know better' than God's decree? Write down one specific matter and commit to surrendering it to Him today.
?
The dualists' doctrine made knowledge impossible. Is there any belief or habit in your life that logically contradicts your claim to follow Islam? Be honest: if your actions were analyzed, would they lead to a self-defeating conclusion about your faith?

God's Wisdom in Creation: Created for Consequences
Maturidi argues that creation's purpose is the benefit of creatures, not God, and that this necessitates both good and evil as means of discernment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's theological argument that God creates not for His own benefit but for the benefit of creatures, and that the existence of both good and evil serves a wise purpose in human testing and discernment.

Core Idea
God creates for our benefit, not His own.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi establishes a foundational principle of Islamic theology: God's acts are wise and purposeful, but that purpose is never for His own benefit—He is utterly self-sufficient. Instead, creation exists for the sake of its creatures, to allow them to seek beneficial consequences and to distinguish good from evil through experience. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Maturidi uses a chain of logical deductions.
2
Identify the opening principle
The passage begins with a general principle about blameworthy actions. Understand what makes an agent blameworthy according to this principle.
This principle is then applied to God.
3
Trace the argument for consequences
Follow the logic: God does not benefit from creation → creation must be for consequences → consequences are for creatures. Then see how this leads to the necessity of both good and evil.
The argument moves from divine self-sufficiency to the purpose of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ثم الأصل أن من يفعل فعلا لا ينتفع هو به لهلاكه وفنائه أنه عائب ، والله سبحانه لم يكن لينتفع بما ينشئه لتعاليه عن الحاجات وغناه بنفسه عن غيره ، فيبطل أن يكون فعله لينتفع به هو ، ثم لو كان للهلاك لا غير لكان لا معنى لخلقه ، فثبت أن خلق العالم للعواقب ، ثم خلق خلائق لم يجعل عندها تمييزا ولا إدراكا لعواقب الأمر ، ثبت / أنه خلقهم لا لأنفسهم ، وخلق خلقا يعرفون ذلك ويطلبون جميع صنيعهم نفع العواقب حتى من خرج ذلك ؛ إذ هو محتاج كل غير ، حكيم في فعله ، فلزمت محبتهم المنشئ فيهم من العقول التي يدركون بها العواقب ، ولأنهم لو تركوا وتدبيرهم لم يكونوا يرضون من أنفسهم التقلب فيما لا يؤثر نفعا ولا يعقبه حمدا ، ومن تعاطى منهم مثله فهو سفيه جاهل . وإذا لزم ما ذكرنا لزم فى الحكمة خلق الضار والنافع ، وخلق الجوهر المحتمل للألم واللذة وإنشاء الآلام والملاذ ؛ ليعلموا ما يرغب إليه الأنفس وما تهرب منه ، فيحذرون ويرغبون بمثله فيها امتحنوا به ؛ وليعلموا النفع من الضرر الذي لولا ذلك لم يكن لخلقهم معنى ، فخلقهم الله على ما خلق من الاختلاف لهذين [السببين] .
The shaykh said, may Allah have mercy on him: Then the principle is that whoever does an act from which he does not benefit due to his own destruction and annihilation, that he is blameworthy. And Allah, exalted, is not such that He would benefit from what He originates due to His transcendence above needs and His self-sufficiency from others. Thus it is invalid that His act is for Him to benefit thereby. Then if it were only for destruction, there would be no meaning to His creation. So it is established that the creation of the world is for consequences. Then He created creatures without giving them discernment or perception of the consequences of affairs; it is established that He created them not for themselves. And He created a creation who know that and seek in all their actions the benefit of consequences, even from what deviates from that; since He is in need of nothing other, wise in His action. So their love became necessary for the one who originated in them the intellects by which they perceive consequences. And because if they were left to their own management, they would not be pleased with themselves turning to that which does not bring benefit nor is followed by praise. And whoever among them engages in such is foolish and ignorant. And when what we mentioned is necessary, then in wisdom it is necessary to create the harmful and the beneficial, and to create the essence that is capable of pain and pleasure and to originate pains and pleasures; so that they may know what souls desire and what they flee from, so they may be cautious and desirous by means of what they are tested with. And that they may know the benefit from the harm, because without that there would be no meaning to their creation. So Allah created them according to what He created of difference for these two reasons.
Source pages p. 765

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God's creation is motivated by wisdom and benefit for creatures, not for Himself. Maturidi begins with a principle: if an agent does an act from which he himself does not benefit because he perishes or is annihilated, he is blameworthy. Since God is transcendent and self-sufficient, He cannot benefit from His acts; therefore, His acts are not for His own benefit. If creation were solely for destruction (i.e., without eventual benefit to creatures), it would be meaningless. So creation must be for consequences ('awāqib), meaning outcomes that benefit creatures. He then notes two categories of creatures: those without intellect (like animals) that do not perceive consequences—they are created for a purpose beyond themselves (i.e., to serve others). And those with intellect who seek beneficial outcomes. God placed in them intellects to perceive consequences, and they love the originator of those intellects. If left to themselves, they would not be content with purposeless actions. Anyone who engages in such is foolish. Since this is established, wisdom requires creating both harm and benefit, pleasure and pain, so that humans can distinguish what to seek and what to avoid through testing. Without this, creation would have no meaning. So God created diversity in the world for these two reasons: to test and to teach discernment.

Key Terms
عاقبة ('āqiba - consequence)
نفع (naf‘ - benefit)
ضرر (ḍarar - harm)
حكمة (ḥikma - wisdom)
جوهر (jawhar - essence/substance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God creates because He needs creation or benefits from it.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly refutes this: God is self-sufficient and does not benefit from His acts. Creation is for the benefit of creatures, not for God.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say that creation must be 'for consequences' (للعواقب)?
A) Because God benefits from creation.
B) Because God is self-sufficient and does not benefit, so creation must be for the benefit of creatures.
C) Because creation is for destruction.
D) Because God needed creation to be known.

Key Takeaway
God's creation is a wise system designed for the benefit of intelligent creatures, allowing them to discern and choose what leads to good consequences through the experience of both benefit and harm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God created all things for your benefit and not His own, why do you often live as if your actions have no eternal consequences? How would your daily decisions change if you truly believed every moment is a test for your ultimate good?
?
When you face pain or difficulty, do you accept it as part of God's wise plan to teach you discernment, or do you resent it? What would it look like to embrace hardship as a tool for learning what your soul should flee from?
?
The passage says that whoever acts without regard to beneficial consequences is foolish and ignorant. Where in your life are you acting without thinking about the end? What is one habit you need to change today to align with seeking the 'benefit of consequences' in every action?

Harmony of Creation Proves One Creator
Maturidi proves one Creator through the harmony of benefit and harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the interconnection of benefit and harm in creation demonstrates that the universe is managed by a single wise Creator.

Core Idea
The harmony of benefit and harm in creation points to one Manager.

Imam Maturidi presents a powerful argument from the harmony of creation. He points out that every essence is created capable of both benefit and harm, and these are interconnected in a way that reveals a single wise Manager. In this passage, he begins by describing this interconnection and then argues that if there were two conflicting principles, creation would be in chaos.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
Read the passage and find where Maturidi states that the interconnection of benefit and harm shows one Manager.
2
Understand the refutation of dualism
Notice how Maturidi argues that if there were two conflicting sources (good and evil), their effects would conflict, but we see harmony.
The argument assumes that a good essence only produces good, and an evil essence only produces evil.
3
Consider the consequence of not saying one
Maturidi warns that if we do not attribute all to one, knowledge itself would be corrupted because we would lack a foundation.
4
See the practical proof
The passage concludes that in the world, each thing has benefit when restrained by a single Manager, proving oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بلطفه خلق كل جوهر محتملا للنفع والضرر ، يحل به لغيره ، وأوصل منفعة كل جوهر بغيره من الجواهر التي فيها المضار ؛ ليعلم الناظرون أن مدير ذلك كله واحد ، وأنه لو كان من مختلف لتدافع الخلق ؛ لأن جوهر الخير إذ لا يجى منه غير الخير ، ومن جوهر الشر غير الشر ، لكان صنع وإفساده ما يقوم مع مثله عالى ، فدل كل واحد منهما في بعض صنع الآخر الاتساق وتعلق منافع بعض ببعض على فساد هذا . على أنا إذا لم نقل نقل بأن الكل بادا لواحد لم يحتمل القول منا لعدد ؛ إذ لم يقدر واحد منهم على افراد الذي منه يدل عليه ، ولا أعلم عليه علم يدل عليه ، لم يجب بمثله حق / المعرفة به والعلم ما مع ا بحاله ، فيفسد العلم جميعا ؛ لجهل الأصل الذي كل أنواع العلم وفروعه به . ينفع أحد الجوهرين يضر الآخر ، وفى ذلك يلاقى الضار النافع ، فيبطل به نفع البتة ؛ لما معه المانع عنه . وفى وجود العالم وما فيه لكل منهم نفع هو الدليل الحق على أن مدير ذلك كله واحد ، لحبس كل ضار عن عمله من وجه ضرره باللطف لتقبل ما أراد من النفع ليصل إلى من أراد نفعه . وهكذا هذه القصة فيمن أراد ضرره ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أنه معلوم أن العقول ليست تركب للأكل والشرب ، ما لا عقل له في ذلك ما له العقل ، وتعظيم " محل قوم اتقوا الأكل والشرب في القلوب وهم الملائكة ، فثبت أنها خلقت للعبر والنظر ؛ لما فيه المحامد والمكارم ، وإذ كان كذلك لزم خلق مختلف الجواهر فى الحكمة : ليكون بطريق العبرة تاما ، وحق النظر وافرا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أنه معلوم في الشاهد أن من يعمل الأمرين جميعا هو أتم ، بل لا يقدر
Then with His gentleness He created every essence capable of benefit and harm, it settles in others, and He connected the benefit of each essence with other essences that contain harms; so that the observers may know that the Manager of all that is one, and that if it were from different [principles], there would be conflict in creation. Because the essence of good does not come from it except good, and from the essence of evil only evil, then its act and corruption would be what stands with its like high? So the harmony of each of them in some of the act of the other and the attachment of benefits of some to some indicates the corruption of this. Upon that, if we do not say that the whole is from one, it is not possible for us to say a number; since none of them is able to isolate that from which he indicates, nor do I know a knowledge that indicates it, then the right of knowledge of it and the knowledge of its state would not be fulfilled, so all knowledge would be corrupted due to ignorance of the principle from which all types of knowledge and its branches are. One of the two essences benefits, the other harms, and in that the harmful meets the beneficial, so benefit is nullified entirely due to the prevention that is with it. And in the existence of the world and what is in it, each of them has benefit, that is the true proof that the Manager of all that is one, because He restrains every harmful thing from its action from the aspect of its harm by gentleness to receive what He wills of benefit so that it may reach whom He wills to benefit. And likewise this story concerning whom He wills to harm. And there is no power except with Allah. And it is known that the intellects are not created for eating and drinking; what has no intellect in that matter has intellect? And the veneration of a people who refrained from eating and drinking in hearts, and they are the angels. So it is established that they were created for reflection and consideration; because of what they contain of praiseworthy qualities and virtues. And if that is the case, then it is necessary in wisdom to create diverse essences, so that the way of reflection is complete and the right of consideration is full. And there is no power except with Allah. And it is known in witnessed experience that one who does both matters is more perfect, rather he is not able...
Source pages p. 766

Commentary
This passage provides a proof from harmony (iṭtirād) for the oneness of the Creator and also discusses the purpose of intellect. Maturidi argues that God, by His gentleness (luṭf), created every essence (jawhar) capable of both benefit and harm, and connected the benefit of each essence with other essences that contain harms. This interconnection shows that the Manager of all is one; if there were two different principles (e.g., good and evil), their effects would conflict, because a good essence only produces good, and an evil essence only produces evil. But we see that the parts of the act of one harmonize with the other, and benefits are attached to harms, which indicates the falsity of dualism. If we do not say all is from one, we cannot even say a number, because no one can isolate a pure effect from its source, and knowledge would be corrupted due to ignorance of the origin. Furthermore, if one essence benefits and another harms, they would cancel each other out, but in the world each has a benefit in its context, which is a true proof that the Manager is one, as He restrains harmful things from acting fully so that benefit may reach whom He wills. The passage then turns to the purpose of intellects: they are not created for eating and drinking, but for reflection and consideration (ʿibra and naẓar). Angels, who abstain from eating and drinking, exemplify this. Therefore, it is necessary in wisdom to create diverse essences to make reflection and consideration complete. Finally, Maturidi notes a witnessed principle: one who does both matters (i.e., creates contrasts) is more perfect, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
لطف (luṭf)
جوهر (jawhar)
مدير (mudīr)
نظر (naẓar)
عبرة ('ibra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument denies that evil exists.
Correction: The argument does not deny evil; it shows that the existence of both good and evil in a harmonious system proves a single wise Creator.

Checkpoint
How does the interconnection of benefit and harm in creation refute dualism?
A) It shows that good and evil cannot coexist.
B) It shows that a single Manager restrains harms so that benefits reach their recipients, which would not be possible if there were two conflicting principles.
C) It proves that harms are illusions.
D) It shows that evil is stronger than good.

Key Takeaway
The interconnectedness of benefit and harm in creation is a clear sign that the universe is governed by one wise Manager.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that everything in your life—both the good and the bad—is managed by one wise Creator, or do you sometimes feel that different forces (luck, people, circumstances) control your fate? How does this affect your reliance on Allah? Will you consciously attribute both your successes and trials to Him alone starting today?
?
When you experience harm or difficulty, do you immediately see it as part of a coherent plan that will ultimately yield some benefit, or do you resent it as pointless? Can you identify any past harm that, in hindsight, brought about a good you value? Will you commit to looking for the hidden benefit in your current trials?
?
The proof shows that if there were multiple managers, benefit and harm would cancel each other out, leaving no net benefit. In your own life, have you ever seen Allah 'restrain harm' to allow you to receive a benefit? Make a specific memory and thank Him for that. Will you actively notice and record such instances as reminders of His oneness?

The Purpose of Intellect and the Wisdom of Diversity
Maturidi discusses the purpose of intellect and the wisdom of diversity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's view that intellect is created for reflection and consideration, not for mere physical needs, and that the diversity of essences serves a wise purpose.

Core Idea
Intellect is created for reflection, not consumption; diversity in creation enables complete consideration.

In the latter part of this passage, Imam Maturidi shifts from the proof of one Creator to the purpose of intellect. He argues that intellects are not created for eating and drinking, but for reflection (ʿibra) and consideration (naẓar). He cites angels as exemplars and explains that diverse essences are necessary for wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on intellect
Read the passage carefully and identify the main claim about the purpose of intellect.
2
Notice the example of angels
Maturidi mentions angels who refrain from eating and drinking as evidence that intellect is for higher purposes.
3
Understand the necessity of diversity
He concludes that diverse essences must be created so that reflection and consideration can be complete.
4
Reflect on the final observation
The passage ends with a note that one who does both matters is more perfect, though the text cuts off.
