ثم بلطفه خلق كل جوهر محتملا للنفع والضرر ، يحل به لغيره ، وأوصل منفعة كل جوهر بغيره من الجواهر التي فيها المضار ؛ ليعلم الناظرون أن مدير ذلك كله واحد ، وأنه لو كان من مختلف لتدافع الخلق ؛ لأن جوهر الخير إذ لا يجى منه غير الخير ، ومن جوهر الشر غير الشر ، لكان صنع وإفساده ما يقوم مع مثله عالى ، فدل كل واحد منهما في بعض صنع الآخر الاتساق وتعلق منافع بعض ببعض على فساد هذا . على أنا إذا لم نقل نقل بأن الكل بادا لواحد لم يحتمل القول منا لعدد ؛ إذ لم يقدر واحد منهم على افراد الذي منه يدل عليه ، ولا أعلم عليه علم يدل عليه ، لم يجب بمثله حق / المعرفة به والعلم ما مع ا بحاله ، فيفسد العلم جميعا ؛ لجهل الأصل الذي كل أنواع العلم وفروعه به . ينفع أحد الجوهرين يضر الآخر ، وفى ذلك يلاقى الضار النافع ، فيبطل به نفع البتة ؛ لما معه المانع عنه . وفى وجود العالم وما فيه لكل منهم نفع هو الدليل الحق على أن مدير ذلك كله واحد ، لحبس كل ضار عن عمله من وجه ضرره باللطف لتقبل ما أراد من النفع ليصل إلى من أراد نفعه . وهكذا هذه القصة فيمن أراد ضرره ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أنه معلوم أن العقول ليست تركب للأكل والشرب ، ما لا عقل له في ذلك ما له العقل ، وتعظيم " محل قوم اتقوا الأكل والشرب في القلوب وهم الملائكة ، فثبت أنها خلقت للعبر والنظر ؛ لما فيه المحامد والمكارم ، وإذ كان كذلك لزم خلق مختلف الجواهر فى الحكمة : ليكون بطريق العبرة تاما ، وحق النظر وافرا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أنه معلوم في الشاهد أن من يعمل الأمرين جميعا هو أتم ، بل لا يقدر
Then with His gentleness He created every essence capable of benefit and harm, it settles in others, and He connected the benefit of each essence with other essences that contain harms; so that the observers may know that the Manager of all that is one, and that if it were from different [principles], there would be conflict in creation. Because the essence of good does not come from it except good, and from the essence of evil only evil, then its act and corruption would be what stands with its like high? So the harmony of each of them in some of the act of the other and the attachment of benefits of some to some indicates the corruption of this. Upon that, if we do not say that the whole is from one, it is not possible for us to say a number; since none of them is able to isolate that from which he indicates, nor do I know a knowledge that indicates it, then the right of knowledge of it and the knowledge of its state would not be fulfilled, so all knowledge would be corrupted due to ignorance of the principle from which all types of knowledge and its branches are. One of the two essences benefits, the other harms, and in that the harmful meets the beneficial, so benefit is nullified entirely due to the prevention that is with it. And in the existence of the world and what is in it, each of them has benefit, that is the true proof that the Manager of all that is one, because He restrains every harmful thing from its action from the aspect of its harm by gentleness to receive what He wills of benefit so that it may reach whom He wills to benefit. And likewise this story concerning whom He wills to harm. And there is no power except with Allah. And it is known that the intellects are not created for eating and drinking; what has no intellect in that matter has intellect? And the veneration of a people who refrained from eating and drinking in hearts, and they are the angels. So it is established that they were created for reflection and consideration; because of what they contain of praiseworthy qualities and virtues. And if that is the case, then it is necessary in wisdom to create diverse essences, so that the way of reflection is complete and the right of consideration is full. And there is no power except with Allah. And it is known in witnessed experience that one who does both matters is more perfect, rather he is not able...
Source pages p. 766

Commentary
This passage provides a proof from harmony (iṭtirād) for the oneness of the Creator and also discusses the purpose of intellect. Maturidi argues that God, by His gentleness (luṭf), created every essence (jawhar) capable of both benefit and harm, and connected the benefit of each essence with other essences that contain harms. This interconnection shows that the Manager of all is one; if there were two different principles (e.g., good and evil), their effects would conflict, because a good essence only produces good, and an evil essence only produces evil. But we see that the parts of the act of one harmonize with the other, and benefits are attached to harms, which indicates the falsity of dualism. If we do not say all is from one, we cannot even say a number, because no one can isolate a pure effect from its source, and knowledge would be corrupted due to ignorance of the origin. Furthermore, if one essence benefits and another harms, they would cancel each other out, but in the world each has a benefit in its context, which is a true proof that the Manager is one, as He restrains harmful things from acting fully so that benefit may reach whom He wills. The passage then turns to the purpose of intellects: they are not created for eating and drinking, but for reflection and consideration (ʿibra and naẓar). Angels, who abstain from eating and drinking, exemplify this. Therefore, it is necessary in wisdom to create diverse essences to make reflection and consideration complete. Finally, Maturidi notes a witnessed principle: one who does both matters (i.e., creates contrasts) is more perfect, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
عقل ('aql - intellect)
عبرة ('ibra - reflection)
نظر (naẓar - consideration)
حكمة (ḥikma - wisdom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellect is primarily for survival and fulfilling physical needs.
Correction: Maturidi argues that intellect is created for higher purposes like reflection and consideration, not just for eating and drinking.

Checkpoint

B) Reflection and consideration

D) Pleasure

Key Takeaway
Intellect is created for reflection and consideration, not for mere physical sustenance; diversity in creation enables this higher purpose.

Identify one worldly distraction you will minimize for the next week to free up mental space for reflection.
?
Maturidi says diversity in creation enables complete reflection. What diversity in your life—people with different beliefs, challenges you resist, or aspects of nature you ignore—are you overlooking? This week, intentionally engage with something or someone unfamiliar to you, seeking through that the wisdom of the Creator.

Refutation of Dualists on Creation from Nothing
Maturidi refutes dualists' denial of creation ex nihilo

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the dualists' denial of creation from nothing by showing their own principles are equally beyond imagination, and the argument from witnessed actions and God's attributes.

Core Idea
Dualists cannot deny creation from nothing while accepting unimaginable first principles.

Maturidi engages with the dualists (thnawiyya) who reject creation ex nihilo on the grounds that it is inconceivable. He argues that their own foundational principles—whether spirit, intellect, or senses—are equally beyond imagination. Moreover, he points to the witnessed actions of the weak and ignorant as evidence that things can come from nothing, making it more fitting to attribute such origination to the Creator of the entire world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Familiarize yourself with Maturidi's dense argument.
The passage contains multiple conditional arguments.
2
Identify the dualists' objection and Maturidi's counter
Notice that the dualists deny creation from nothing because it is beyond imagination. Maturidi responds that their own principles (spirit, intellect, senses) are also beyond imagination.
3
Examine the argument from witnessed actions
Maturidi brings up the actions of weak and ignorant people as evidence that things can come from nothing. This is an empirical observation.
Consider how this analogy supports creation ex nihilo.
4
Reflect on the conclusion about God's attributes
The final part references God's self-sufficiency, power, and transcendence, emphasizing that inability to grasp wisdom does not negate creation.
The formula 'upon Him we depend' reinforces reliance on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن الذي دعى الثنوية إلى إنكار شيء من لا شيء خروجه عن التصور في العقول ، أو تقديرهم في تعرف الحكمة في العقل ما عاينوا بينهم ، ولو علموا أن القول بمبادئ العالم على ما عندهم في الخروج من التصور في الوهم مثل الذى أنكروا ، أو من الروح والعقل والحواس ، أو خروج حكمهم عن التصور في الوهم لما أنكروا . ثم لو علموا أنهم شهدوا فعل الضعفاء الجهال بأنفسهم على ما علموا بالخبر أنهم ، ثم كانوا ، لعلموا أن الأشياء من غير شيء مع أو خروج ما معهم أحق أن تنسب إليه ، / من به جملة العالم . ثم لو علموا غناه وقدرته وتعاليه عن تضق قلوبهم عند قصورها عن درك الحكمة في خلقه ، وعلى الله صفة الخلق لم توكل ، وبه نستعين .
Moreover, what called the dualists to deny that a thing comes from nothing is its being outside perception in minds, or their estimation in recognizing wisdom in the intellect of what they witnessed among themselves. Had they known that the statement about the principles of the world according to them in being outside imagination is like that which they denied, or from spirit, intellect, and senses, or their judgment being outside imagination, they would not have denied. Then, had they known that they witnessed the action of the weak and ignorant upon themselves according to what they learned by report—then they were—they would know that things from nothing, or the emergence of what is with them, are more worthy of being attributed to Him, from whom is the whole world. Then, had they known His Self-sufficiency, Power, and Exaltedness beyond what their hearts constrict at their incapacity to grasp the wisdom in His creation—and upon Allah is the attribute of creation, they would not rely, and upon Him we depend.
Source pages p. 767

Commentary
This passage refutes the dualists (thnawiyya) who deny creation ex nihilo. Maturidi explains that their denial arises because they think it is beyond conceptual imagination. But he counters that their own explanations—whether they posit spirit, intellect, or senses as first principles—are equally beyond imagination. So consistency demands they accept creation from nothing as well. He then gives another argument: one can observe weak and ignorant people performing actions (like creating things from nothing, in a manner of speaking, through their own power). Since these actions are witnessed, they actually provide evidence that things can come from nothing, and by analogy, it is more fitting to attribute such origination to the Creator of the entire world. Finally, Maturidi notes that if the dualists truly understood God's self-sufficiency, power, and transcendence, they would not be distressed by their own inability to fully grasp the wisdom in creation; rather, they would rely on God. The passage ends with the formula 'upon Him we depend.'

Correction: Maturidi shows that dualists' own first principles are equally inconceivable, and observed actions of the weak and ignorant provide evidence for creation from nothing.

Checkpoint

D) Because they are ignorant of logic.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes dualists by showing their own first principles are as unimaginable as creation from nothing, and witness of actions supports it.

Will you now humbly accept truths revealed by God even when they transcend your understanding?

The Oneness of the Divine Manager
Maturidi argues that the manager of the body and the world must be one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational proof that the manager of the body and the world must be a single, unified entity, and why alternative views involving mixture or multiple managers are logically unsustainable.

Core Idea
The oneness of the divine manager is proven by the impossibility of multiple managers and the unity of cosmic control.

Maturidi presents a logical proof for tawhid by analyzing the concept of management in the human body and the universe. He argues that just as a single life animates and uses the body, a single intermediary must manage both the higher and lower realms. He then dismantles any notion of multiple managers or mixture, showing that such ideas are inconceivable and have no basis in observed reality. This passage grounds the core Islamic belief in the oneness of Allah in rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Notice that Maturidi begins with a conditional: if the life in the body is its sense and user, then the intermediary (the life) must be the one managing both high and low. This sets up the analogy between the body and the universe.
2
Identify the conclusion
From the premise, he concludes that the deity in reality is one, or else the idea of mixture and imagination would be invalid. This is the core thesis: the divine manager is one.
The term 'mixture' (imtizāj) likely refers to the idea of multiple managers or a composite agent.
3
Examine the supporting argument
Maturidi argues that no human knows the origin of mixture, can correct its corruption, or repel its harm. Therefore, the manager must be one and distinct from the claimed mixture, which itself is under the management of the one.
4
Grasp the final analogy
He draws an equivalence between causing a mixture from nothing and causing anything else from nothing, and between the possibility of change by a powerful agent and the attribution of accidents to that agent. Both cases are equally beyond human perception, reinforcing the oneness of the divine manager.
The missing word in the Arabic (marked with dots) does not affect the overall argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإنسان إن كانت الحياة التى فى البدن فهى محسه للبدن مستعملة له ، فيجب أن يكون الواسط هو الذى له تدبير الغالى والسافل ، وهو المستعمل لهما ، فيصير الإله في الحقيقة واحدا أو يبطل الامتزاج وما ذكر من الخيال وهى حياته خطأ؛ إذ لا إنسان يعرف تدبير ثم إشارته إلى الامتزاج ابتدائه، ولا أصلح ما فسد منه، ولا دفع ما حل به، ثبت أن المدبر واحد، وهو غير الذي ذكر، وأن الذى ذكر تحت تدبير الواحد. ثم لا فرق بين أن يحدث مزاجا لم يكن لا عن أصل هو امتزاج وبين أن يحدث ..... لم يكن لا عن أصل البينونة، ثم لا فرق بين إمكان تغير قد تم إلى احتمال الحوادث بعد أن لم تكن كذلك بقدرة قادر وبين أن يكون الحوادث به، لا يقلب القديم إلى معنى الحديث؛ إذ هما جميعا في البعد عن البصر في الوهم واحد. و بالله المعونة والنجاة.
And if the life that is in the body is its sense for the body and its user, then it is necessary that the intermediary is the one who has the management of the high and the low, and he is the user of both, so the deity in reality becomes one, or the mixture and what is mentioned of imagination is invalid, and it is a mistake; for no human knows then his reference to the mixture from its beginning, nor does he correct what is corrupted from it, nor does he repel what befalls it. It is established that the manager is one, and he is other than the one mentioned, and that the one mentioned is under the management of the one. Then there is no difference between causing a mixture that was not from an origin that is a mixture and between causing ..... that was not from an origin of separation. Then there is no difference between the possibility of changing what has been completed to the capacity for accidents after not being so by the power of a powerful one and between that the accidents are by him; he does not turn the eternal into the meaning of the originated; for both are one in distance from perception in estimation. And with God is help and deliverance.
Source pages p. 771

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the oneness of the divine manager (al-mudabbir). Maturidi begins with a conditional: if the life that is in the body is what animates and uses the body, then the intermediary must be the one who manages both the higher and lower aspects. This implies that the true deity is one, or else the idea of mixture (imtizāj) and imagination fails. Maturidi then supports this by noting that no human can know the origin of mixture, nor can they fix its corruption or repel what affects it. Therefore, the manager must be one, distinct from the claimed mixture, and the claimed mixture is itself under the management of the one. He then argues that there is no difference between creating a mixture from nothing and creating something else from nothing, and no difference between the possibility of change by a powerful agent and the attribution of accidents to that agent. Both cases are equally inconceivable to the mind, establishing the oneness of the divine.

Key Terms
المدبر
الامتزاج
الحياة
تدبير
الوهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument relies on human inability to perceive the manager, implying that the manager's existence depends on human perception.
Correction: Maturidi does not rely on human perception but on logical necessity: the impossibility of multiple managers and the incoherence of mixture as an alternative explanation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument in this passage, what is the conclusion about the manager of the body and the world?
A) He is multiple and operates through mixture.
B) He is one and the mixture is under his management.
C) The manager is the life itself.
D) There is no manager.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves the oneness of the divine manager by showing that the manager of the body must be one, and that any alternative (mixture or multiple managers) is unsustainable and inconceivable.

How can you realign your actions to reflect the oneness of the Manager? Write one specific change you will make this week.
?
The proof concludes that the manager is one. How does this truth affect your sense of accountability and purpose today? What will you do to submit more fully to that one Manager, trusting Him alone as the manager of your affairs?

The Possibility of Creation from Nothing
Maturidi defends the rational viability of creation ex nihilo.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that creation from nothing is rationally defensible and not more inconceivable than natural processes like embryogenesis.

Core Idea
Creation from nothing is no more impossible than natural causation.

Maturidi begins by addressing a common objection: if creation from nothing is beyond our capacity to conceive, then it must be impossible. He turns this objection on its head, arguing that natural processes—which we often take for granted—are equally beyond full comprehension. This sets the stage for a refutation of naturalistic explanations and a defense of divine creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi sets up the argument by equating the inconceivability of creation ex nihilo with that of natural processes.
Pay attention to the phrase 'خروجه من وسع وارتفاعه عن التصور' (coming out of capacity and being beyond conception).
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi claims that no one denies the possibility of creation from nothing, because even natural processes (like the body's formation in the womb) are beyond full understanding. Find the sentence that states this.
3
Examine the comparison
The passage compares creation from nothing to several natural theories: natures (الطبائع), movements of stars, mixing of light and darkness. Maturidi says all these are 'outside the way' he mentioned. What does he mean?
He means they are equally inconceivable as ultimate explanations.
4
Reflect on the implication
If both creation from nothing and natural processes are beyond full conception, then rejecting one while accepting the other is inconsistent. Maturidi uses this to open the door for affirming creation by God.
This is a logical move: if you accept natural causation despite its mystery, you must accept divine creation too.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن لم يكن في خلق الشيء من غير شيء إلا خروجه من وسع وارتفاعه عن التصور فلا أحد امتنع عن القول بتحقيق مثله؛ لأن إنشاء الجسم وكونه في الأرحام بالطبائع وحدوثه بحركات النجوم أو خروج العالم عن هذا الطر وامتزاج النور والظلمة ثم التباين خارج عن الوجه الذي [ذكر]. على أن حقيقة كل شيء من تأمله كذلك نجده؛ لأنه ليس في النطفة ولا في جميع الأغذية ولا في الأرحام شيء من معاني البشر: ثم مما له من العقل والسمع والنظر، فإنما ذلك خارج عن ذلك بتقدير عليم حكيم. وكذلك جميع الطبائع المختلفة أو جواهر الخير والشر لو خلى بينها وبين عملها ما ظهر بها جوهر ولا يمكن بها خلق، بالكون بمثله أبعد عن التصور في العقل، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then, if there is nothing in creating a thing from nothing except its coming out of capacity and its being beyond conception, then no one refrains from affirming the realization of its like; because the origination of the body and its being in the wombs through natures, and its occurrence through movements of stars, or the world's coming out of this manner and the mixing of light and darkness then separation, is outside the way that [mentioned]. Rather, the reality of everything upon reflection we find it so; because there is nothing in the sperm-drop nor in all nutrients nor in the wombs of the meanings of humans: then from what has of intellect, hearing, and sight, that is only outside of that by the decree of a Knowing, Wise One. And likewise all different natures or substances of good and evil, if left between them and their action, no substance would appear through them and no creation would be possible through them, indeed existence like that is more distant from conception in the intellect, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 773

Commentary
This passage is a proof for creation ex nihilo (khalaq al-shay' min la shay') and a refutation of naturalistic explanations. Maturidi argues that if creation from nothing implies only that it is beyond capacity and conception, then no one can deny its possibility—because even natural processes (like embryogenesis through natures or stars) are also beyond full comprehension. More importantly, upon reflection, nothing in the sperm, nutrients, or womb contains the essence of a human (with intellect, hearing, sight). These faculties come from outside, by the decree of a Knowing, Wise Creator. Similarly, all different natures and substances (of good and evil) if left to themselves would not produce any substance or creation. The very existence of such a world is even further from mental conception. Thus natural causation fails to explain creation, and the only valid conclusion is creation by God.

Key Terms
خلق الشيء من غير شيء
الطبائع
حركات النجوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that creation from nothing is utterly impossible because we cannot conceive it, while natural processes are fully understood and acceptable.
Correction: Maturidi shows that natural processes are just as inconceivable in their ultimate nature; thus, consistency requires accepting both or neither.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi claim about natural processes like embryogenesis through natures or movements of stars?
A) They are fully understood by human reason.
B) They are entirely impossible.
C) They are as far beyond human capacity and conception as creation from nothing.
D) They are the only true explanation for creation.

Key Takeaway
If natural processes are accepted despite being beyond full human conception, then creation from nothing cannot be rejected on the basis of inconceivability alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you accept natural explanations for things you don't fully understand, yet reject the possibility of creation from nothing because it seems inconceivable? What does this reveal about your standard of evidence? Will you commit to applying the same standard to divine truths as you do to natural phenomena?
?
If you were to honestly examine your own life, are there areas where you demand a higher level of proof for God's creation than you do for the natural world? What step will you take today to realign your expectations with the humility shown in Maturidi's argument?
?
The passage argues that no one refrains from affirming natural processes despite their mystery. Have you ever felt reluctant to accept a divine truth simply because you couldn't grasp how it works? How can you cultivate trust in God's power over your limited comprehension starting now?

Refuting Natural Causes: The Need for a Wise Creator
Maturidi employs empirical reflection and argument from design.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's empirical argument that human faculties (intellect, hearing, sight) and the existence of substances cannot originate from physical elements like sperm, natures, or mixtures, but must come from a Knowing, Wise Creator.

Core Idea
Human faculties are not in the sperm; they come from Allah's decree.

Having established that creation from nothing is not rationally objectionable, Maturidi now provides a positive argument: upon reflection, we see that the components of the human body (sperm, nutrients, womb) contain none of the distinctively human qualities like intellect and senses. These must therefore come from an external, wise source. He extends this reasoning to all substances and natures, showing that they cannot produce anything on their own.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'على أن حقيقة كل شيء من تأمله كذلك نجده'. Notice the shift from the previous argument to a reflective observation.
The phrase 'من تأمله' means 'upon reflection'—this is an empirical appeal.
2
Identify the evidence from human faculties
Maturidi points out that the sperm, nutrients, and womb contain nothing of human qualities like intellect, hearing, or sight. Find where he states this.
These faculties are 'outside of that' (i.e., beyond the physical elements).
3
Understand the conclusion about natures and substances
The passage extends to all natures and substances: if left to themselves, they would produce nothing. Why does Maturidi say their existence is even more distant from conception?
Because if simple elements cannot even produce human faculties, the existence of a complex world from mere matter is even harder to explain.
4
Connect to the role of God
The faculties come 'بتقدير عليم حكيم' (by the decree of a Knowing, Wise One). This is the positive conclusion: the only adequate explanation is a wise Creator.
Note the phrase 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' at the end, affirming dependence on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن لم يكن في خلق الشيء من غير شيء إلا خروجه من وسع وارتفاعه عن التصور فلا أحد امتنع عن القول بتحقيق مثله؛ لأن إنشاء الجسم وكونه في الأرحام بالطبائع وحدوثه بحركات النجوم أو خروج العالم عن هذا الطر وامتزاج النور والظلمة ثم التباين خارج عن الوجه الذي [ذكر]. على أن حقيقة كل شيء من تأمله كذلك نجده؛ لأنه ليس في النطفة ولا في جميع الأغذية ولا في الأرحام شيء من معاني البشر: ثم مما له من العقل والسمع والنظر، فإنما ذلك خارج عن ذلك بتقدير عليم حكيم. وكذلك جميع الطبائع المختلفة أو جواهر الخير والشر لو خلى بينها وبين عملها ما ظهر بها جوهر ولا يمكن بها خلق، بالكون بمثله أبعد عن التصور في العقل، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then, if there is nothing in creating a thing from nothing except its coming out of capacity and its being beyond conception, then no one refrains from affirming the realization of its like; because the origination of the body and its being in the wombs through natures, and its occurrence through movements of stars, or the world's coming out of this manner and the mixing of light and darkness then separation, is outside the way that [mentioned]. Rather, the reality of everything upon reflection we find it so; because there is nothing in the sperm-drop nor in all nutrients nor in the wombs of the meanings of humans: then from what has of intellect, hearing, and sight, that is only outside of that by the decree of a Knowing, Wise One. And likewise all different natures or substances of good and evil, if left between them and their action, no substance would appear through them and no creation would be possible through them, indeed existence like that is more distant from conception in the intellect, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 773

Commentary
This passage is a proof for creation ex nihilo (khalaq al-shay' min la shay') and a refutation of naturalistic explanations. Maturidi argues that if creation from nothing implies only that it is beyond capacity and conception, then no one can deny its possibility—because even natural processes (like embryogenesis through natures or stars) are also beyond full comprehension. More importantly, upon reflection, nothing in the sperm, nutrients, or womb contains the essence of a human (with intellect, hearing, sight). These faculties come from outside, by the decree of a Knowing, Wise Creator. Similarly, all different natures and substances (of good and evil) if left to themselves would not produce any substance or creation. The very existence of such a world is even further from mental conception. Thus natural causation fails to explain creation, and the only valid conclusion is creation by God.

Key Terms
النطفة
تقدير عليم حكيم
جواهر الخير والشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that human faculties like intelligence and perception are automatically produced by the physical development of the embryo, without need for divine intervention.
Correction: Maturidi points out that the physical ingredients (sperm, etc.) contain none of these faculties, so they must be granted from an external, wise source.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say would happen if all different natures and substances were left to themselves?
A) They would eventually produce a human being.
B) They would produce only good or only evil.
C) No substance or creation would appear through them.
D) They would mix randomly and produce nothing.

Key Takeaway
Human faculties and the existence of substances cannot arise from physical matter alone; they require the decree of a Knowing, Wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use your intellect to make a decision, do you pause to acknowledge that this very ability is a gift from Allah that could not have arisen from the material world? How will you cultivate this awareness daily?
?
If you truly believed that every faculty you possess is by the decree of a Knowing, Wise Creator, how would that change your attitude towards your own abilities and shortcomings?
?
This lesson forces us to admit that without Allah's decree, there is no power. In what area of your life are you still relying on your own strength rather than His? What concrete step can you take today to shift that reliance?

Purposeful Creation and the Limits of Imagination
Maturidi presents creation as purposeful and refutes denial of the unseen based on imagination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the purposefulness of creation and the dependence of imagination on sensory experience to refute those who deny the unseen.

Core Idea
Imagination cannot disprove what it cannot conceive.

Maturidi begins by establishing that the world is created with purpose, providing humans with proofs through blessings and trials. He then confronts a critical objection: can we deny something simply because it is not perceived by the senses or imagined? Through analyzing the nature of imagination (al-wahm), he shows that such denial is logically flawed, especially in the case of the Magians who blindly follow predecessors.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on creation's purpose
Read the opening lines that describe God placing everything in its proper place and testing humans with blessings and trials.
Notice how the variety of creation serves as proofs and warnings.
2
Analyze the refutation of denial by imagination
Maturidi argues that if one could deny what is not imaginable, then any defective sense could deny what it perceives. This refutes the Magians.
The argument refutes those who rely on sensory limitation to deny the unseen.
3
See how imagination depends on sensed things
Imagination (al-wahm) is based on estimation from sensed objects. Since God is not sensed and has no likeness, He cannot be estimated by imagination.
This shows that imagination cannot be used to deny God's existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووضع كل شيء موضعه ، وأن الله تعالى إذ لم يخلق لحاجات نفسه وإنما خلق بذاته ، إنه خالق ليكون الخلق الذي ركب فيهم العقول وجعلهم أهل المعرفة ، بالنعم و البلايا يمتحنون ، بوضع كل شيء موضعه والقيام بالشكر لما أنعم عليهم بأن جعل لهم جميع الخلائق على اختلاف جواهرهم أدله وعبرا ومحنة وابتلاء بمعاداة جواهر وموالاة أخرى ، وليغرفوا كيفية الاتقاء ووجه الجذر وما فيه الرُّعْبُ ووجوه المبادرة فى ذلك للعواقب المحمودة في العقول وإبقاء المكروهة فيها بما عاينوا من مختلف الجواهر والأحوال في حق الترغيب والترحيب ليكون الوعد والوعيد مقدرا عن الحسن والعيان ؛ إذ ذلك طريق المعارف و به يوصل إلى درك النهايات ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ولو جاز إنكار الشيء لا من شيء بما لا يتصور في الوهم الجاز لكل مؤوف الحاسة إنكار ما يدرك بها إذ هو غير مدرك إنكار كل غائب لم يبلغه الحاسة وفي ذلك نقض المجوسية وغيرهم : إذ جميعا اتبعوا أوائلهم . ثم التصور في الوهم تقدیره مما تقع عليه الحاسة ، إذا ارتفعت فتصور حال وقوع الحاسة في وهمه ، أو يقدر مثله فى الوهم . ثم الله سبحانه لم يعرف من طريق الحواس ولا له مثال في المعروف ، بطل التقدير به . ثم الأصل أن التصور في الوهم هو علم الحسن ، : أو في علم الحس دليل لزوم العلم بما لم يحس ، ولأن يعرف : إذ كل ذي جاهل بمائية الحس وكيفيته ، فلزم ذلك في كل حس هو كذلك . فيجب كون الحواس بمن يعرف حقائقها وينشئها ، على ما يرى أهل الحواس أن الذي أنشأها لا يحتمل إدراكه بالحواس ؛ إذ كل ذي حاسة جاهل بما عليه أحواله وعاجز عن احتمال وسعه ما فسد منه ، فأوجب ذا أن وراء هذا عليم حكيم ، لا يحتمل ما احتمل المحسوس ؛ إذ لو جاز واحتمل ، لم يحتمل كون المحسوس به ، لم يحتمل بأمثالنا ، وبالله العصمة والنجاة
And He placed everything in its proper place, and that God Most High did not create for the needs of Himself but created by His essence, He is Creator so that creation—in whom He instilled intellects and made them people of knowledge—are tested with blessings and trials, by placing everything in its proper place and performing gratitude for what He bestowed upon them by making for them all creatures, despite the difference of their essences, proofs, lessons, trial, and testing by befriending some essences and opposing others, that they may know the manner of piety and the aspect of caution and what contains fear and the aspects of initiative in that for praiseworthy consequences in intellects and the preservation of detestable things in them through what they witnessed of various essences and states in terms of encouraging and warning, so that the promise and threat are estimated by the sense and sight; for that is the path of knowledge and by it one reaches the perception of ends, and there is no power except with God. And if it were permissible to deny a thing from nothing by what is not imaginable in the imagination, then it would be permissible for every defective sense to deny what it perceives, since it is not perceived — denial of every unseen that the sense has not reached, and in that is the refutation of Magianism and others: for all followed their predecessors. Then imagination in the mind is an estimation of what the sense falls upon; when it is removed, one imagines the state of the sense's occurrence in his imagination, or he estimates something like it in the imagination. Then God, may He be glorified, is not known through the senses, nor does He have a likeness among known things, so estimation by it is invalid. Then the principle is that imagination in the mind is knowledge of the sense, or in the knowledge of the sense is a proof of the necessity of knowledge of what is not sensed, and so that one may know: for every possessor of sense is ignorant of the quiddity of sense and its modality, so that follows for every sense it is likewise. So it is necessary that the senses belong to one who knows their realities and originates them, according to what the people of the senses see that the one who originated them cannot be perceived by the senses; for every possessor of sense is ignorant of what his states are upon and incapable of bearing the extent of what is corrupted from it, so this necessitates that behind this is a Knowing, Wise One, who does not bear what the sensed bears; for if it were permissible and possible, it would not be possible for the sensed to be by it, it would not be possible by ones like us, and with God is protection and deliverance.
Source pages p. 774

Commentary
This passage is a complex rational proof for the existence and transcendence of God, structured in several steps. First, Maturidi establishes that God placed everything in its proper place and created humans with intellects to know Him, testing them through blessings and trials. The variety of created things serves as proofs and warnings. Then he launches into a refutation of those who deny the unseen because it is not perceived by the senses. He argues that if one were to deny whatever is not imaginable through the senses, then anyone with defective senses could deny what they perceive — absurd. This refutes the Magians and others who blindly follow predecessors. Next, he analyzes the imagination (al-wahm): imagination constructs ideas from sensed things; but God is not known through the senses nor has He a likeness among known things, so He cannot be estimated by imagination. The principle is that imagination is based on sense-knowledge, but the knowledge of sense itself provides evidence for what is not sensed. Every person who has sense is ignorant of the true nature and modality of sense — thus the senses themselves require a Creator who knows their realities and originates them. The senses cannot perceive their own Creator because every possessor of sense is ignorant of its own inner states and cannot bear the extent of sensory corruption. Therefore, there must be a Knowing, Wise Being beyond sensory perception, who does not bear the limitations of the sensed. The argument concludes that this reasoning leads to the affirmation of God's existence and transcendence.

Key Terms
الحواس
الوهم
التقدير
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something is not perceived by the senses or imagined, it can be denied as non-existent.
Correction: Maturidi shows this leads to absurdity because then any defective sense could deny what it does not perceive, and it would deny all unseen things. This refutes the Magians who deny the unseen.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument, what is the basis of imagination (al-wahm)?
A) Pure reason independent of senses
B) Estimation based on previously sensed things
C) Direct knowledge of the unseen
D) Divine revelation

Key Takeaway
Imagination is limited to sense-based estimation, so it cannot be used to deny what lies beyond sensory perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth about God or the unseen simply because you could not imagine it or sense it? What would it cost you to submit your imagination to your intellect?
?
If your imagination is limited to what you have seen, how can you claim to have a complete picture of reality? What unseen truths are you currently ignoring because they don't fit your mental models?
?
This passage calls you to gratitude by recognizing creation as proof. What in your life have you taken for granted as mere coincidence rather than as a sign placed by a wise Creator? What would change if you saw every blessing and trial as a deliberate test?

Senses Necessitate a Transcendent Creator
Maturidi argues from the limitations of sense-perception to a transcendent Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the ignorance of sense-perception to prove the existence of a Creator beyond sensory reach.

Core Idea
The very nature of the senses points to a Knower beyond them.

Continuing his proof, Maturidi now turns to a deeper analysis: if imagination is based on sense, what does sense itself reveal? He argues that every person with senses is ignorant of the true quiddity and modality of sense. Therefore, the senses themselves require a Creator who knows their realities and cannot be perceived by them. This leads to the affirmation of a Knowing, Wise One transcendent over the created world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle: imagination is knowledge of sense
Read the opening line establishing that imagination is based on sense-knowledge, which provides evidence for the unseen.
This sets up the argument that sense itself points beyond.
2
Recognize the ignorance of sense-quiddity
Maturidi states that every possessor of sense is ignorant of the true nature and modality of sense.
This ignorance is key to the proof.
3
See the necessity of a Creator for the senses
Since we are ignorant, the senses must belong to a Creator who knows their realities and originated them.
The Creator cannot be perceived by the senses.
4
Conclude with the transcendence of the Creator
The argument concludes that behind the senses is a Knowing, Wise One who does not bear the limitations of sensed things.
This affirms God's transcendence.

?

Knowing now that they are limited and even corrupt, will you commit today to seeking knowledge of the Unseen through revelation and reason, rather than through your unreliable senses? What specific step will you take to put this into practice?

The Magnet Stone Analogy: Divine Selection for Prophethood
Maturidi presents the fourth objection and answers with divine selection analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the analogy of a magnet stone to explain divine selection for prophethood and refute the objection that human effort could replicate the Quran.

Core Idea
God gives prophets a unique power that cannot be claimed or imitated.

The fourth objection claims that humans have tried hard to produce something like the Quran but failed, implying it is within human capacity. Maturidi answers by introducing the concept of divine selection: God grants prophets a unique power, just as He gives a magnet its special property, which no one else can claim. This lesson unpacks that analogy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the answer
First read the Arabic passage that contains the objection and the beginning of the answer, focusing on the magnet stone analogy. Then read the translation to capture the flow.
Notice the phrase 'كما منع من يظفر بحجر المغناطيس' — this is the core analogy.
2
Understand the objection
The objection states that people have exerted themselves in poetry for a year, but if it were possible, they would have succeeded. Instead, they gave up and tried to extinguish the light of Islam. What assumption does this objection make about human ability?
The objection assumes that the Quran is a work of human linguistic skill that can be matched by enough effort.
3
Analyze the magnet stone analogy
Maturidi says God singles out a prophet with a power no one shares, and prevents him from claiming prophethood by speech, just as He prevents someone from obtaining the magnet's property. Why does this analogy work? What does it teach about divine selection?
The magnet's property is inherent and cannot be claimed by others — similarly, prophetic power is a divine gift.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how this analogy refutes the objection: if the Quran were merely human, it could be replicated. But because it is a divine gift, it is unique and inimitable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع قد تكلفوا المجاوبات لأقوام معروفين في فن حتى اجتهدوا في قصيدة حولاً ، فلو كان يحتمل وسعهم يرجون البلوغ بطرق ما احتمل تركهم ، وفى ذلك تشبيه على القوم ، وقد بذلوا مهجهم ودنياهم في إطفاء هذا النور. وجواب الرابع أن الله تعالى إذا خص أحدا بقوة لا يشاركه فيها أحد يمنعه عن دعوى النبوة باللفظ كما منع من يظفر بحجر المغناطيس ، ولو علم أنه يدعى لا يعطيه . والثانى أن لا أحد في شيء له فضل قوة إلا طمع غيره استمام ذلك أو عمل ذلك النوع بقدر قوته ، والدليل ما يخرج من الطباع و بعد ، فإنه لو كان له فى ذلك فضل قوة / بها عمل لكان لا يتمكن نيلها [?]، وليست لهم ؛ إذ لا يوجد مثل ذا فى شيء من الأمور ، دل أن الله جعل فيه ليكون آية لقوله بهم وسنذكر جمل هذه التأويلات بعد الفراغ من فصوله وقوله على البديهة ، فقد أمهلوا ، مع ما لم يحتمل أن يكون من البشر يعلم بفضل القوة ما تسأل عنه ، وقد مالم تكلفوا الاشعار ثم نصب الحروب وجمع الأعوان وبذل الأعيان ثم اقتتال الأقران والمبادرات الفظيعة ، فلو كان ومهم يحتمل القيام بذلك أيسر عليهم، ثم قد دعوا إلى اتيان السورة ، نحو ثلاث آيات ، لو احتملها وسع البشر لكان ساعة من النهار كافية لذلك
The fourth: They have taken on responses to known people in a field until they exerted themselves in a poem for a year. If it were possible within their capacity, they would hope to achieve it through methods, but they did not do it; and in that is a comparison against the people, and they have sacrificed their lives and their worldly goods to extinguish this light. And the answer to the fourth: That God, exalted, when He singles out someone with a power that no one shares with him, He prevents him from claiming prophethood through speech, just as He prevents whoever obtains the magnet stone; and if he knew that he would claim, He would not give it. And the second: That no one has a superiority of power in anything except that another covets completing that or doing that type according to his power; the evidence is what comes out from nature. And then, if he had in that a superiority of power by which he acted, he would not be able to attain it [?], and they do not have it; since nothing like this exists in any matter, this indicates that God placed it in him to be a sign for His saying. And we will mention the summary of these interpretations after finishing its sections. And his saying spontaneously: They were given respite, along with what it is not possible for a human to know by superiority of power that which you ask about; and they did not undertake poetry, then setting up wars, gathering supporters, sacrificing lives, then fighting peers, and terrible initiations. If it were possible for them to undertake that, it would be easier for them; then they were called to bring a surah, about three verses; if it were possible for humans, an hour of the day would be sufficient for that.
Source pages p. 791

Commentary
This passage contains a fourth objection to the miraculous nature of the Qur'an and its answer. The objection states that people have worked hard to compose poems over a year, but if it were humanly possible to produce something like the Qur'an, they would have succeeded, yet they abandoned the effort, sacrificing their lives to extinguish the light of Islam. Maturidi answers that when God selects a prophet with a unique power, He prevents him from claiming prophethood by speech, similar to how He prevents someone from obtaining the magnet's property. If a person knew he would falsely claim prophethood, God would not give him that power. The second point is that if someone had a superior power in a field, others would try to equal or surpass it, as seen in natural inclinations. But since no one can replicate the Qur'an, it proves that God made it a unique miracle. He also mentions that the Prophet was given time, and despite not being a poet before, he delivered the Qur'an spontaneously. The Arabs were challenged to produce even three verses, but they could not, proving it is beyond human capacity.

Key Terms
نبوة
قوة
آية
حجر المغناطيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran can be matched by sufficient human effort, as shown by poets' attempts.
Correction: The Quran is a divine gift with a unique power that cannot be claimed or imitated by any human, just as the property of a magnet stone cannot be acquired by effort.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi compare the prophet's unique power to?
A) A magnet stone
B) A poet's craft
C) The power of nature
D) An army's strength

Key Takeaway
God grants prophets a unique, inimitable power, like the property of a magnet, which cannot be claimed by others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something, do you sincerely attribute it to God's gift or secretly credit your own effort? How does the magnet stone analogy challenge your pride?
?
If God can prevent a prophet from claiming his own power, what does that mean for the way you view your own talents? Are you willing to see them as purely borrowed?
?
The people in this objection sacrificed their lives to extinguish the light of prophethood. What have you sacrificed to oppose the truth? And more importantly, what are you willing to sacrifice to accept it?

The Argument from Universal Competition and the Spontaneous Quran
Maturidi presents the second argument and the spontaneous delivery proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second argument: that if anyone had a superior power, others would try to replicate it, and the Quran's uniqueness proves it is a divine miracle, supported by the Prophet's spontaneous delivery.

Core Idea
Unmatched superiority proves divine intervention, not human skill.

Maturidi continues his answer with a logical argument: whenever someone has a superior power in any field, others naturally covet and try to match it. But the Quran remains unmatched, proving its divine origin. He also highlights that the Prophet delivered it spontaneously, without prior practice, and the Arabs were challenged to produce just three verses—an impossible task. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the answer
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'والثانى' to the end, along with the translation. Notice the logical flow: premise, evidence, conclusion.
2
Understand the universal competition argument
Maturidi argues that if anyone possessed a superior power, others would try to match or surpass it. Find the evidence he gives from 'nature' (الطباع). Why does this prove the Quran is unique?
The evidence is that in all natural things, people attempt to imitate excellence, but no one has succeeded with the Quran.
3
Analyze the spontaneous delivery and challenge
The passage mentions that the Prophet spoke spontaneously (على البديهة) and was given respite, yet he was not a poet. Then the challenge to produce a surah (three verses) is mentioned. Why does this support the argument?
If it were humanly possible, an hour would suffice; but they could not do it, showing it is beyond human capacity.
4
Connect to the lesson's core idea
The core idea is that the Quran's unmatched superiority, combined with the Prophet's spontaneous delivery and the failed challenge, proves it is a miracle from God, not a product of human effort.

The Unchanging Meaning of Prophethood
Al-Maturidi establishes the unchanging nature of prophethood's essential proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the essential meaning of prophethood, which is proven by miracles, remains identical across all prophets, even if the miracles themselves differ in form.

Core Idea
The meaning that makes a miracle a proof is unchanging.

Imam al-Maturidi begins by asserting a fundamental principle: the core meaning that necessitates prophethood does not change from prophet to prophet. This principle is crucial for arguing that if one accepts the prophethood of earlier prophets based on miracles, then one must also accept the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) because the underlying proof is identical. In this passage, he explains that even if miracles are different in their external form, the essential quality that makes them 'miracles' is the same.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms like 'ma'na' (meaning) and 'ayah' (miracle/sign).
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence where al-Maturidi states that the meaning that makes a miracle a miracle is not different. This is the core thesis.
It is at: 'فإن المعنى الذي صارت الآية به آية غير مختلف'
3
Consider the opponents' objection
Al-Maturidi anticipates that opponents might cling to the outward forms (zawahir) of the verses. He argues that even if they do, they will find no one equal to Muhammad in miracle and elevation.
This shows that outward forms also point to Muhammad's superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحقيق ذلك أنه من المعاني التي توجب النبوة، ألزمناهم في نبوة محمد صلى الله عليه ذلك المعنى بعينه، وإن كانت الآية مختلفة بأنفسها، فإن المعنى الذي صارت الآية به آية غير مختلف، وإن تعلقوا بظواهر الآيات لم يجدوا لأحد مثل الذي لمحمد عليه السلام في الأعجوبة والرفعة، أو يخرجان على أمر واحد، وإن ادعوا موافقتنا إياهم فان جواب ذلك يخرج من وجوه: أحدها يسأل عن علتهم قبل كوننا وظهور موافقتنا، والثاني إنا قررنا بما ثبت لنا أن الذي أخبرنا بهم رسول، وأنتم تنكرونه، برهانكم؟، والثالث أن يقابلوا بالفرق الذي لم يقرّوا بما ادعوا، والرابع أن يقال: إنما أقررنا نحن ممن قد أقر بنبوه نبينا، فإن كان من يدعونه هو، فقد ثبتت نبوة نبينا، وإن لم يكن هو، فما الدلالة على نبوة محمد؟ سقط دليلكم، فها ممن ادعيتم له النبوة ليسلم لكم ما أردتم، وبالله المعونة.
The verification of that is that from the meanings that necessitate prophethood, we impose in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) that same meaning exactly, even if the miracle is different in its essence, for the meaning by which the miracle becomes a miracle is not different. And if they cling to the outward meanings of the verses, they will not find for anyone the like of what Muhammad (peace be upon him) had in miracle and elevation, or they come out on one matter. And if they claim our agreement with them, then the answer to that comes from several aspects: one of them is to ask about their reason before our existence and the appearance of our agreement. The second: we have established by what is proven to us that the one who informed us about them is a messenger, and you deny him—what is your proof? The third: that they should be confronted with the distinction which they did not acknowledge regarding what they claimed. The fourth: that it be said: we only acknowledge those who have acknowledged the prophethood of our prophet. So if the one they claim is him, then the prophethood of our prophet is proven; if he is not him, then what is the evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad? Your proof has fallen; so produce someone for whom you claimed prophethood so that what you want may be granted to you. And with God is help.
Source pages p. 809

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument about the unchanging nature of the essential meaning of prophethood across different prophets. The author begins by stating that the meaning that necessitates prophethood is the same for all prophets. Therefore, if opponents accept the prophethood of earlier prophets based on miracles, they must accept Muhammad’s prophethood because the underlying meaning that makes a miracle a proof of prophethood is identical, even if the miracles themselves differ in form. He then anticipates an objection: opponents might claim that the verses (miracles) of earlier prophets have outward signs that are not found in Muhammad’s miracle. The author replies that if they look at the outward aspects, they will find no one who surpasses Muhammad in miracle and elevation. Next, he addresses the possibility that opponents might claim that the author agrees with them (i.e., that the meaning is different). The author provides four responses: (1) Ask them what their reason was before the author existed and before his agreement appeared (i.e., their position must stand on its own). (2) The author has established that his informant is a messenger, which they deny; thus the burden of proof is on them. (3) Confront them with the distinction (between outward and inward meanings) that they themselves do not accept in their own claims. (4) The author only accepts those who acknowledge the prophethood of his own prophet; if the prophet they claim is Muhammad, then his prophethood is established; if not, they must provide evidence for their claimed prophet. The passage ends with a call for God’s assistance.

Key Terms
معنى النبوة (meaning of prophethood)
آية (miracle/sign)
ظواهر الآيات (outward meanings of verses)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the outward form of a miracle is what proves prophethood.
Correction: Al-Maturidi argues that it is the meaning that makes a miracle a miracle—the fact that it is a divine sign—that proves prophethood, not its external form.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maturidi, what is the relationship between the miracle of Muhammad and the miracles of previous prophets?
A) The miracles are different in essence, so the proof is different.
B) The meaning that makes a miracle a proof is the same, so the proof is the same.
C) Only the miracles of previous prophets are valid proofs.
D) Muhammad’s miracle is greater in outward form only.

Key Takeaway
The proof of prophethood lies in the unchanging meaning of a divine sign, not in its specific form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you engage with its miraculous meaning that proves prophethood, or do you get caught up in its outward form? What would change in your faith if you focused on that unchanging meaning?
?
Have you ever felt that because you didn't see a physical miracle like Musa's staff, your certainty in Muhammad's prophethood is somehow less? How does Al-Maturidi's argument challenge that feeling, and what can you do to strengthen your conviction starting today?
?
Al-Maturidi says that no one can find the like of Muhammad's miracle and elevation. Do you live as if you truly believe that the Qur'an is the greatest, most elevated miracle? What practical change would prove that belief is real in your daily life?

Four Responses to the Objection
Al-Maturidi presents four logical responses to a potential objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four logical responses al-Maturidi gives to the claim that Muslims agree with opponents on the nature of prophethood.

Core Idea
Four logical replies refute the claim of agreement with opponents.

In this passage, al-Maturidi anticipates a potential objection: opponents might claim that Muslims agree with them on the criteria for prophethood, thus undermining the argument for Muhammad's prophethood. He provides four distinct responses, each based on logical reasoning and the burden of proof. These responses demonstrate the strength of the Islamic position and challenge the opponents to present their own evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the four responses carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Identify each of the four responses. Notice how each response uses a different logical tactic: questioning the opponent's reason, shifting the burden of proof, pointing out inconsistencies in their own claims, and tying acceptance of prophethood to recognition of Muhammad.
The responses are numbered: 'one of them...', 'the second...', 'the third...', 'the fourth...'
2
Analyze the first response
Al-Maturidi asks the opponents about their reason for denying prophethood before Muslims existed. This challenges the basis of their objection.
This response shows that their objection is not based on new evidence but on prior position.
3
Analyze the second and third responses
The second response asserts the Muslim has proof that his informant is a messenger, and demands the opponents' proof. The third response points out that the opponents do not apply their own distinction consistently.
These responses shift the burden of proof onto the opponents.
4
Analyze the fourth response
This response ties the acceptance of any prophet to acceptance of Muhammad, creating a dilemma: if the opponent's claimed prophet is Muhammad, prophethood is proven; if not, they must provide evidence for their own prophet.
This response forces the opponents to provide an alternative proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحقيق ذلك أنه من المعاني التي توجب النبوة، ألزمناهم في نبوة محمد صلى الله عليه ذلك المعنى بعينه، وإن كانت الآية مختلفة بأنفسها، فإن المعنى الذي صارت الآية به آية غير مختلف، وإن تعلقوا بظواهر الآيات لم يجدوا لأحد مثل الذي لمحمد عليه السلام في الأعجوبة والرفعة، أو يخرجان على أمر واحد، وإن ادعوا موافقتنا إياهم فان جواب ذلك يخرج من وجوه: أحدها يسأل عن علتهم قبل كوننا وظهور موافقتنا، والثاني إنا قررنا بما ثبت لنا أن الذي أخبرنا بهم رسول، وأنتم تنكرونه، برهانكم؟، والثالث أن يقابلوا بالفرق الذي لم يقرّوا بما ادعوا، والرابع أن يقال: إنما أقررنا نحن ممن قد أقر بنبوه نبينا، فإن كان من يدعونه هو، فقد ثبتت نبوة نبينا، وإن لم يكن هو، فما الدلالة على نبوة محمد؟ سقط دليلكم، فها ممن ادعيتم له النبوة ليسلم لكم ما أردتم، وبالله المعونة.
The verification of that is that from the meanings that necessitate prophethood, we impose in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) that same meaning exactly, even if the miracle is different in its essence, for the meaning by which the miracle becomes a miracle is not different. And if they cling to the outward meanings of the verses, they will not find for anyone the like of what Muhammad (peace be upon him) had in miracle and elevation, or they come out on one matter. Your proof has fallen; so produce someone for whom you claimed prophethood so that what you want may be granted to you. And with God is help.

Commentary
This passage is a logical argument about the unchanging nature of the essential meaning of prophethood across different prophets. The author begins by stating that the meaning that necessitates prophethood is the same for all prophets. Therefore, if opponents accept the prophethood of earlier prophets based on miracles, they must accept Muhammad’s prophethood because the underlying meaning that makes a miracle a proof of prophethood is identical, even if the miracles themselves differ in form. He then anticipates an objection: opponents might claim that the verses (miracles) of earlier prophets have outward signs that are not found in Muhammad’s miracle. The author replies that if they look at the outward aspects, they will find no one who surpasses Muhammad in miracle and elevation. (3) Confront them with the distinction (between outward and inward meanings) that they themselves do not accept in their own claims. (4) The author only accepts those who acknowledge the prophethood of his own prophet; if the prophet they claim is Muhammad, then his prophethood is established; if not, they must provide evidence for their claimed prophet. The passage ends with a call for God’s assistance.

Key Terms
برهان (proof)
علة (cause/reason)
فرق (distinction)
دلالة (evidence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Muslims and opponents share the same criteria for prophethood, so there is no specific proof for Muhammad.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that even if the criteria were shared, the opponents lack consistent evidence for their own position, and their denial of Muhammad is baseless.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the fourth response?
A) To question the timing of the objection.
B) To demand proof from the opponents.
C) To create a dilemma: if the opponent's prophet is Muhammad, his prophethood is proven; if not, they must provide evidence.
D) To accuse the opponents of inconsistency.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's four responses effectively turn the objection back on the opponents, showing that they lack a consistent and rational basis for denying Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you share your faith, do you rely more on emotional stories or logical arguments? Which of the four responses challenges you most to strengthen your own reasoning? What step will you take this week to improve?
?
Al-Maturidi's responses require you to ask the opponent for their proof. When was the last time you honestly examined your own beliefs and asked yourself for proof? Are you as rigorous with yourself as you expect others to be?

The Mu'tazilite Doctrine of al-Aslah
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazilite argument that God must do the best for creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that God must always do what is best for His creatures, and the reasoning they used to impose this obligation on God.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites wrongly measure God's actions by human standards of benefit.

This passage presents the reasoning of those who claim that God must always do what is best for others. They argue that if God acted without benefit, He would not be wise. By understanding their logic, we can see how they mistakenly restrict divine freedom.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the Mu'tazilite argument unfold as presented.
2
Identify the two causes of deviation
The passage begins by noting that people deviate from tawhid in two ways: ignorance of the obligatory, or inability to refute dualists and atheists. This sets the stage.
This framing suggests the Mu'tazilites see themselves as defenders of tawhid.
3
Follow the core argument
Trace the reasoning: actions for no benefit are not wise; therefore God cannot do harm. Hence, they impose on God that every action must be the best (al-aslah) for others.
The argument relies on an analogy to human wise agents.
4
Understand the analogy to human actions
The Mu'tazilites compare God to wise humans who act for benefit or to repel harm. They claim just as lying or injustice cannot proceed from God, so His actions are measured by the same standard.
This is the key point of contention for Maturidi.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
They conclude that God's action must be wisdom, meaning it must always serve a beneficial purpose for others. This sets up the refutation in later lessons.
Note the word 'wisdom' here is defined by human standards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أفعال الله عن أن زعم قوم من أهل التوحيد أن أكثر منتحليه خرج منه من وجهين : إمــا جهلا بواجبه ، وإما عجزا عن تلخيص القول فيه من مذهب الثنوية وسائر الملحدين . فزعم قوم أنه إذ كان كل مما يعقل لغير نفع [فعله يقع ] فليس بحكيم ، ومن فعل فعلا لغير علة فهو عابث ، فظنوا أن لا يجوز لله أن يبتدأ فعل ضرر بأحد ، وأن ذلك يزيل الحكمة عنه ، فألزموه في كل فعل يفعله الأصلح لغيره فى الدين والأحسن لغيره في العاقبة ؛ إذ هو متعال عن قول ينفعه أو يضره شيء ، فلم يروا له الفعل إلا بما ينفع غيره ، أو يدفع به الضرر عن غيره ، فيكون ذلك أيضا علة فعله ، على ما كان علة فعل كل حكيم منا ، ما تأمل من نفع عاجل أو آجل أو دفع [ ضرر ] لزم به ، فيجر بذلك حسن الثناء جزيل الثواب . وضربوا لتقدير فعله بفعل غيره مثلا بما لا يجوز أن يكون منه الكذب أو الجور ، أو يكون منه الحركة [من] غير زوال ، أو السكون [من] غير قرار ، فثبت أن تقدير فعله على فعل الحكماء فى الشاهد لازم ، إلا أنهم دفعوا عنه الارتفاع بالفعل، والانحطاط بترك فعل ما ، فأوجبوا بذلك أنه بفعله لا يجر إلى نفسه النفع ولا يدفع عنها الضرر ، فيجب أن يكون فعله الحكمة
Question: The actions of God. Concerning that some people among the people of tawhid claimed that most of its adherents deviated from it in two ways: either through ignorance of what is obligatory, or through inability to summarize the statement about it from the doctrine of the dualists and the rest of the atheists. So some people claimed that since everything that is rationally considered for other than benefit [if its action occurs] is not wise, and whoever does an action for no reason is a frivolous one, so they thought that it is not permissible for God to initiate an act of harm to anyone, and that that removes wisdom from Him. So they imposed upon Him in every action He does that it must be the best (al-aslah) for others in religion and the most excellent for others in the outcome; since He is exalted above what benefits Him or harms Him. So they did not see action for Him except in what benefits others, or by which He repels harm from others, and that too becomes the cause of His action, like the cause of every wise person among us, who considers immediate or delayed benefit or repelling harm that necessitates it, thus obtaining good praise and abundant reward. And they gave for measuring His action by the action of others an example: that it is not permissible that from Him should occur lying or injustice, or that from Him should occur movement without transition, or stillness without rest. So they established that measuring His action upon the action of the wise in the witnessed world is necessary, except that they removed from Him exaltation by action, and degradation by omission of an action. So they necessitated thereby that He by His action does not draw benefit to Himself nor repel harm from Himself, so His action must be wisdom.
Source pages p. 814

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who impose on God the obligation to always do what is best for creatures (al-aslah). Maturidi begins by stating that some people (the Mu'tazilites) claimed that most adherents of tawhid deviated in two ways: ignorance of what is obligatory or inability to articulate the refutation of dualists and atheists. Then he presents their argument: If an action is not for benefit, it is not wise; if without cause, it is frivolous. Therefore, they think God cannot initiate harm, and so they require that every action of God must be the best for others in religion and outcome, because God is beyond benefit or harm. So they restrict God's actions to benefiting others or repelling harm, making that the cause of His action—similar to human wise persons who act for benefit. They analogize God's actions to human actions, saying just as lying or injustice cannot proceed from Him, so His actions must be measured by the actions of the wise. However, they removed from Him elevation by action and degradation by omission—meaning they deny that God can be exalted by doing any action or lowered by abstaining, thereby claiming His action is purely wisdom. Maturidi clearly disagrees, as the context of the book refutes this view. The commentary explains the Mu'tazilite position and the flaw: they improperly compare God to humans and restrict His will.

Key Terms
الأصلح
الأحسن
الحكمة
العبث
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's wisdom requires Him to always do what is most beneficial for creatures, similar to human ethical obligations.
Correction: This incorrectly limits God's absolute freedom and sovereignty, as Maturidi refutes by showing God's actions are not restricted by created standards.

Checkpoint
What is the main claim of the Mu'tazilites as presented in this passage?
A) God can do whatever He wants, including harmful actions.
B) God must always do what is best (al-aslah) for His creatures.
C) God is not wise.
D) God does nothing.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite argument imposes on God a requirement derived from human standards of benefit, which fails to recognize His absolute sovereignty and wisdom beyond human comprehension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been angry at God because a situation did not turn out 'best' by your calculation? How does this lesson expose the arrogance of that expectation?
?
In which area of your life are you still imposing your own definition of 'what is good for you' on God, refusing to trust that His wisdom is higher? What would it cost you to surrender that control?
?
If you truly believed that God's actions are always the best—even when they bring you pain—how would your response to hardship change starting today?

Praise of Allah and Creation for Trial
Maturidi praises Allah and states that humans were created for trial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi begins this section with praise and how he establishes the purpose of human creation as trial.

Core Idea
Allah created humans for trial, giving them discernment to choose right from wrong.

Maturidi opens this section by praising Allah with His unique attributes and sovereignty. He then declares the profound purpose of creation: humans were made for trial (al-miḥna). This praise sets the stage for understanding that all human actions occur within a framework of divine wisdom and testing.

Guided Path
1
Read the praise of Allah
Notice how Maturidi emphasizes Allah's uniqueness, power, and wisdom. This establishes that all creation is under His control and wisdom.
The praise is not just ritual; it grounds the theological discussion.
2
Understand the purpose of creation
Maturidi states that Allah created humans for trial. Consider what 'trial' means in this context: a test of obedience and faith.
3
Reflect on the role of wisdom
The passage mentions that humans are capable of wisdom and foolishness, and they will be questioned and rewarded or punished. This shows the moral framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في أفعال الخلق وإثباتها
الحمد لله المتوحد بالقدم والإلهية ، المتفرد بالدوام والربوبية ، ذى البرهان المنير ، والملك الكبير ، الذي فطر الخلق بقدرته ، وصرفهم بحكمته على سابق علمه ومشيئته ، وتقلب كل .... فى مواهبه وإحسانه ، أنشأ الأشياء كيف شاء ، لا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ ، ؛ لما يتمكن منهم ۲ السفه والحكمة ليزجر وا بالسؤال ثم بالجزاء عن السفه ، ويرغبوا فى الحكمة ، ونسأله أن يكرمنا بالتوفيق ، ويجدد عزمنا التسديد، وينور قلوبنا بالتوحيد ، فإنه حميد مجيد
أما بعد ، فإن الله تعالى لما خلق البشر للمحنة بما جعلهم أهل تمييز وعلم بالمحمود من الأمور والمذموم ، وجعل ما يذم منها قبيحا في عقولهم ، وما يحمد حسنا ، وعظم في أذهانهم إيثار القبيح على الحسن والرغبة فيما يذم على ما يحمد ، دعاهم على ما عليه رُكبوا وما به أكرموا إلى إيثار أمر على أمرٍ ، وقبح في عقولهم احتمال أمثالهم ، جعل الله جميع ما لهم فيه متقلب بين ضرر يتقى ونفع يرغب فيه ؛ ليكون ذلك لهم علما للموعود مما به الترغيب والترهيب ، وأنشأهم على طبائع تنفر عن أشياء وتميل إلى أشياء ، وأراهم فى تقويم حسن بعض. [مما] تنفر عنه الطباع بحمد العواقب ، الطباع بحمد العواقب ، وقبح بعض ما تميل إليه بذم العواقب ، فصيرهم بحيث يحتملون المكروه على الطباع بلذيذ العاقبة ، ويقهرونه عما يدعوهم إليه بشهي النهاية
Issue concerning acts of creation and their affirmation. Praise be to Allah, the Unique in pre-eternity and divinity, the Sole in perpetuity and lordship, possessor of the clear proof and the great kingdom, who created creatures by His power and directed them by His wisdom according to His prior knowledge and will, and the fluctuation of everything in His gifts and beneficence. He brought things into existence as He willed; He is not asked about what He does, but they are asked. Because both foolishness and wisdom are possible among them, so that they may be deterred by questioning and then by punishment from foolishness, and desire wisdom. And we ask Him to honor us with success, renew our resolve for right guidance, and illuminate our hearts with tawḥīd, for He is Praiseworthy, Glorious. To proceed: Verily Allah, when He created humans for trial, made them people of discernment and knowledge of what is praiseworthy and blameworthy among matters. And He made what is blameworthy ugly in their minds and what is praiseworthy beautiful, and He magnified in their minds the preference of the ugly over the beautiful and the desire for what is blameworthy over what is praiseworthy. He called them, upon what they were constituted and honored with, to prefer one matter over another, and He made it ugly in their minds to endure likes of themselves. Allah made all that they have of fluctuation between harm to be avoided and benefit to be desired, so that this might be for them knowledge of the promised reward and warning. And He created them with natures that recoil from some things and incline to others, and He showed them in evaluating the goodness of some [things] from which natures recoil for the praise of outcomes, and the ugliness of some things to which they incline for the blame of outcomes. Thus He made them such that they endure disliked things contrary to their natures for the sake of a pleasant outcome, and they overcome their natures regarding what calls them to it with the desire of the end.
Source pages p. 820

Commentary
This passage begins a new section titled 'Issue on acts of creation and their affirmation.' Maturidi first praises God with attributes of uniqueness, power, and wisdom. He then states the purpose: God created humans for trial, giving them discernment between good and bad. He made the bad appear ugly in their minds and the good beautiful, but also emphasized in their minds the preference for the ugly over the good. He called them to prefer one thing over another, and made it ugly to endure their equals. God then made all their affairs fluctuate between harm to avoid and benefit to desire, so that this would teach them about promised reward and punishment. He created them with natures that recoil from some things and incline to others. He showed them that some things that natures recoil from are actually good in outcome, and some things they incline to are bad in outcome. Thus He made them able to endure hardship for a pleasant outcome, overcoming their natural inclinations for the sake of a desirable end.

Key Terms
المحنة
التمييز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Allah create humans according to this passage?
A) For amusement
B) For trial
C) For worship only
D) For no reason

Key Takeaway
Allah created humans for a purposeful trial, with the capacity for wisdom and foolishness, holding them accountable.

?

?
The passage says Allah is not asked about what He does, but you are asked. Does that truth comfort you or unsettle you? Why? How will you respond to being held accountable for your choices today?
?
You have the capacity for both foolishness and wisdom. Which one have you been nurturing? What is one foolish habit you will abandon today because you know you will be asked?
