The Mechanism of Human Trial
Maturidi explains the psychological and moral mechanism of the divine trial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah tests humans by making good and bad appear in their minds, creating inclinations, and linking outcomes to choices.

Core Idea
Allah uses discernment, inclinations, and outcomes to test human choices.

After establishing that creation is for trial, Maturidi explains the mechanism: Allah gives humans discernment, makes blameworthy acts appear ugly and praiseworthy acts beautiful, yet also emphasizes in their minds a preference for the ugly. He then creates natures that recoil from some things and incline to others, and shows that outcomes can reverse initial judgments.

Guided Path
1
Understand discernment (tamyīz)
Allah made humans people of discernment, able to distinguish between praiseworthy and blameworthy matters.
2
See the inversion of values
Allah made what is blameworthy appear ugly in minds, yet He magnified the preference for the ugly over the beautiful. This is the test: humans must overcome this inclination.
This explains why humans often choose what is wrong.
3
Recognize the role of outcomes
Allah created fluctuation between harm and benefit, and showed that some things natures avoid are good in outcome, and some things they desire are bad. This teaches humans to judge by consequences.
4
Conclusion: humans can endure hardship
Because of this, humans can endure disliked things for a pleasant outcome, overcoming their natural inclinations.

Proof from Uniqueness of Creation and Divine Power
Maturidi argues creation belongs only to God, refuting creatorship in servants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's two logical arguments that creation belongs exclusively to God, refuting any creatorship in servants.

Core Idea
Creation belongs only to God; human actions are under divine power.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents two arguments to uphold the uniqueness of creation. First, he appeals to common consensus and shows that attributing the occurrence of actions to servants would imply another creator. Then, he argues that human actions are essentially movements and stillness, and since God is omnipotent over them, He grants humans power, thus actions remain under God's control. This lesson walks through these arguments to reinforce tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow of the two arguments.
The passage starts with 'وأيضا' which indicates an additional argument.
2
Identify the first argument
Look for the part that mentions the common saying (al-muta'arif) and the hypothetical scenario of making actions emerge from non-existence. Understand why that would imply another creator.
The key phrase is 'لزوم القول بخالق سواه'.
3
Identify the second argument
Find where Maturidi discusses actions as movements and stillness, and how God's power over them implies He gives servants power. See how this keeps actions under God's control.
The phrase 'صارت هي لأنفسها تحت قدرته عليها' is crucial.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how both arguments together prevent attributing any creative power to creatures, preserving God's exclusive right as Creator and Lord.
This connects to the core idea of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا القول بالمتعارف فى الخلق أن لا خالق غير الله ولا رب سواه ، ولو جعلنا حدث الأفعال وخروجها من العدم إلى الوجود ثم فناءها بعد الوجود ثم خروجها على تقدير من أربابها لجعلنا لها وصف الخلق الذى به صار الخلق خلقا، وفى ذلك لزوم القول بخالق سواه، وفى جوازه مناقضة قول من ذكرت. مع ما لو جاز ذلك الجاز القول برب فعله وذلك مدفوع، وبالله التوفيق وأيضا إن العباد إذ أفعالهم في الحقيقة حركات وسكون في الظاهر، والله قادر عليها، لولا [ذلك] ما أقدرهم عليها، فصارت هي لأنفسها تحت قدرته عليها
And also the common saying among creatures is that there is no creator other than God and no lord besides Him. If we were to make the occurrence of actions and their emergence from non-existence to existence, then their perishing after existence, then their emergence upon the estimation of their owners, we would attribute to them the description of creation by which creation becomes creation, and in that is the necessity of affirming a creator other than Him, and its permissibility contradicts the statement of those mentioned. Moreover, if that were permissible, then it would be permissible to affirm a lord for His action, and that is rejected. And success is from God. And also the servants, since their actions are in reality movements and stillness in appearance, and God is capable over them – if not for that, He would not have given them power over them – so they become, in themselves, under His power over them.
Source pages p. 829

Commentary
This final passage contains two interconnected arguments. First, Maturidi invokes the common consensus (al-muta'arif) that there is no creator but God. If we were to consider that servants produce the coming-to-be (huduth) of actions—their emergence from non-existence, their passing away, and their coming about according to the servant's estimation—then we would be attributing the very quality of creation (khalq) to the servant, implying another creator. This contradicts tawhid. Second, he argues that since actions are essentially movements and stillness, and God is omnipotent over them, He gives the servant power over them. Thus, the actions remain under God's ultimate control.

Key Terms
خالق
رب
خلق
قدرة
حركة
سكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that human power to act implies independent creation.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that creation is exclusive to God, and human power is derived from and subordinate to God's power.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence of attributing the occurrence of actions to the servant's own estimation?
A) It would confirm human responsibility
B) It would imply a creator other than God
C) It would deny God's knowledge
D) It would affirm free will

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's arguments establish that creation and ultimate control belong solely to God, and human actions are subordinate to divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your every action—every movement and stillness—is under God's power, what does that mean for your sense of control over your life? Are you living as if your actions are independent, or are you sincerely relying on God in every moment? What specific habit can you change today to acknowledge that all power belongs to Him?
?
The common consensus Maturidi invokes is that there is no creator but God. Yet do you truly live as though your achievements, your work, your deeds are created by God alone? Where in your heart do you still attribute 'creation' to yourself—your talents, your successes? What would it look like to completely surrender that false sense of independence?
?
Maturidi argues that if humans were considered creators of their actions, it would imply a lord other than God. Have you ever felt that you are the 'lord' of your own actions—deciding their outcome without divine involvement? How does this lesson challenge that feeling? What is one decision you can make today that consciously places the outcome entirely in God's hands?

The Proof of Temporality and Actions by Other Than God
Maturidi argues that attributing actions to other than God invalidates the proof of the world's temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that if actions can be attributed to other than God, the proof of the world's temporal origination collapses.

Core Idea
All actions must ultimately be from God for the proof of creation to hold.

Maturidi here presents a critical argument in defense of tawhid. He shows that the standard proof for the world's createdness — the inability of bodies to initiate their own attributes — would be undermined if those attributes could come from anyone other than God. This passage reinforces the central Islamic doctrine that all effective agency belongs to Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Get a sense of Maturidi's argument flow.
Notice the conditional chain: if actions from other than God, then proof collapses.
2
Identify the key proof
Identify what Maturidi says is the basis for recognizing temporal origination: the inability of bodies to exit from attributes like movement and stillness.
This is the standard kalam proof for the creation of the world.
3
Understand the implication
Reflect on why attributing these attributes to others than God would invalidate the proof. It would mean the proof is established by that other, not by Allah.
This leads to the failure to prove tawhid and lordship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن الذى به عرف أهل التوحيد حدث الأعيان امتناعها عن الخروج من التفريق والاجتماع والتحرك والسكون ، فإذا لم يكن هذه الأحوال في الحقيقة الله على يدى من جرت عليه يديه لم نقدر أن نثبت جسم وعين يدرك خلقا من على ما هو عليه بفعل الله ; إذ الأفعال التي ذكرنا من الأسماء يجوز تحقيقها لا بالله ، وإن كنا نبصر من به ذلك ، فيصير دليل حدث العالم يقيمه غير الله ; إذ لا سبيل له إلى إظهار الذى منه من الأحوال التي ذكرنا مما ليست منه ، ولولا تلك الأحوال لم يعرف حدث العالم فيبطل طريق العلم به بدليل أقامه هو ، ثم لما احتمل جميع الأحوال بغيره لم يثبت بها أنه صانع تلك ، والأجسام لا تعاين إلا بها ، فيبطل أن يكون الله تعال جعل لوحدانيته دليلا يعرف ، ولربوبيته العالم شاهدا يشهد على هذا القول ، وبالله العصمة والنجاة
And also, that by which the people of tawhid recognize the temporal origination of bodies is their inability to exit from separation and combination, movement and stillness. So if these states are not in reality from Allah upon the hands of those upon whom His hands proceed, we cannot establish a body and an object that perceives creation as it is by the act of Allah; because the acts that we mentioned from the names can be actualized without Allah, even if we see the one who has that. Then the proof of the temporal origination of the world would be established by other than Allah; because he has no way to manifest that from which he is from among the states that we mentioned, which are not from him. And were it not for those states, the temporal origination of the world would not be known, so the path to knowledge of it would be invalidated by a proof that he himself establishes. Then, since he can assume all states from other than Him, it is not established by them that He is the maker of those states, and bodies are only perceived by them. Thus it becomes invalid that Allah Most High made for His oneness a proof by which He is known, and for His lordship a witness that testifies to this saying. And success and deliverance are from Allah.
Source pages p. 830

Commentary
This passage is a proof that if actions could be attributed to other than God, then the proof of the world's creation would be compromised. Maturidi argues that the recognized proof of temporal origination is the inability of bodies to initiate attributes like movement and stillness. If those attributes can be produced by other than God, then the proof would be established by that other, not by God. This would lead to the invalidation of the proof for divine oneness and lordship. So the argument defends the necessity of attributing all actions ultimately to God.

Key Terms
حدث الأعيان
التفريق والاجتماع
التحرك والسكون
دليل التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage denies that humans have any choice or action.
Correction: Maturidi does not deny human choice; he denies that actions can be independently produced without God's role as the ultimate creator. Humans acquire actions, but God is the creator of the action itself.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what do the people of tawhid use to recognize the temporal origination of bodies?
A) Their own reasoning
B) The inability of bodies to exit from separation/combination and movement/stillness
C) The Quran
D) The consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
If actions could be attributed to other than God, the proof of the world's temporal origination would be invalidated, along with the evidence for God's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Quranic Proof for Divine Oneness: Surah Al-Mu'minun 23:91
Maturidi cites Quran 23:91 to argue against multiple gods, then discusses proofs on accidents and unseen creations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quran 23:91 to argue that multiple gods would lead to conflict and how he extends this to show that every accident has a proof of its Creator.

Core Idea
If there were multiple gods, each would take his creation—leading to conflict.

This lesson takes us into Imam Maturidi's use of direct Quranic evidence against polytheism. The verse from Surah Al-Mu'minun presents a simple yet powerful argument: if there were multiple gods, each would claim his own creation, resulting in domination and disorder. Maturidi then expands this reasoning to discuss how every created thing bears a mark of its Maker. Let's examine the passage closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Start by reading the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if there were with Him any god, then each god would have taken what he created.' This sets up a scenario where multiple gods would inevitably conflict.
2
Understand the proof on accidents
Maturidi asserts that Allah places a proof on every accident (creation) by which it is known that He created it. This is a key extension of the verse's logic: if every accident has a clear sign of its Creator, then attributing creation to multiple gods is incoherent.
Accidents are fleeting attributes that in themselves point to a creator.
3
Consider unseen creations
Maturidi discusses that there may be creations we do not see that can gather, separate, move, and be still, yet we recognize their acts through changes in substance. This shows that even unseen things bear the mark of their Creator.
This counters the argument that if we don't see something, it might not have a creator.
4
Note the sectarian critique
Maturidi concludes by pointing out that both the Mu'tazilites and the Mulhida (heretics) are partners in error regarding this issue. They fail to acknowledge the clear proofs of divine oneness in creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال : " مَا اتَّخَذَ اللَّهُ مِنْ وَلَدٍ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهِ ثم قال : " إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِله بِمَا خَلَقَ " ثم الله جل ثناؤه لم يخلق عرضا قط إلا جعل عليه دليلا يعلم أنه خلق ; لما كانت الأعراض لما ذكرنا ، ويجوز أن يكون في خلقه خلق يجمع ويفرق ويحرك ويسكن ونحن لا نراه ، كما كان فيهم من لا نراه بجوهره وإن كان يرى ، وتلك الأفعال لأنفسها لا ترى ، إنما ترى وتعلم بتغير الأحوال على الجوهر ، فإذا كانت جواهر لا ترى جائز منها مثلها لم يجعل لما خلق علما ولا ذهب به فكيف ناقض به قول المعتزلة قول الملحدة وهم شركاؤهم فى هذا الوجه ، فنسأل الله النجاة من قول هذا عقباه
And also, Allah Most High said: 'Allah has not taken any son, nor was there with Him any god.' Then He said: 'Then each god would have taken what he created.' Then Allah, may His praise be exalted, did not create any accident ever except that He placed upon it a proof by which it is known that He created it; because accidents are as we mentioned. And it is possible that in His creation there is a creation that gathers, separates, moves, and stays still while we do not see it, just as there were among them those whom we do not see in his substance even though he is seen. And those acts in themselves are not seen; they are only seen and known by the change of states upon the substance. So if there are substances that are not seen, it is possible from them similar to them. He did not make for what He created a knowledge nor did He do away with it. So how could the statement of the Mu'tazilites contradict the statement of the Mulhida, for they are partners in this aspect. So we ask Allah for deliverance from the evil consequence of this saying.
Source pages p. 830

Commentary
This passage uses Quranic evidence (23:91) to argue against polytheism. The verse implies that if there were multiple gods, each would take his creation and they would dominate each other. Maturidi then discusses that God places a proof on every accident to show He created it. He also addresses the possibility of unseen creations that can act, but those acts are known by changes. He concludes by noting that the Mu'tazilites and Mulhida are partners in error regarding this.

الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is merely quoting the verse without deeper reasoning.
Correction: Maturidi actively uses the verse to build an argument about proofs on accidents and unseen creations, refuting those who claim independent agents.

Checkpoint

B) If there were multiple gods, each would take his creation and conflict
C) Accidents have no proofs

Key Takeaway
The Quranic argument from Surah Al-Mu'minun is that multiple gods would inevitably conflict over creation, and this logic extends to seeing proofs of God in every created thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Mu'tazilites were condemned for denying that Allah creates all actions. Where in your life do you subtly assume you are the independent creator of your choices? How can you surrender this false sense of autonomy and live in constant acknowledgment of Allah's exclusive creativity?

The Argument from Composition for Divine Oneness
Maturidi refutes the idea that some actions are from creatures, preserving tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the composition of the world to prove that all actions must be created by Allah alone, preserving tawhid.

Core Idea
If creatures could create actions, the world would have multiple creators.

Maturidi presents a concise argument rooted in the observable composition of the world. Everything we see consists of bodies and accidents. If any accident—including human actions—could be truly created by someone other than Allah, then the world would be a product of multiple originators. This would directly contradict the fundamental Islamic belief in the oneness of the Creator. Let's examine this logical proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its full translation. Let the author's words sink in before analyzing.
Notice the logical structure: premise, conditional, conclusion.
2
Identify the key components
Break down the argument: What is the world composed of? What would happen if accidents could be acts of creatures? What is the final consequence?
The argument hinges on the concepts of 'accidents' (أعراض) and 'bodies' (أجسام).
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the theological implication: If tawhid is true, then no accident can be the act of a creature. This is a strong assertion about divine sovereignty.
This connects to debates on human free will and divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن العالم لا يخلو من الأعراض والأجسام ، وكل أنواع الأعراض أمكن في الحقيقة أن تكون فعلا لغيره فيكون العالم لله ولخلقه من طريق الإنشاء والوجود ، وفى ذلك بطلان القول بوحدانية صانع العالم .
And also, the world is not free of accidents and bodies, and all kinds of accidents possibly in reality being an act of another, then the world would belong to Allah and to His creation in terms of origination and existence, and in that is the nullification of the statement of the oneness of the Maker of the world.
Source pages p. 832

Commentary
This is a concise argument from the composition of the world. The world consists of bodies and accidents. If accidents (like actions) could truly be the act of someone other than Allah, then the world would be a composite of acts from Allah and from creatures. This would entail that the world has multiple originators, thereby nullifying the oneness of the Creator (tawhid). Since all Muslims affirm that the Maker of the world is one, it follows that all accidents—including human actions—must be created by Allah alone.

Key Terms
عرض ('arad)
جسم (jism)
وحدانية (wahdaniyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans can independently create their own actions.
Correction: If humans could truly create any accident, the world would have multiple originators, which contradicts tawhid. All accidents, including actions, are created by Allah.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say would happen if accidents could be acts of creatures?
A) The world would still be one
B) The oneness of the Creator would be nullified
C) Nothing would change
D) Accidents would cease to exist

Key Takeaway
If any accident could be created by a creature, the world would have multiple creators, which nullifies tawhid — thus all events must be from Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that the action itself (the movement, the will, the intention) is created by Allah? If so, how does that reshape your understanding of your own responsibility and your need for His mercy? Are you willing to say, 'Allah created my sin, but I am accountable' without falling into despair or presumption?
?
Think of a recent success you attribute to your own effort. Can you identify the exact moment you realized that effort, skill, or decision was an accident created by Allah? If not, what would change in your heart if you began each day acknowledging that every breath, thought, and action is His creation? Will you practice this awareness tomorrow?
?
If all events are from Allah alone, then what is your role? Does this make you passive or more active? How does knowing that your very choice to act is created by Allah humble you and increase your reliance on Him? Write down one specific way you will depend on Allah for a future action.

Proof that God is Creator of All Things
Maturidi argues that if God's power is established, then all existing things are created by Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that God is the sole creator of all things, based on the impossibility of giving what one lacks and the necessary dependence of the world on God.

Core Idea
God's sole creativity follows from His power and the world's dependence.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a logical proof that establishes God as the creator of everything. He begins with a general principle about power and knowledge, then applies it to God, and finally argues from the composition of the world to the necessity of a single creator. This lesson unpacks each step of his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice how Maturidi uses analogies and logical deductions.
The first sentence may be garbled in OCR; focus on the meaning.
2
Understand the principle of inability to give what one lacks
Maturidi states that no one can enable another to do what they themselves cannot do, nor can they give knowledge they don't have. This is a logical axiom.
This sets the foundation for the argument.
3
Apply the principle to God's power
If God has power over something, then that thing cannot exist without God's power, because God cannot delegate power He doesn't have. Thus, God must be the creator.
This step directly links the axiom to God's role as creator.
4
Examine the argument from the world's composition
The world consists of accidents and bodies. Accidents could be acts of creatures, implying multiple creators. But this contradicts the oneness of the maker. Therefore, all must be from one creator.
This is a second independent argument supporting the same conclusion.
5
Conclusion: oneness of the creator
Both arguments converge: God's power and the world's unity require that God is the sole creator of all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يجز لأحد القدرة على إقدار غيره على شيء لم يقدر هو عليه، ومن علم يعلم به غيره لم يجز أن لا يعلم هو، فمثله الذي بينا، وإذا ثبتت قدرة الله عليه، وما يقدر الله عليه فهو محال وجوده بغيره ثبت أنه خالق ذلك وأيضا إن العالم لا يخلو من الأعراض والأجسام، وكل أنواع الأعراض أمكن في الحقيقة أن تكون فعلا لغيره فيكون العالم لله ولخلقه من طريق الإنشاء والوجود، وفى ذلك بطلان القول بوحدانية صانع العالم.
It is not permissible for anyone to have the power to enable another to do something that he himself does not have power over, and whoever has knowledge by which another knows, it is not permissible that he himself does not know. So the example is as we have stated. And when it is established that God has power over something, and what God has power over, its existence without Him is impossible, then it is established that He is its creator. Also, the world is not free from accidents and bodies, and all types of accidents are possible in reality to be an act of another, so the world would belong to God and to His creation in terms of origination and existence. And in that is the invalidation of the statement of the oneness of the Maker of the world.
Source pages p. 832

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is the sole creator of all things. Maturidi begins by establishing a principle: it is impossible for one to enable another to do something that he himself cannot do, and likewise one cannot cause another to know something that he himself does not know. This principle is then applied to God: if God's power is established over something, then that thing cannot exist without God, so God must be its creator. Then he argues that the world consists of accidents and bodies, and every type of accident could, in principle, be an act of another (i.e., a creature). If so, then the world would be partly from God and partly from creatures, which would negate the oneness of the creator. Since the world is one, the creator must be one and all things are from Him.

Key Terms
قدرة
إقدار
خالق
أعراض
أجسام
وحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi's argument denies human action and free will.
Correction: The argument does not deny human action; it states that all existence ultimately depends on God's power and that creatures cannot create independently.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, if something is possible for God to have power over, what is its relationship to God?
A) It exists independently of God.
B) Its existence without God is impossible, so God is its creator.
C) It can be created by someone else.
D) It proves multiple creators.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi rationally demonstrates that God is the sole creator because nothing can exist without His power, and the world's unity requires a single maker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that nothing exists without God's power, how would it change the way you view your own achievements and failures? Are you willing to attribute every success and every trial to Him alone, not to your own ability or others' actions? What would you need to let go of today to live that out?
?
The passage argues that the unity of the world demands a single Creator. Reflect: in your own life, where do you sense disunity or conflict that might stem from attributing power to multiple sources (e.g., your own strength, other people, circumstances) instead of one God? Can you commit to seeing every situation as coming from His sole hand?
?
Maturidi uses the principle that no one can give what they do not have. How does this apply to your own attempts to help others? Are you relying on your own limited resources or acknowledging that all goodness comes from God? What would it look like to depend entirely on His power in your interactions today?

Consensus and Quranic Refutation of Multiple Creators
Maturidi invokes Muslim consensus and Quranic verse to refute polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Muslim consensus and the Quranic verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay' to logically refute the idea of multiple creators.

Core Idea
Muslim consensus and a single Quranic verse dismantle the claim of multiple creators.

In this passage, Maturidi presents a concise yet powerful argument: the unanimous agreement of the Muslim community (ijma) together with the Quranic statement that nothing is like Allah, suffices to refute anyone claiming partners in creation. He shows that the very existence of the world points to the oneness of the Creator, and any attempt to introduce partners collapses under its own logic. Let's explore his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the flow of the argument settle before interpreting.
Notice that Maturidi begins with a strong statement of consensus.
2
Identify the two proofs
Maturidi uses two main supports: the consensus of the Muslims (ijma') and the Quranic verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay'' (42:11) along with 'Ilahu kulli shay' (73:9). Mark where each appears.
3
Trace the logical refutation
Maturidi argues that if the world had partners, God would not be uniquely deserving of being its God. Follow the logic: consensus → verse → conclusion of oneness.
This connects the objective of understanding the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يختلف أهل الإسلام في إطلاق القول بأن صانع العالم واحد، وقول من يبطل قوله عند التحصيل هذه الجملة التي شارك فيها الجميع مردود بالجملة على نحو قول الله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ، وقوله: إله كل شيء. إن قول الناس في التحصيل يجعل له شبها وعدلا في العباد منقوض بتلك الجملة، وإن احتال فمثله الأول، بل الأول أحق؛ لأنه طريق العلم بالحرف الثاني وهو أن في تحقيق العالم تحقيق الوحدانية للخالق، وبه يسلم له القول لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ، وأنه الواحد لا شريك له، فإذ أثبت العالم بشركاء له فيه لم يكن هو أحق بأن أن يكون لمثله أشياء، أو أن يكون إلها لما أنشأه وأخرجه من ليس كمثله شيء من العدم إلى الوجود من غيره في ذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And the people of Islam did not differ in affirming the statement that the Maker of the world is one. And the statement of those who invalidate their own statement upon investigation—this general statement in which all participated—is refuted by that general statement, in the manner of the saying of God Most High: 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11), and His saying: 'God of everything' (73:9). Indeed, the statement of people upon investigation makes for Him a likeness and an equal in the servants, and is refuted by that general statement. And if one resorts to a trick, then his case is like the first, but the first is more fitting because it is the path of knowledge of the second matter, which is that in the verification of the world there is a verification of the oneness of the Creator, and by it the statement 'There is nothing like unto Him' is secured, and that He is the One, no partner for Him. So if one establishes that the world has partners in it, then He is not more deserving that for His likeness there be things, or that He be a god for what He originated and brought out from non-existence to existence, while there is nothing like unto Him, from another in that. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 832

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim multiple creators. Maturidi begins by stating the unanimous consensus of the Muslims that the Maker of the world is one. He then argues that those who deny this are refuted by the Quranic verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay'' (There is nothing like Him) and 'Ilahu kulli shay' (God of everything). If one claims that God has a likeness or equal in creation, that is refuted by this universal statement. If one tries to use a trick to avoid this, his argument is like the first refuted one, but the first refutation is more appropriate because it is the way to knowledge of the second point: that verifying the existence of the world leads to verifying the oneness of the Creator. By this, the verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay'' is upheld. If one attributes partners to the world, then God is no longer uniquely deserving of being the god of what He originated, since another also originates. This would contradict His uniqueness. Maturidi concludes with 'La quwwata illa billah' (there is no power except with God).

Key Terms
أهل الإسلام
صانع العالم
لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ
إله كل شيء
شريك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay' is just a statement of God's uniqueness, not a logical argument.
Correction: Maturidi uses it as a premise in a logical deduction: if God is unlike anything, then He cannot have partners in creation, and the world's existence confirms His oneness.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say is the result of establishing that the world has partners in creation?
A) God is still the only god.
B) God would not be uniquely deserving of being the god of His creation.
C) The world would be self-sufficient.
D) The consensus of Muslims would be broken.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that Muslim consensus and the Quranic principle that nothing resembles Allah logically refute any claim of partners in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson proves that any claim of multiple creators is logically incoherent. Do you ever live as though something other than Allah has ultimate control over your life—like your job, health, or status? What would it mean for you to truly internalize that only Allah is the Creator and Sustainer?
?
The consensus of all Muslims affirms that the Maker is one. Yet, how often do you catch yourself attributing the outcomes of your actions to your own power or the power of others? Consider a recent success or failure—did you acknowledge Allah as the sole originator of that situation? What needs to change in your thoughts or speech to align with this lesson?
?
Maturidi uses the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' to negate any partner in creation. Is there any created thing that you have elevated in your heart to a level of fear, love, or trust that is due only to Allah? Be honest: what might that be, and what step will you take today to remove it from its false station?

If God Were Not Creator of All Actions, His Proofs Would Be Deficient
Maturidi argues that if God did not create all actions, His proofs and management would require help from creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that God must be the creator of all actions, and the implications for God's wisdom and power.

Core Idea
God's proofs cannot depend on creatures; He must create all actions.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a powerful argument for God's exclusive creative power. He shows that if God were not the creator of all actions, His prophetic miracles and world management would be flawed, requiring help from creatures. This would contradict God's attributes of wisdom and power. Maturidi's argument thus reinforces that everything that happens is created by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the main argument. Note the conditional structure.
The passage uses a 'if...then' logical form.
2
Identify the conditional premise
Find the 'if' clause: 'if He were not the creator of the actions of creatures generally'. Consider what follows.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Maturidi says that the alternative would make God's proofs defective and corrupted, and He would need help from creatures. Think about why that is impossible for God.
The example of subsistence and offspring illustrates the dependence.
4
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that all actions appear through God's creation, by His will. Notice how the argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أنه لو لم يكن خالقا لأفعال الخلق عامة [لما قدر على إظهار] من حجته التي أظهرها على أيدي رسله والتدبير الذي جرى عليه من أمر عالمة ما أنشأه خلقه إلى آخر ما ينتهي إليه أمره منتقصا فاسدا لولا مساعدة خلقه له، فيما شبر من البقاء وفيها جعل من العدم فيها أنشأ من النسل، إن ذلك كله مما ظهر بأفعال خلقه وتم به، وليس بحكيم ولا قادر من أراد أن يظهر حجة لا يقدر عليها إلا بالمعونة بعلم غيره وفعله، بل هو جاهل عاجز. فثبت أنها كلها ظهرت بما خلقها على يدي من شاء، كيف شاء، على ما شاء جل ثناؤه.
And also that if He were not the creator of the actions of creatures generally, [He would not be able to manifest] from His proof which He manifested through the hands of His messengers, and the management that proceeded from Him concerning the affair of His knowledgeable world, what His creatures originated, up to the end of what His affair reaches, defective and corrupted without the help of His creatures to Him, in what is extended of subsistence, and in it He made from non-existence that which He originated from offspring. Indeed, all of that is what appeared through the actions of His creatures and was completed by it. And he is not wise nor powerful who wants to manifest a proof that he cannot accomplish except with the help of another's knowledge and action; rather, he is ignorant and incapable. So it is established that all of them appeared by what He created through the hands of whom He willed, how He willed, as He willed, glorified be His praise.
Source pages p. 832

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God must be the creator of all actions of creatures. Maturidi presents a conditional argument: if God were not the creator of all actions, then His proofs (miracles) that He displayed through His prophets and the overall management of the world would be defective and corrupted, because they would require the help of creatures. For example, the subsistence of the world and the creation of offspring from non-existence are acts that appear through the actions of creatures. If God needed the help of creatures to manifest these proofs, He would not be truly wise (hakim) or powerful (qadir); rather, He would be ignorant (jahil) and incapable (ʿajiz). Since this is impossible for God, it is established that all actions are created by God through whomever He wills, in the manner He wills. The argument emphasizes that God's independence from creation is necessary for His divinity.

Key Terms
خالق
أفعال الخلق
حجة
تدبير
حكيم
قادر
جاهل
عاجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates all actions, humans are passive puppets with no agency.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that God creates actions through human agents ('through the hands of whom He willed'), indicating that humans are involved, but the creation is solely from God. Human agency is preserved as acquisition (kasb).

Checkpoint
What would God be called if He needed the help of creatures to manifest His proofs?
A) Wise and powerful.
B) Ignorant and incapable.
C) Merciful and forgiving.
D) Just and fair.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that God must be the creator of all actions because otherwise His proofs and management would depend on creatures, contradicting His wisdom and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever rely on your own abilities or others' help to prove something about your faith, rather than trusting that God's proofs are complete through His creation? How does this lesson challenge your dependence on created means in matters of certainty?
?
If God's proofs depended on creatures, He would be deficient. In your life, are you living as if God's power is limited by human actions? What would it mean to truly believe that every proof of God's existence and management is entirely His doing?
?
When you see the birth of a child or the maintenance of the world, do you attribute the act to the human or to God? How does this passage press you to reconsider who the true agent is behind every action, including your own choices?

Creation Points to the Unity of the Creator
Maturidi argues that the modality of creation is unknowable, distinguishes human acquisition from divine creation, and refutes multiple gods using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the modality of God's creation is unknowable and that this points to His exclusive divine status, refuting multiple creators.

Core Idea
Creation's inner workings are hidden, but the act itself proves the Creator's oneness.

Imam Maturidi opens this passage by establishing a fundamental principle: we cannot perceive how God creates. We only know creation through what is created. This principle then serves as a foundation for two key points: human action is not creation like God's (kasb), and there cannot be multiple gods because each would have their own creation, leading to division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage and find the statement that the modality of origination cannot be perceived and is only known through the originated thing.
Notice the phrase 'لا سبيل إلى معاينة كيفية الإنشاء'.
2
Understand the kasb argument
See how Maturidi applies this principle to human action: if one attributes to a human an action in the same sense as God's creation, that would be claiming a creation like God's, which is false.
This distinguishes divine creation from human acquisition.
3
Trace the proof of tawhid
Examine how the Quranic verses ('Creator of everything' and 'each god would have taken what he created') are used to argue that only God creates and that multiple creators are impossible.
The unity of creation leads to the unity of the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلق كخلقه . ثم لا سبيل إلى معاينة كيفية الإنشاء وإنما يعلم بالمنشأ، إنه في حق الكسب في حق الخروج من العدم إلى الوجود والحدث من لا أصل، أو والتحرك والسكون، فمن حقق للعبد من الفعل من الوجه الذي يحقق من الله فقد وجد خلق كخلقه؛ إذ لا وجه لفعله غير ذلك، ولو كان بالذي يذكره [دفع لكان؟] لا وجه للاحتجاج؛ لأنهم لو أثبتوا يقولون ليس ذلك كذلك؛ لأن الذي منكم كان بفلاح، وهذا النوع من الخيال، ثم اتباع ذلك الحرف ودفع إمكان حقيقته بقوله: (خَالِقُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ) ليعلم كل أنه أي شيء أضافه إلى أحد أنه خلقه لم يقدروا عليه لوجود ضرورات له فيه توجب تدبير غيره في ذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقد قال الله عز وجل: "إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلِّ إِله بِمَا خَلَق"، وإذا جعلت لكل عند المعنى الذي به وصف الله تعالى بالخلق، ويذهب كل بالذي فكان في ذلك تثبيت آلهة، ذهب كل بما خلق، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Creation like His creation. Then there is no way to perceive the modality of origination, and it is only known through the originated thing. It is in the right of acquisition (kasb) in the right of exiting from non-existence to existence and origination from no origin, or movement and stillness. So whoever realizes for the servant an action from the aspect that is realized from God has found a creation like His creation, for there is no aspect for his action other than that. And if it were by what he mentions [it would be a repulsion?], there would be no ground for argument; because if they affirmed they say it is not so, because what is from you was by [flah?], and this type is imagination. Then following that letter and repelling the possibility of its reality by His saying: 'Creator of everything' so that everyone knows that whatever he attributes to anyone that he created it, they are not able to do so due to necessities in it that require the management of other than Him in that, and there is no power except with Allah. And Allah the Exalted said: 'Then each god would have taken what he created,' and if you made for each according to the meaning by which Allah the Exalted is described with creation, and each goes with what he created, then in that is the establishment of gods. Each goes with what he created, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 848

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the modality of creation is unknowable and a refutation of multiple creators. Maturidi begins by stating that creation is like His creation, but there is no way to perceive the how of origination; we only know it through the originated thing. He then discusses acquisition (kasb) and the relation of human action to divine creation, emphasizing that if one attributes to the servant an action from the same aspect as God's action, then one has claimed a creation like God's, which is impossible. He then cites the Quranic verse (6:102) 'Creator of everything' to show that attributing creation to anyone else is futile. He further cites verse (23:91) to argue that if there were multiple gods, each would take his creation and they would separate, which is not observed. Thus the proof is complete: the impossibility of perceiving the modality of creation and the unity of the Creator as demonstrated by the Quran.

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
كسب (kasb)
كيفية (kayfiyya)
إنشاء (insha')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'how' of God's creation can be known through analogy with human creation.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that the modality of origination is unknowable; we only know creation through the created thing, not through comparison with human acts.

Checkpoint

A) Through direct perception of the act of creation
B) Only through the created thing, not the modality of origination
C) Through rational analogy with human fabrication
D) Through revelation describing the process

Key Takeaway
The modality of creation is beyond human perception, and this reinforces the oneness of the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Oneness of God from the Coherence of Action
Maturidi deduces the oneness of the Creator from the coherence of the world and the servant's action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the coherence of the world and the servant's action to argue for the oneness of the Creator.

Core Idea
The servant's action and the world's order share one source: the One Creator.

Maturidi concludes a longer argument with a crisp summary. He notes that wonder at the argument itself is misplaced because the conclusion is clear: from the consistent nature of actions, we see that the Creator is one. This lesson unpacks that final inference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice the opening remark about wonder.
2
Identify the key claims
Identify the three parts: remark about wonder, statement about resemblance and difference in choices, and the core argument linking the servant's action to the world's command.
3
Understand the conclusion
See how Maturidi concludes that the Creator is one, and that actions are attributed to the servant from a different aspect. Reflect on why this resolves the apparent conflict.
This connects to the common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العجب ممن يعجب منه، وفي ذلك أنه واحد، والتشابه والاختلاف أبدا تقع في الأخيار، وجملة ذلك أنا نجد فعل العبد من الوجه الذي عليه أمر العالم لله، فثبت أن خالق العالم كله واحد، وإنما يجعل للعبد لا من ذلك الوجه، والله الموفق
Then wonder about who wonders from it. And in that He is one. And resemblance and difference always occur in the choices (al-akhyar). And the summary of that is that we find the action of the servant from the aspect upon which the command of the world is for God. So it is established that the Creator of the whole world is one. And it is only attributed to the servant from a different aspect. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 849

Commentary
This passage is a concluding summary of a preceding argument. Maturidi comments on the wonder of those who are amazed at the argument. He states that God is one. He notes that resemblance and difference always occur in matters of choice (al-akhyar). The key point is that we find the servant's action to be from the same aspect as the command of the world, which is for God. Therefore, it is established that the Creator of the entire world is one. The attribution of actions to the servant is from a different aspect (i.e., the aspect of acquisition, not creation). This reinforces the unity of the Creator.

Key Terms
واحد (wahid)
تشابه (tashabuh)
اختلاف (ikhtilaf)
أخيار (akhyar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates all actions, humans have no role.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that actions are attributed to the servant from a different aspect (acquisition), not creation.

Checkpoint

A) That the servant is the true creator of his actions
B) That the Creator of the world is one
C) That actions are purely accidental
D) That the world has multiple creators

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the unity of the Creator is evident from the coherence of all actions, whether human or cosmic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
How does the fact that resemblance and difference in your choices are all under God's sovereignty affect the way you make decisions? Are you willing to submit your will entirely to the One Creator, even when it conflicts with your personal preferences?

The Objection about the Acquired and the True Goal
Maturidi refutes an objection about knowing the acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the objection about the acquired is a distraction, and the real purpose is to know Allah, not to analyze the acquired.

Core Idea
Knowing Allah is the goal, not analyzing the acquired.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses an objection that questions whether we can know the acquired (muktasab) separately from other things. He explains that this objection misses the point: the discussion is not about distinguishing the acquired but about establishing the knowledge of Allah. He then criticizes the Mu'tazilites for leading to doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its premise
Read the opening lines where the objector questions whether the acquired can be known apart from other things. Notice the confusion between the acquired and other entities.
The objector assumes that distinguishing the acquired is necessary for knowing Allah.
2
Identify the Sheikh's response
The Sheikh redirects the discussion: the goal is not to know the acquired in itself, but to know what belongs to Allah (tawḥīd). He warns against attributing false qualities to Allah.
This shift is crucial—theological inquiry is about Allah, not about defining creation.
3
Understand the Mu'tazilite error and the Quranic quote
Maturidi criticizes the Mu'tazilites for claiming there is no way to know Allah, leading to perpetual doubt. He cites Quran 23:91 to refute the idea of multiple gods.
The verse shows that if there were multiple gods, each would take what He created—so creation indicates the uniqueness of the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فى أنه لم ينظر إليه وأغفل عنه حيث لم ير موضع أن الحدث والقدم إنما هو الدلالة ، وما نحن فيه ليس ثمة ما يفصل إن كان فهو في غيره ، ثبت أنهما بحث أنفسهما شبيهات ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم عارض : هل يعرف به المكتسب من غيره ؟ قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وهى المعارضة أن اشتبه المكتسب لغيره حتى لا يعرف حقيقة واحد منهما ، ثبت أنهما مخلوقان معا لذلك له وبعد ، فإنه ليس على معرفة المكتسب وإنما على معرفة ما لله ، لا عرفه في خلقه ، لا نفى عنه ما هو ، ولا أثبت له ما ليس له ، فأكون كاذبا عليه ، وذلك كفر ، وعلى قول المعتزلة : لا وجه لمعرفته، فتحيل أبدا على الشك ، ولا يصل إليه ، وذلك هو المعنى الذى نفى الله أن يكون معه إله حققه أهل الاعتزال سفها بغير علم ، وذلك في قوله تعالى] : إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلٌّ إِلَهِ بِمَا خَلَقَ ، والله الموفق . فبلغ قوله إنه لا يعلم بنفس الحركة أنها مخلوقة ، فيجب هذا في كل عرض نحو الجمع والتفريق ، فيبطل أن يكون في شيء من ذلك دلالة خلقه ثم لا سبيل إلى معرفة حقيقة الأعيان بدونها ، فكأن الله لم يقم دليلا على خلقه يكون تلك بالله دون خلقه / أبدا ، وذلك قول لم يتوهمه الشيطان ، لعل أحدا [؟] أوليائه يبلغ بطاعته إياه هذا المبلغ ، نسأل الله العصمة عن ذلك . وعلى قوله : إن الشيء لا يدل على الله ، إنما يدل إذا علم سبيه [؟] إسقاطه الدلالة الأجسام يعرف بها الله سبحانه . قال : ومن عظيم ما أجمعوا [عليه] أن دليل خلق من حدثه ، فكذلك كل محدث يدفع هذا ، وسأل الدليل ، وأيد ذلك بما يجوز أن يعرفه محدثا من لا يعرف خلقا [؟] من أن الجسم
In that he did not look at it and neglected it because he did not see a place that the state of being temporally originated and being eternal are only the indication, and our situation here is nothing that distinguishes if it is then it is in something else, it is established that both are similar in themselves, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he objected: Is the acquired known from other than it? The Sheikh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: This is the objection that the acquired is confused with other than it such that the reality of neither of them is known, so it is established that both are created together for that reason. And after, it is not about knowing the acquired but rather about knowing what is for Allah, not recognizing Him in His creation, not negating from Him what He is, nor affirming for Him what He is not, for then I would be lying about Him, and that is disbelief. And according to the Mu'tazilites: there is no way to know Him, so you always fall into doubt and cannot reach Him. And that is the meaning that Allah negated that there be with Him a god – the people of I'tizal verified it foolishly without knowledge, and that is in His statement (the Exalted): 'Then each god would have taken what He created' (Quran 23:91). And Allah is the grantor of success. Then his statement reached that he does not know through the movement itself that it is created, so this applies to every accident such as combination and separation, so it invalidates that there be in any of that an indication of its creation. Then there is no path to knowing the reality of entities without them, so it is as if Allah never established a proof for His creation such that that is for Allah without His creation – ever. And that is a statement that even Satan did not imagine; perhaps one of His allies may reach this level through his obedience to Him; we ask Allah for protection from that. And on his statement: The thing does not indicate Allah; it only indicates if its way [؟] is known, its removal of indication – bodies are known by Allah the Exalted. He said: Among the great things they agreed upon is that the proof of creation is from its temporal origination, so likewise every temporally originated thing repels this, and he asked for the proof, and supported that with what may allow him to know a temporally originated thing from one who does not know a creation [؟] from the body.
Source pages p. 850

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-response followed by a proof from contingency. The objection (muʿāraḍa) questions whether the acquired (muktasab) can be known apart from other things. The Sheikh responds that if the acquired is confused with others, then both are created; but the goal is not to know the acquired but to know Allah. He criticizes the Mu'tazilites for leading to doubt. Then he extends the argument: if one denies that a movement itself indicates its createdness, then all accidents become unknowable, and God's proof collapses. He refutes this by stating the agreed principle that the proof of creation is from temporal origination (ḥudūth). The passage then affirms that bodies are known through God and the proof from temporality is sound.

Key Terms
مكتسب
عارض
معرفة
الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The goal of the discussion is to define the acquired (muktasab) in itself.
Correction: The goal is to know Allah, not to analyze the acquired. The objection is a distraction from tawḥīd.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Sheikh say is the real purpose of the discussion?
A) To know the acquired (muktasab) in itself
B) To know what is for Allah, not to prove the acquired
C) To refute the Mu'tazilites on every point
D) To prove that movements are not created

Key Takeaway
The purpose of theological discussion is to know Allah, not to get lost in peripheral definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study theology, do you ever get so absorbed in abstract technicalities that you forget the ultimate purpose is to know and worship Allah? What specific change will you make today to keep that goal central?
?
The Sheikh warns that falsely attributing something to Allah is disbelief. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that you haven't verified from revelation? How will you actively seek certainty?
?
The Mu'tazilites ended up in perpetual doubt because they claimed no path to knowing Allah. Have you ever felt that endless debates lead you to confusion rather than faith? What concrete step can you take to anchor your certainty in clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah?

Defending the Proof from Contingency
Maturidi defends the proof from contingency and its application to all accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the proof from contingency (ḥudūth) remains valid because denying its indication leads to complete ignorance of all created entities.

Core Idea
If we deny that movement indicates creation, we cannot know anything.

Maturidi continues by extending the implication of the objection: if one denies that a movement itself indicates its createdness, then all accidents become unknowable, and the very proof of God's existence collapses. He reaffirms the universal principle that temporal origination (ḥudūth) proves creation, and that this proof is established by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Understand the extension to all accidents
Read how the objection is generalized: if movement does not show its createdness, then no accident (like combination or separation) does either. Thus all accidents lose their indicative power.
This step shows the logical consequence: the objection destroys all evidence from creation.
2
See the consequence: no knowledge of entities
Without indication from accidents, we cannot know the reality of any entity (aʿyān). This would mean God never established a proof for His creation.
This is an absurd conclusion—God's wisdom requires that creation point to Him.
3
Affirm the agreed proof from temporal origination
Maturidi states that it is a great agreed-upon principle that the proof of creation comes from temporal origination (ḥudūth). Every temporally originated thing points to its Creator, and this proof is universal.
The proof from contingency does not rely on identifying each accident individually but on the general fact of temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فى أنه لم ينظر إليه وأغفل عنه حيث لم ير موضع أن الحدث والقدم إنما هو الدلالة ، وما نحن فيه ليس ثمة ما يفصل إن كان فهو في غيره ، ثبت أنهما بحث أنفسهما شبيهات ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم عارض : هل يعرف به المكتسب من غيره ؟ قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وهى المعارضة أن اشتبه المكتسب لغيره حتى لا يعرف حقيقة واحد منهما ، ثبت أنهما مخلوقان معا لذلك له وبعد ، فإنه ليس على معرفة المكتسب وإنما على معرفة ما لله ، لا عرفه في خلقه ، لا نفى عنه ما هو ، ولا أثبت له ما ليس له ، فأكون كاذبا عليه ، وذلك كفر ، وعلى قول المعتزلة : لا وجه لمعرفته، فتحيل أبدا على الشك ، ولا يصل إليه ، وذلك هو المعنى الذى نفى الله أن يكون معه إله حققه أهل الاعتزال سفها بغير علم ، وذلك في قوله تعالى] : إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلٌّ إِلَهِ بِمَا خَلَقَ ، والله الموفق . فبلغ قوله إنه لا يعلم بنفس الحركة أنها مخلوقة ، فيجب هذا في كل عرض نحو الجمع والتفريق ، فيبطل أن يكون في شيء من ذلك دلالة خلقه ثم لا سبيل إلى معرفة حقيقة الأعيان بدونها ، فكأن الله لم يقم دليلا على خلقه يكون تلك بالله دون خلقه / أبدا ، وذلك قول لم يتوهمه الشيطان ، لعل أحدا [؟] أوليائه يبلغ بطاعته إياه هذا المبلغ ، نسأل الله العصمة عن ذلك . وعلى قوله : إن الشيء لا يدل على الله ، إنما يدل إذا علم سبيه [؟] إسقاطه الدلالة الأجسام يعرف بها الله سبحانه . قال : ومن عظيم ما أجمعوا [عليه] أن دليل خلق من حدثه ، فكذلك كل محدث يدفع هذا ، وسأل الدليل ، وأيد ذلك بما يجوز أن يعرفه محدثا من لا يعرف خلقا [؟] من أن الجسم
In that he did not look at it and neglected it because he did not see a place that the state of being temporally originated and being eternal are only the indication, and our situation here is nothing that distinguishes if it is then it is in something else, it is established that both are similar in themselves, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he objected: Is the acquired known from other than it? The Sheikh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: This is the objection that the acquired is confused with other than it such that the reality of neither of them is known, so it is established that both are created together for that reason. And after, it is not about knowing the acquired but rather about knowing what is for Allah, not recognizing Him in His creation, not negating from Him what He is, nor affirming for Him what He is not, for then I would be lying about Him, and that is disbelief. And according to the Mu'tazilites: there is no way to know Him, so you always fall into doubt and cannot reach Him. And that is the meaning that Allah negated that there be with Him a god – the people of I'tizal verified it foolishly without knowledge, and that is in His statement (the Exalted): 'Then each god would have taken what He created' (Quran 23:91). And Allah is the grantor of success. Then his statement reached that he does not know through the movement itself that it is created, so this applies to every accident such as combination and separation, so it invalidates that there be in any of that an indication of its creation. He refutes this by stating the agreed principle that the proof of creation is from temporal origination (ḥudūth). The passage then affirms that bodies are known through God and the proof from temporality is sound.

The Definition of Creation and the Qadariyya Contradiction
Maturidi defines creation and presents a logical syllogism against Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of creation and how he uses it to expose a contradiction in the Qadariyya view.

Core Idea
Creation means bringing from non-existence; if accidents are created, bodies must be too.

Imam al-Maturidi begins his refutation by establishing a clear definition of creation. He argues that the Qadariyya, who accept that God creates accidents, are logically bound to also accept that God creates bodies, including human actions. This lesson unpacks that foundational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of creation
Notice how Maturidi defines 'creating the body' as bringing it from non-existence into existence. This is a key premise.
The Arabic uses 'خروج من العدم' - coming out of non-existence.
2
Follow the syllogism
Maturidi points out that the Qadariyya describe themselves as doing acts (accidents) and attribute creation to God for those acts. He then asks: why not also for bodies?
3
Understand the response about Zayd's act
The Qadariyya might respond that human acts are not like the creation of bodies. Maturidi argues that if we cannot truly verify the aspect of existence in our acts, then the argument does not apply to us, but it applies to them because they claim human acts are created by humans.
This is a subtle point; the commentary will clarify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وليس هذا تقدير السؤال ، ولكن بما ليس معنى خلق الجسم إلا خروجه من العدم ووجوده بعد أن لم يكن ، وبه وصفتم أنفسكم فى فعل الأعراض ، كيف لا جاز الوصف بخلق الجسم وليس ثمة غير ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . فأجاب بالفعل ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لأناً لم نحقق لنا فى فعلنا الوجه الذي هو وجه وجود الجسم وكونه ليلزمنا ذلك ، وهم قد حققوا فيلزمهم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم قال : إذ ليس فعل زيد سوى فعل بقدرة ، وانتم تفعلون بها ، كيف فعلتم فعل زيد ؟ قيل : لأن زيدا لا يقدرنا على فعله ، فلم يفعل ، والله قد أقدركم على المعنى الذي به كان الجسم ، فلزمكم ما قابلناكم به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . قال : واحتج بالكاتب والمصوّر إنه لو أراد أن يخرج الثاني على ما عليه الأول لم يمكنه ، دل أن الأول لم يخرج على ذلك به ، فزعم أولا أنه يجوز أن يكون كذلك ما ألقاه الله فيه تلك القدرة. فإن قيل : لم لا يأتى بمثله ؟ فأجاب بأنا وإن كنا نفعل بتلك القدرة نفعله بأسباب لا تجتمع بكليتها حتى لا يخرج منها شيء من نحو الذهن والحفظ وأنواع الأشغال . قال : ولو وجب بهذا محدث لم يلزم من آخر ليجب به مصوّر آخر . وعارض بالفعل : إنه لم يدل العجز على أنا نفعل ، ولو كان العجز يدل على ما ذكروا كان الثانى إذا كان أحسن ، فدل أن الأول له . ثم عارض أنه ما يمنعه ؟ فقال : لأنا نفعل بآلة وقدرة وعلاج وفكر ولا مستوى هذه ، ولو استوت أمكننا ذلك . فيقال له : الوجوه التي تمنعك فعلك أو لا ، فإن قال : لا ، أعظم القول أن علاجه وفكره ونحو ذلك الله ، وهو الذي أنكر خلق ذلك ، فقد أقر به . وإن قال : بلى قيل : السؤال عن ذلك كله أن القدرية زعمت أن الله لو أبقاها ، وقد أبقاها للفعل وكل ذلك أفعال لها القدرة [عليها] ، فما بالها لم تستو ، وقد قصدت أن تستوى ، وكانت لك القدرة ، فهذا يبين أنه على غير تقديرك تخرج. وما ذكر من المعنى هو الدليل الواضح لأنه مع أن قد يخرج أحسن من الأول وأسوى على قصد الاستواء ، إن ذلك كان كذلك ؛ ما لا يبلغ علم أحد إلى تقدير حركته من الهواء والمكان ومن ارتفاع اليد وانخفاضها لو اجتهد كل الجهد ، والفعل لا يخلو عنه ، ثبت أنه لغيره من هذا الوجه : ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك لا أحد يقصد قصد بقبيح الفعل ، وقد يكون كذلك ، ثبت أنه من ذلك الوجه ليس له ، ولو جاز وقوع فعل من وجه لا يعلمه ولا يريده ، ولو اجتهد كل جهده ليعرف حده ومبلغه ويكون له على ما هو عليه ذلك الفعل لجاز مثله في جميع العالم وآيات الرسل وغيرها . والقول فى المصور هو القول في الفاعل ، وفى الصورة هو القول فى الفعل ، لا فرق بينها . ثم قوله : لو أبقى الله القوة ، ومن مذهبه أن القوة لا تبقى وقتين ، لا معنى له . ثم ما عارض من الفعل فهو يختاره ويعلم ما يفعله ويقصده ، فهو من ذلك الوجه له . وقد بينا فى ذلك ما ليس هو بعالم بذلك الوجه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الدليل عندنا من طريق القرآن على لزوم القول بخلق الأفعال قوله : وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوْ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إنَّه عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ ، أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الخَبِيرُ ، فلو لم يكن جل ثناؤه خالقا لما يجهر ويخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه ، ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله ، لم يكن للاحتجاج به بفعل سواه معنى . وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال : هُوَ الَّذِي يُسَبِّرُكُم في البَرِّ وَالْبَحْرِ ، وقال فى موضع آخر : وَقَدَّرْنَا فِيهَا السَّيْرَ سِيرُوا فِيهَا لَيَالِيَ ، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله و به كان السير . وقال : وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُم أَزْوَاجًا ، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: This is not the estimation of the question, but rather because the meaning of creating the body is nothing other than its coming out of non-existence and its existence after it was not, and by this you described yourselves in the act of accidents; why is it not permissible to describe [God] with creating the body when there is no other? And there is no power except with God. So he answered with the act, and that is corrupt; because we have not verified for ourselves the aspect which is the aspect of the body's existence and its being so that it would be binding on us, but they have verified it so it is binding on them. And there is no power except with God. Then he said: Since the act of Zayd is only an act by a power, and you act with it, how did you do the act of Zayd? It was said: Because Zayd did not empower us over his act, so he did not do [it], and God empowered you over the meaning by which the body existed, so what we confronted you with is binding on you. And there is no power except with God. He said: And he argued by the writer and the painter that if he wanted to produce the second [work] as the first was, he could not, indicating that the first was not produced by that [power] alone. So he first claimed that it is possible that it is thus because God instilled in him that power. If it is said: Why does he not produce its like? He answered: Although we act with that power, we perform it with causes that do not come together completely so that nothing of it comes out, such as the mind, memory, and various occupations. He said: And if by this an originated thing were necessitated, it would not necessitate another so that another maker would be necessitated? And he objected by the act: Indeed, the inability does not indicate that we do [the act]; and if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second [work] if it is better would indicate that the first is his. Then he objected: What prevents him? He said: Because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; and if they were equal, we would be able to do that. So it is said to him: The aspects that prevent you, are they your act or not? If he says: No, he makes a great claim that his treatment, thought, and so forth are from God, and he is the one who denied the creation of that, so he has acknowledged it. And if he says: Yes, it is said: The question about all that is that the Qadariyya claimed that if God had preserved them, and He had preserved them for the act, and all that is acts for which they have power, why are they not equal, when they intended to be equal, and you had the power? So this clarifies that it comes out not according to your estimation. And what was mentioned of the meaning is the clear proof, because with it, that may produce a better and more perfect one than the first, intending equality; that is thus; what no one's knowledge reaches to the estimation of its motion from air, place, raising and lowering of the hand, if he exerts all effort, and the act is not free from it; it is established that it is from other than him from this aspect: And there is no power except with God. And upon that, no one intends an intention by an ugly act, and it may be thus; it is established that from that aspect it is not his; and if it were permissible for an act to occur from an aspect he does not know nor intend, even if he exerts all effort to know its limit and extent and have it as it is, then the like would be permissible in the entire world, the signs of the messengers, and other things. And the statement about the maker is the statement about the actor, and about the image is the statement about the act; there is no difference between them. Then his statement: If God preserved the power, and from his doctrine is that power does not remain for two moments, has no meaning. Then what he objected concerning the act, he chooses it and knows what he does and intends it, so from that aspect it is his. And we have clarified concerning that what is not known from that aspect. And there is no power except with God. Then the proof according to us from the way of the Quran for the necessity of asserting the creation of actions is His statement: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Acquainted?' (67:13-14) So if He, exalted, were not the Creator of what is public and secret, He would not have argued by it for His knowledge. And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it; so there would be no meaning to arguing by it for an action other than His. And also that God said: 'He is the One who causes you to travel on land and sea' (10:22), and said elsewhere: 'And We determined therein the journey; travel therein nights' (34:18). He informed that the determination of the journey and the causing of travel is His act and by it the journey was. And He said: 'And among His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates' (30:21), in which is the news that the placing of affection and mercy is among His signs.
Source pages p. 852

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (those who claim humans create their own actions) by Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, arguing that all actions are created by God. It begins by clarifying the definition of creation: creating a body means bringing it from non-existence to existence. The Maturidi argues that if the Qadariyya admit divine creation for accidents, they must also admit it for bodies. He then addresses an objection about the human act: human actions are performed by a power given by God, but humans do not control the specific outcome (e.g., Zayd's act) because God empowers them over the meaning (the essential cause) of the body's existence. The proof is that if someone tries to produce an identical second work of art, he cannot, indicating that the first was not produced merely by his own power but by God's instilled power. The inability to reproduce perfectly shows that the act relies on factors beyond human control like mind, memory, and tools, which are not fully equal. The Qadariyya claim that if God preserved the power, actions would be equal. Maturidi responds that even with preserved power, equality is impossible due to varying conditions, proving the act is not entirely the human's. He also argues that if an undesirable ugly act occurs without the agent's full knowledge or intention, then the same would apply to all acts and even miracles, which is absurd. He concludes that the power (quwwa) does not remain for two moments, refuting the Qadariyya claim. Finally, he brings Quranic proofs: God's knowledge of secrets proves He creates them; otherwise He would not argue by them. Verses about travel and determination of journey show that the action (journey) is by God's determination and act. The creation of spouses and placing affection and mercy are also signs of God's creation of actions.

Key Terms
خلق الجسم
خروج من العدم
فعل الأعراض
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that creation means simply causing change or alteration, not bringing from non-existence.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly defines creation as خروج من العدم (coming out of non-existence), which is a specific act of bringing into being that only God can do.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the meaning of 'creating the body'?
A) Bringing it from non-existence to existence
B) Giving it shape and form
C) Combining its parts
D) Giving it life

Key Takeaway
Creation is defined as bringing from non-existence, and this definition is used to show that if God creates accidents, He must create bodies as well.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you attribute your successes to your own efforts, do you realize you are implicitly claiming a creative power that only God has? How can you shift your mindset to see your actions as acquisition (كسب) rather than creation?
?
Maturidi says the Qadariyya 'verified for themselves' a power over the aspect of existence. Where in your life have you assumed an attribute of God for yourself, and what would it look like to surrender that assumption today?
?
The Qadariyya's inconsistency lay in applying the definition of creation to some things but not others. Are there areas of your belief or practice where you apply different standards to God's actions and your own? Will you commit to aligning your thoughts with the truth of God's sole creative power?
