Allah's Existence
intermediate
7 min
The Writer and Painter Analogy: Human Inability and Divine Creation
Maturidi argues using the writer/painter analogy, then addresses objections about causes and equality of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the example of a writer or painter to argue that human actions are not created by humans but by God.

Core Idea
The inability to reproduce identical works shows human actions depend on God.

Maturidi presents a powerful analogy: a writer or painter cannot produce a second work exactly like the first. This inability demonstrates that the first work was not created by the person alone but through God's power. This lesson explores the analogy and its implications for the nature of human action.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy of the writer/painter
Maturidi argues that if someone tries to produce a second identical work and cannot, it shows the first was not created by that person alone.
The analogy applies to any skilled artisan.
2
Examine the response about causes
Maturidi responds to the objection that the person might have the power but lacks complete causes. He explains that the act is performed with causes (mind, memory, tools) that never come together completely.
This shows the act is not solely from the agent.
3
Consider the objection about equality
The Qadariyya claim that if God preserved the power, actions would be equal. Maturidi argues that even with preserved power, equality is impossible due to varying conditions, proving the act is not entirely the human's.
4
Reflect on the ugly act discussion
If an ugly act occurs without the agent's full knowledge or intention, it cannot be considered the agent's act. This further shows that actions are from God.
This section concludes with 'ولا قوة إلا بالله'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وليس هذا تقدير السؤال ، ولكن بما ليس معنى خلق الجسم إلا خروجه من العدم ووجوده بعد أن لم يكن ، وبه وصفتم أنفسكم فى فعل الأعراض ، كيف لا جاز الوصف بخلق الجسم وليس ثمة غير ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . فأجاب بالفعل ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لأناً لم نحقق لنا فى فعلنا الوجه الذي هو وجه وجود الجسم وكونه ليلزمنا ذلك ، وهم قد حققوا فيلزمهم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم قال : إذ ليس فعل زيد سوى فعل بقدرة ، وانتم تفعلون بها ، كيف فعلتم فعل زيد ؟ قيل : لأن زيدا لا يقدرنا على فعله ، فلم يفعل ، والله قد أقدركم على المعنى الذي به كان الجسم ، فلزمكم ما قابلناكم به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . قال : واحتج بالكاتب والمصوّر إنه لو أراد أن يخرج الثاني على ما عليه الأول لم يمكنه ، دل أن الأول لم يخرج على ذلك به ، فزعم أولا أنه يجوز أن يكون كذلك ما ألقاه الله فيه تلك القدرة. فإن قيل : لم لا يأتى بمثله ؟ فأجاب بأنا وإن كنا نفعل بتلك القدرة نفعله بأسباب لا تجتمع بكليتها حتى لا يخرج منها شيء من نحو الذهن والحفظ وأنواع الأشغال . قال : ولو وجب بهذا محدث لم يلزم من آخر ليجب به مصوّر آخر . وعارض بالفعل : إنه لم يدل العجز على أنا نفعل ، ولو كان العجز يدل على ما ذكروا كان الثانى إذا كان أحسن ، فدل أن الأول له . ثم عارض أنه ما يمنعه ؟ فقال : لأنا نفعل بآلة وقدرة وعلاج وفكر ولا مستوى هذه ، ولو استوت أمكننا ذلك . فيقال له : الوجوه التي تمنعك فعلك أو لا ، فإن قال : لا ، أعظم القول أن علاجه وفكره ونحو ذلك الله ، وهو الذي أنكر خلق ذلك ، فقد أقر به . وإن قال : بلى قيل : السؤال عن ذلك كله أن القدرية زعمت أن الله لو أبقاها ، وقد أبقاها للفعل وكل ذلك أفعال لها القدرة [عليها] ، فما بالها لم تستو ، وقد قصدت أن تستوى ، وكانت لك القدرة ، فهذا يبين أنه على غير تقديرك تخرج. وما ذكر من المعنى هو الدليل الواضح لأنه مع أن قد يخرج أحسن من الأول وأسوى على قصد الاستواء ، إن ذلك كان كذلك ؛ ما لا يبلغ علم أحد إلى تقدير حركته من الهواء والمكان ومن ارتفاع اليد وانخفاضها لو اجتهد كل الجهد ، والفعل لا يخلو عنه ، ثبت أنه لغيره من هذا الوجه : ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك لا أحد يقصد قصد بقبيح الفعل ، وقد يكون كذلك ، ثبت أنه من ذلك الوجه ليس له ، ولو جاز وقوع فعل من وجه لا يعلمه ولا يريده ، ولو اجتهد كل جهده ليعرف حده ومبلغه ويكون له على ما هو عليه ذلك الفعل لجاز مثله في جميع العالم وآيات الرسل وغيرها . والقول فى المصور هو القول في الفاعل ، وفى الصورة هو القول فى الفعل ، لا فرق بينها . ثم قوله : لو أبقى الله القوة ، ومن مذهبه أن القوة لا تبقى وقتين ، لا معنى له . ثم ما عارض من الفعل فهو يختاره ويعلم ما يفعله ويقصده ، فهو من ذلك الوجه له . وقد بينا فى ذلك ما ليس هو بعالم بذلك الوجه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الدليل عندنا من طريق القرآن على لزوم القول بخلق الأفعال قوله : وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوْ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إنَّه عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ ، أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الخَبِيرُ ، فلو لم يكن جل ثناؤه خالقا لما يجهر ويخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه ، ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله ، لم يكن للاحتجاج به بفعل سواه معنى . وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال : هُوَ الَّذِي يُسَبِّرُكُم في البَرِّ وَالْبَحْرِ ، وقال فى موضع آخر : وَقَدَّرْنَا فِيهَا السَّيْرَ سِيرُوا فِيهَا لَيَالِيَ ، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله و به كان السير . وقال : وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُم أَزْوَاجًا ، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: This is not the estimation of the question, but rather because the meaning of creating the body is nothing other than its coming out of non-existence and its existence after it was not, and by this you described yourselves in the act of accidents; why is it not permissible to describe [God] with creating the body when there is no other? And there is no power except with God. So he answered with the act, and that is corrupt; because we have not verified for ourselves the aspect which is the aspect of the body's existence and its being so that it would be binding on us, but they have verified it so it is binding on them. And there is no power except with God. Then he said: Since the act of Zayd is only an act by a power, and you act with it, how did you do the act of Zayd? It was said: Because Zayd did not empower us over his act, so he did not do [it], and God empowered you over the meaning by which the body existed, so what we confronted you with is binding on you. And there is no power except with God. He said: And he argued by the writer and the painter that if he wanted to produce the second [work] as the first was, he could not, indicating that the first was not produced by that [power] alone. So he first claimed that it is possible that it is thus because God instilled in him that power. If it is said: Why does he not produce its like? He answered: Although we act with that power, we perform it with causes that do not come together completely so that nothing of it comes out, such as the mind, memory, and various occupations. He said: And if by this an originated thing were necessitated, it would not necessitate another so that another maker would be necessitated? And he objected by the act: Indeed, the inability does not indicate that we do [the act]; and if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second [work] if it is better would indicate that the first is his. Then he objected: What prevents him? He said: Because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; and if they were equal, we would be able to do that. So it is said to him: The aspects that prevent you, are they your act or not? If he says: No, he makes a great claim that his treatment, thought, and so forth are from God, and he is the one who denied the creation of that, so he has acknowledged it. And if he says: Yes, it is said: The question about all that is that the Qadariyya claimed that if God had preserved them, and He had preserved them for the act, and all that is acts for which they have power, why are they not equal, when they intended to be equal, and you had the power? So this clarifies that it comes out not according to your estimation. And what was mentioned of the meaning is the clear proof, because with it, that may produce a better and more perfect one than the first, intending equality; that is thus; what no one's knowledge reaches to the estimation of its motion from air, place, raising and lowering of the hand, if he exerts all effort, and the act is not free from it; it is established that it is from other than him from this aspect: And there is no power except with God. And upon that, no one intends an intention by an ugly act, and it may be thus; it is established that from that aspect it is not his; and if it were permissible for an act to occur from an aspect he does not know nor intend, even if he exerts all effort to know its limit and extent and have it as it is, then the like would be permissible in the entire world, the signs of the messengers, and other things. And the statement about the maker is the statement about the actor, and about the image is the statement about the act; there is no difference between them. Then his statement: If God preserved the power, and from his doctrine is that power does not remain for two moments, has no meaning. Then what he objected concerning the act, he chooses it and knows what he does and intends it, so from that aspect it is his. And we have clarified concerning that what is not known from that aspect. And there is no power except with God. Then the proof according to us from the way of the Quran for the necessity of asserting the creation of actions is His statement: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Acquainted?' (67:13-14) So if He, exalted, were not the Creator of what is public and secret, He would not have argued by it for His knowledge. And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it; so there would be no meaning to arguing by it for an action other than His. And also that God said: 'He is the One who causes you to travel on land and sea' (10:22), and said elsewhere: 'And We determined therein the journey; travel therein nights' (34:18). He informed that the determination of the journey and the causing of travel is His act and by it the journey was. And He said: 'And among His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates' (30:21), in which is the news that the placing of affection and mercy is among His signs.
Source pages p. 852

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (those who claim humans create their own actions) by Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, arguing that all actions are created by God. It begins by clarifying the definition of creation: creating a body means bringing it from non-existence to existence. The Maturidi argues that if the Qadariyya admit divine creation for accidents, they must also admit it for bodies. He then addresses an objection about the human act: human actions are performed by a power given by God, but humans do not control the specific outcome (e.g., Zayd's act) because God empowers them over the meaning (the essential cause) of the body's existence. The proof is that if someone tries to produce an identical second work of art, he cannot, indicating that the first was not produced merely by his own power but by God's instilled power. The inability to reproduce perfectly shows that the act relies on factors beyond human control like mind, memory, and tools, which are not fully equal. The Qadariyya claim that if God preserved the power, actions would be equal. Maturidi responds that even with preserved power, equality is impossible due to varying conditions, proving the act is not entirely the human's. He also argues that if an undesirable ugly act occurs without the agent's full knowledge or intention, then the same would apply to all acts and even miracles, which is absurd. He concludes that the power (quwwa) does not remain for two moments, refuting the Qadariyya claim. Finally, he brings Quranic proofs: God's knowledge of secrets proves He creates them; otherwise He would not argue by them. Verses about travel and determination of journey show that the action (journey) is by God's determination and act. The creation of spouses and placing affection and mercy are also signs of God's creation of actions.

Key Terms
الكاتب
المصوّر
القوة
الأسباب
العجز
القبيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human inability to perfect actions proves that humans have no responsibility, but Maturidi uses it to show that actions are created by God while humans acquire them.
Correction: Inability to reproduce perfectly shows the act is not solely human, but Maturidi does not deny human acquisition; he clarifies that the act is from God in terms of creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's analogy, why cannot a writer or painter produce a second work exactly like the first?
A) Because he lacks the necessary power
B) Because the necessary causes (mind, memory, tools) are never completely equal
C) Because God changes his intention each time
D) Because he was not the true maker of the first work

Key Takeaway
The inability to produce identical actions demonstrates that human actions are not created by humans alone but by God, while humans are the acquirers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to repeat a good deed or avoid a sin, do you recognize that the exact outcome is not entirely in your hands? How does this realization change your reliance on God and your attitude toward your own efforts? Will you still exert your best, knowing the final result is from Him?
?
Think of a time you intended to do something perfectly but failed. Did you blame external factors or your own lack of skill? This lesson teaches that even your own causes (mind, memory, tools) are not fully under your control. How does this perspective affect your sense of accountability and your need to seek God's help?
?
The lesson discusses ugly acts: no one intends them but they occur. Reflect on a specific sin you committed. Can you see that there was an aspect beyond your control while still acknowledging your role as the acquirer? How does this deepen your need for God's protection and your hope in His mercy, knowing that even your bad actions are encompassed by His power?

Quranic Proofs for the Creation of Actions
Maturidi presents three Quranic proofs for God's creation of human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three Quranic proofs that Maturidi uses to establish that all actions are created by God.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of secrets and control over travel and affection prove He creates actions.

After the rational arguments, Maturidi turns to Quranic evidence. He cites verses showing that God knows what is hidden because He creates it, that He causes travel and determines journeys, and that He creates spouses and places affection and mercy. These verses directly support the doctrine that actions are created by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof (Quran 67:13-14)
Maturidi argues that God's knowledge of secrets implies He creates them; otherwise, the argument would not hold.
The verse: 'He knows what is in the breasts' followed by 'Does He who created not know?'
2
Read the second proof (Quran 10:22 and 34:18)
God causes travel and determines journeys, showing that the act of traveling is created by Him.
These verses connect God's action of causing travel with the act itself.
3
Read the third proof (Quran 30:21)
The creation of spouses and placing of affection and mercy are signs of God, indicating He creates these relational actions.
Affection and mercy are actions of the heart, yet they are among God's signs.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وليس هذا تقدير السؤال ، ولكن بما ليس معنى خلق الجسم إلا خروجه من العدم ووجوده بعد أن لم يكن ، وبه وصفتم أنفسكم فى فعل الأعراض ، كيف لا جاز الوصف بخلق الجسم وليس ثمة غير ، ولا أبقاها ، وقد أبقاها للفعل وكل ذلك أفعال لها القدرة [عليها] ، فما بالها لم تستو ، وقد قصدت أن تستوى ، وكانت لك القدرة ، فهذا يبين أنه على غير تقديرك تخرج. وما ذكر من المعنى هو الدليل الواضح لأنه مع أن ويكون له على ما هو عليه ذلك الفعل لجاز مثله في جميع العالم وآيات الرسل وغيرها . والقول فى المصور هو القول في الفاعل ، وفى الصورة هو القول فى الفعل ، لا فرق بينها . ثم قوله : لو أبقى الله القوة ، ومن مذهبه أن القوة لا تبقى وقتين ، لا معنى له . ثم ما عارض من الفعل فهو يختاره ويعلم ما يفعله ويقصده ، فهو من ذلك الوجه له . وقد بينا فى ذلك ما ليس هو بعالم بذلك الوجه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الدليل يكن جل ثناؤه خالقا لما يجهر ويخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه ، ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله ، لم يكن للاحتجاج به بفعل سواه معنى . وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال : هُوَ الَّذِي يُسَبِّرُكُم في البَرِّ وَالْبَحْرِ ، وقال فى موضع آخر : وَقَدَّرْنَا فِيهَا السَّيْرَ سِيرُوا فِيهَا لَيَالِيَ ، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله و به كان السير . وقال : وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُم أَزْوَاجًا ، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته.
Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: This is not the estimation of the question, but rather because the meaning of creating the body is nothing other than its coming out of non-existence and its existence after it was not, and by this you described yourselves in the act of accidents; why is it not permissible to describe [God] with creating the body when there is no other? And there is no power except with God. So he answered with the act, and that is corrupt; because we have not verified for ourselves the aspect which is the aspect of the body's existence and its being so that it would be binding on us, but they have verified it so it is binding on them. And there is no power except with God. Then he said: Since the act of Zayd is only an act by a power, and you act with it, how did you do the act of Zayd? It was said: Because Zayd did not empower us over his act, so he did not do [it], and God empowered you over the meaning by which the body existed, so what we confronted you with is binding on you. And there is no power except with God. He said: And he argued by the writer and the painter that if he wanted to produce the second [work] as the first was, he could not, indicating that the first was not produced by that [power] alone. So he first claimed that it is possible that it is thus because God instilled in him that power. If it is said: Why does he not produce its like? He answered: Although we act with that power, we perform it with causes that do not come together completely so that nothing of it comes out, such as the mind, memory, and various occupations. He said: And if by this an originated thing were necessitated, it would not necessitate another so that another maker would be necessitated? And he objected by the act: Indeed, the inability does not indicate that we do [the act]; and if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second [work] if it is better would indicate that the first is his. Then he objected: What prevents him? He said: Because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; and if they were equal, we would be able to do that. So it is said to him: The aspects that prevent you, are they your act or not? If he says: No, he makes a great claim that his treatment, thought, and so forth are from God, and he is the one who denied the creation of that, so he has acknowledged it. And if he says: Yes, it is said: The question about all that is that the Qadariyya claimed that if God had preserved them, and He had preserved them for the act, and all that is acts for which they have power, why are they not equal, when they intended to be equal, and you had the power? So this clarifies that it comes out not according to your estimation. And what was mentioned of the meaning is the clear proof, because with it, that may produce a better and more perfect one than the first, intending equality; that is thus; what no one's knowledge reaches to the estimation of its motion from air, place, raising and lowering of the hand, if he exerts all effort, and the act is not free from it; it is established that it is from other than him from this aspect: And there is no power except with God. And upon that, no one intends an intention by an ugly act, and it may be thus; it is established that from that aspect it is not his; and if it were permissible for an act to occur from an aspect he does not know nor intend, even if he exerts all effort to know its limit and extent and have it as it is, then the like would be permissible in the entire world, the signs of the messengers, and other things. And the statement about the maker is the statement about the actor, and about the image is the statement about the act; there is no difference between them. Then his statement: If God preserved the power, and from his doctrine is that power does not remain for two moments, has no meaning. Then what he objected concerning the act, he chooses it and knows what he does and intends it, so from that aspect it is his. And we have clarified concerning that what is not known from that aspect. And there is no power except with God. Then the proof according to us from the way of the Quran for the necessity of asserting the creation of actions is His statement: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Acquainted?' (67:13-14) So if He, exalted, were not the Creator of what is public and secret, He would not have argued by it for His knowledge. And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it; so there would be no meaning to arguing by it for an action other than His. And also that God said: 'He is the One who causes you to travel on land and sea' (10:22), and said elsewhere: 'And We determined therein the journey; travel therein nights' (34:18). He informed that the determination of the journey and the causing of travel is His act and by it the journey was. And He said: 'And among His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates' (30:21), in which is the news that the placing of affection and mercy is among His signs.
Source pages p. 852

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (those who claim humans create their own actions) by Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, arguing that all actions are created by God. It begins by clarifying the definition of creation: creating a body means bringing it from non-existence to existence. The Maturidi argues that if the Qadariyya admit divine creation for accidents, they must also admit it for bodies. He then addresses an objection about the human act: human actions are performed by a power given by God, but humans do not control the specific outcome (e.g., Zayd's act) because God empowers them over the meaning (the essential cause) of the body's existence. The proof is that if someone tries to produce an identical second work of art, he cannot, indicating that the first was not produced merely by his own power but by God's instilled power. The inability to reproduce perfectly shows that the act relies on factors beyond human control like mind, memory, and tools, which are not fully equal. The Qadariyya claim that if God preserved the power, actions would be equal. Maturidi responds that even with preserved power, equality is impossible due to varying conditions, proving the act is not entirely the human's. He also argues that if an undesirable ugly act occurs without the agent's full knowledge or intention, then the same would apply to all acts and even miracles, which is absurd. He concludes that the power (quwwa) does not remain for two moments, refuting the Qadariyya claim. Finally, he brings Quranic proofs: God's knowledge of secrets proves He creates them; otherwise He would not argue by them. Verses about travel and determination of journey show that the action (journey) is by God's determination and act. The creation of spouses and placing affection and mercy are also signs of God's creation of actions.

Key Terms
القوة
وقتين
خلق الأفعال
آيات القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human choice and intention create the act, but Maturidi distinguishes between the human's aspect (choice, intention) and God's aspect (creation).
Correction: Maturidi affirms that from the perspective of choice and intention, the act is the human's, but from the perspective of creation, it is God's. This avoids denying human responsibility.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Maturidi use to argue that God's knowledge of actions implies He creates them?
A) 'He is the One who causes you to travel' (10:22)
B) 'And We determined therein the journey' (34:18)
C) 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knowing... Does He who created not know?' (67:13-14)
D) 'And among His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates' (30:21)

Key Takeaway
Three Quranic verses prove that all actions, including speech, travel, and emotional states, are created by God, while humans are responsible through their choice and intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that even your most private thoughts and secret words are created by God, does that change how you guard your inner self? What would it mean for your sincerity if every intention you hold is also directly from Him?
?
The passage teaches that affection and mercy between spouses are placed by God as a sign. When you experience love or kindness, do you recognize it as a direct creation from Allah, or do you take it for granted? How might acknowledging His role deepen your gratitude?
?
If your ability to act is renewed by God at every moment, what does that imply about your dependence on Him for even the smallest movement? Are there areas in your life where you live as if your power is self-sustained rather than borrowed?

The Proof from Revelation and Reason: The Example of Hajj
Maturidi presents the thesis and the first example of Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that obligation in Islamic law is based on capacity of means (asbab) rather than actual power to perform the act, as demonstrated by the verse on Hajj.

Core Idea
Obligation depends on means, not on the power to act.

Imam Maturidi begins by laying out the twofold evidence for his thesis: revelation and reason. The revelation includes verses that negate capacity in certain situations, and the intellect perceives the logical necessity. To illustrate, he focuses on the Hajj verse, which makes pilgrimage obligatory only for those who have the means (sabil) of provision and transportation. This example shows that if actual power were required, Hajj would never be binding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting how Maturidi introduces the evidence and the Hajj example.
2
Identify the thesis statement
Find the sentence that states the overall claim about obligation and capacity.
It is the very first sentence.
3
Analyze the Hajj example
Break down the logic of the Hajj verse: what does 'able to it a way' mean? Why would requiring actual power lead to a problem?
Consider that actual power arises only at the moment of travel.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this principle applies to other areas of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرت من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير. وأما العقل فذلك إدراك العقل. ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضا قوله تعالى: {وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا} ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحدا ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يعرض عليه الخروج، ومعلوم أن قوة العقل بعد البلوغ قوة ليست معه للحال، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عير من قعد. وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد، ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يكلف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى وما بها يحتم غير موجودة، والتكلف لازم، وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك مجيء السمع واتفاق الألسن على سؤال المعونة من الله والتقوية على ما أمر من العبادات، فلو كانت هي موجودة أو العبادة من تسقط لعدمها كان السؤال سؤال جور والأمر بكفران ما أنعم عليه من القوة، ثبت بما ذكرنا لزوم التكليف دونه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك قول شعيب: {إِنْ أُرِيدُ إِلَّا الْإِصْلَاحَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُ} أثبت تحقيق الذي قال بوجود الاستطاعة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم في إثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذي له أبطل القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفي ما يريد الآخر إثباته، أو يسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر، فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن لا يكون وعلى أن يجعله كاذبا فيما [؟]
Then the evidence for the necessity of obligation without the reality of this type of power is revelation and reason. As for revelation, it is what it told of verses on negating capacity, then command and prohibition and rebuke. And as for reason, it is that perception of the intellect. Then what also clarifies this is His statement: 'And Allah owes upon people the Hajj of the House, whoever is able to it a way' and it is known that there is no way to the reality of actions while one finds provision and mount. And if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of power, the power of action, then it would not be binding on anyone; because the power of actions is that which occurs at the occurrence of times, and Hajj is not obligatory until that power comes, and it only comes by traveling, so one would have the excuse to stay behind since it is not obligatory. And likewise the matter of Jihad; for if one knew that what he has of means does not reach it, he would not be called to go out. And it is known that the strength of reason after puberty is a strength that is not with him at present, and yet its obligation is binding on him where he is rebuked for staying behind. And likewise we find standing, fasting and the like, one has a way out by substitution, even though the reality of the power of action may exist by effort, it is established that the obligation of things is not by it, but by conditions. And upon that are all acts of worship: one who knows that he does not have the means to complete prayer, fasting, or Hajj is not initially obligated for that. Then the power of actions does not remain and what is not present is not possible, and obligation is binding. And likewise Zakat is obligatory by wealth and conditions even if it is possible that payment is hindered by excuses, and there is no power except by Allah. And upon that comes revelation and the agreement of tongues on asking Allah for help and strength for what He commanded of acts of worship. For if that power were present or worship were to fall due to its absence, then the request would be a request of injustice and the command would be ingratitude for the strength He bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned the binding of obligation without it, and there is no power except by Allah. And upon that is the statement of Shu'ayb: 'I only intend reform as much as I am able' - he affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of capacity, and there is no power except by Allah. Then in establishing power is the realization of the meaning for which the claim of two [gods] is invalidated, which is that each of them would be able to negate what the other wants to affirm, or one would conceal what the other's knowledge does not reach. So who empowers the slave over what Allah does not know to not be and to make Him a liar in what [؟]
Source pages p. 857

Commentary
This passage provides the proof that obligation is based on the capacity of conditions (asbab) rather than the actual power of action. Maturidi first states that the evidence is from revelation and reason. For revelation, he points to verses that negate capacity in certain situations, followed by commands and rebukes. For reason, he appeals to the intellect's perception. He then elaborates with the example of Hajj: the verse makes Hajj obligatory for those who have the 'means' (sabil) of provision and transportation. If obligation required actual power to perform the action, then no one would be obligated because actual power only arises at the moment of travel, creating a vicious cycle. Similarly for Jihad: if a person lacks means, he is not called. Even for prayer, fasting, and other acts, one may fulfill them through substitution if unable, showing that obligation is tied to conditions, not actual power. He also notes that asking God for help in worship would be unjust if capacity were already present. Finally, he connects this to tawhid: if the slave had independent power, it would imply two gods, since each could negate the other's will. Thus the correct view of capacity supports divine unity.

Key Terms
دليل
سمع
عقل
حج
استطاعة
سبيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that for an act to be obligatory, one must have the actual ability to perform it at the moment of command.
Correction: Maturidi shows that obligation is based on having the means (like provision for Hajj), not on the actual power to perform the act at that moment.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the phrase 'able to it a way' in the Hajj verse refer to?
A) The actual power to perform Hajj at that moment
B) Provision and transportation
C) Physical strength and health
D) Faith and intention

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Hajj is tied to having the means, not to possessing the actual power to perform it at the moment of command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the Hajj verse and Maturidi's reasoning. Now reflect: In what areas of your life have you been using the excuse of 'I don't have the ability yet' when Allah has already given you the means? What step can you take today to act on the means He has provided?
?
Maturidi argues that obligation is based on means, not actual power. When you consider the commands of Allah that seem difficult, do you tend to focus on your perceived lack of power, or on the means He has already placed in your life? What would change if you shifted your focus?
?
The example of Hajj teaches that the obligation becomes binding once you have the provision and mount. Are there any acts of worship or good deeds that you know are required of you but you delay because you think you need to be 'more capable' first? What means do you already possess that make you obligated right now?

Further Examples: Jihad, Prayer, Fasting, and Zakat
Maturidi provides multiple examples from Islamic law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Maturidi uses examples from Jihad, prayer, fasting, and Zakat to reinforce that obligation is based on conditions and available means.

Core Idea
Obligations are tied to conditions, not to the power to act.

Maturidi continues his argument by drawing on further examples from Islamic law. Jihad is only required when one has the means to reach the battlefield. For prayer, fasting, and similar acts, one may fulfill them through substitution (badal) if unable, showing that the original obligation is based on the presence of conditions. Zakat is due based on wealth and conditions, even if payment becomes difficult. These examples collectively establish that obligations are determined by circumstances, not by the actual power to perform.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic for this lesson, focusing on the examples of Jihad, prayer, fasting, and Zakat.
2
Analyze the Jihad example
Why would knowledge of lacking means excuse someone from Jihad? What does this say about obligation?
Consider that obligation is not unconditional.
3
Understand substitution (badal)
How does the option of substitution for prayer and fasting indicate that obligation is not based on actual power?
If actual power were required, substitution would not be needed.
4
Consider Zakat
Why is Zakat tied to wealth and conditions, even if payment is hindered?
Obligation is based on the presence of wealth, not on the ability to pay at that instant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to Maturidi, why is the example of Jihad relevant to his argument?
A) It shows that Jihad is always obligatory regardless of means

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself excused from a religious obligation due to circumstances, do you thank Allah for His mercy, or do you feel a sense of relief that you 'got away'? How does this lesson change your attitude toward the conditions Allah places on you?
?
Consider a time when you used a legitimate excuse to delay or avoid an obligation. Did you remember that all power is from Allah, or did you rely on your own reasoning? How can you cultivate a greater reliance on Allah's strength in fulfilling your duties?
?
This lesson shows that Allah ties obligations to conditions, not abstract ability. Are there areas in your life where you assume you cannot fulfill an obligation because of your current situation, yet you have the means? What is one step you can take today to act on that obligation?

The Logical Conclusion: Asking Help and the Unity of God
Maturidi provides the final arguments from practice and tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if obligation were based on actual power, asking God for help in worship would be unjust, and that this correct view of capacity supports the oneness of God (tawhid).

Core Idea
Correct understanding of capacity affirms divine unity.

Maturidi concludes his argument by pointing to the universal practice of asking God for help in worship. If humans already possessed the power to do good deeds, such prayers would be unjust. Moreover, the proper view of capacity leads to the invalidation of polytheism: if the slave had independent power, it would imply two gods, each capable of negating the other's will. Maturidi cites the verse of Prophet Shu'ayb to ground his view in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage for this lesson, focusing on the argument about asking help and the tawhid connection.
2
Analyze the argument from asking help
Why would asking God for strength be unjust if humans already had the power? What does this imply about the source of capacity?
Consider that asking for help acknowledges that capacity comes from God.
3
Examine the statement of Shu'ayb
How does Shu'ayb's statement 'as much as I am able' affirm that capacity is a real thing given by God?
4
Understand the connection to tawhid
Explain the reasoning that invalidates two gods based on mutual negation and the limit of the slave's power.
If the slave had independent power, each god could negate the other's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرت من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير. وأما العقل فذلك إدراك العقل. ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضا قوله تعالى: {وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا} ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحدا ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يعرض عليه الخروج، ومعلوم أن قوة العقل بعد البلوغ قوة ليست معه للحال، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عير من قعد. وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد، ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يكلف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى وما بها يحتم غير موجودة، والتكلف لازم، وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك مجيء السمع واتفاق الألسن على سؤال المعونة من الله والتقوية على ما أمر من العبادات، فلو كانت هي موجودة أو العبادة من تسقط لعدمها كان السؤال سؤال جور والأمر بكفران ما أنعم عليه من القوة، ثبت بما ذكرنا لزوم التكليف دونه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك قول شعيب: {إِنْ أُرِيدُ إِلَّا الْإِصْلَاحَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُ} أثبت تحقيق الذي قال بوجود الاستطاعة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم في إثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذي له أبطل القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفي ما يريد الآخر إثباته، أو يسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر، فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن لا يكون وعلى أن يجعله كاذبا فيما [؟]
Then the evidence for the necessity of obligation without the reality of this type of power is revelation and reason. As for revelation, it is what it told of verses on negating capacity, then command and prohibition and rebuke. And as for reason, it is that perception of the intellect. Then what also clarifies this is His statement: 'And Allah owes upon people the Hajj of the House, whoever is able to it a way' and it is known that there is no way to the reality of actions while one finds provision and mount. And if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of power, the power of action, then it would not be binding on anyone; because the power of actions is that which occurs at the occurrence of times, and Hajj is not obligatory until that power comes, and it only comes by traveling, so one would have the excuse to stay behind since it is not obligatory. And likewise the matter of Jihad; for if one knew that what he has of means does not reach it, he would not be called to go out. And it is known that the strength of reason after puberty is a strength that is not with him at present, and yet its obligation is binding on him where he is rebuked for staying behind. And likewise we find standing, fasting and the like, one has a way out by substitution, even though the reality of the power of action may exist by effort, it is established that the obligation of things is not by it, but by conditions. And upon that are all acts of worship: one who knows that he does not have the means to complete prayer, fasting, or Hajj is not initially obligated for that. Then the power of actions does not remain and what is not present is not possible, and obligation is binding. And likewise Zakat is obligatory by wealth and conditions even if it is possible that payment is hindered by excuses, and there is no power except by Allah. And upon that comes revelation and the agreement of tongues on asking Allah for help and strength for what He commanded of acts of worship. For if that power were present or worship were to fall due to its absence, then the request would be a request of injustice and the command would be ingratitude for the strength He bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned the binding of obligation without it, and there is no power except by Allah. And upon that is the statement of Shu'ayb: 'I only intend reform as much as I am able' - he affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of capacity, and there is no power except by Allah. Then in establishing power is the realization of the meaning for which the claim of two [gods] is invalidated, which is that each of them would be able to negate what the other wants to affirm, or one would conceal what the other's knowledge does not reach. So who empowers the slave over what Allah does not know to not be and to make Him a liar in what [؟]
Source pages p. 857

Commentary
This passage provides the proof that obligation is based on the capacity of conditions (asbab) rather than the actual power of action. Maturidi first states that the evidence is from revelation and reason. For revelation, he points to verses that negate capacity in certain situations, followed by commands and rebukes. For reason, he appeals to the intellect's perception. He then elaborates with the example of Hajj: the verse makes Hajj obligatory for those who have the 'means' (sabil) of provision and transportation. If obligation required actual power to perform the action, then no one would be obligated because actual power only arises at the moment of travel, creating a vicious cycle. Similarly for Jihad: if a person lacks means, he is not called. Even for prayer, fasting, and other acts, one may fulfill them through substitution if unable, showing that obligation is tied to conditions, not actual power. He also notes that asking God for help in worship would be unjust if capacity were already present. Finally, he connects this to tawhid: if the slave had independent power, it would imply two gods, since each could negate the other's will. Thus the correct view of capacity supports divine unity.

معونة
شعيب
استطاعة
اثنين
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that humans have independent power of action, separate from God's creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this would lead to shirk (polytheism) because independent power would mean multiple gods, each able to negate the other's will.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would be the consequence if humans already possessed the power to perform worship?
A) Asking God for help would be a request of injustice
B) Worship would be easier
C) Tawhid would be strengthened
D) The slave would be independent

Key Takeaway
The correct understanding of human capacity—derived from God, not independent—upholds tawhid and invalidates shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you next pray 'Ihdinā al-ṣirāṭ al-mustaqīm' (Guide us to the straight path), do you truly feel your absolute need for Allah's guidance every moment, or do you take it as a formality? This lesson shows that asking for help is proof that capacity is from God—so how sincere is your asking?
?
Prophet Shu'ayb said 'I only intend reform as much as I am able.' In your own life, is there an area where you claim to rely on Allah but secretly trust your own strength—perhaps your career, your family, or your personal development? What would it look like to truly say 'there is no power except by Allah' about that area?
?
If you genuinely internalized that every bit of your ability comes from Allah alone, would you still react to your successes with pride and to your failures with despair? How does this lesson challenge the subtle shirk in your heart that makes you feel self-sufficient?

Refuting Dualism Through the Concept of Power
Maturidi refutes dualism by analyzing the implications of divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses rational analysis of divine power to refute the claim that two independent creators could coexist.

Core Idea
Two independent powers would conflict, making each unable to be truly divine.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi presents a rational argument that goes beyond scriptural rejection of dualism. He shows that the very concept of power (qudra) implies that if there were two gods, each would have the ability to negate the other's will—leading to absurdities like one god being able to make the other a liar or ignorant. This argument establishes that true divinity requires exclusive, uncontested power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a compressed logical style.
2
Identify the central claim
Find the statement that establishing power (qudra) invalidates dualism. Understand that this is a rational argument, not just scriptural.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Maturidi shows that if each of two beings had power, each could negate the other's will. This leads to the absurd consequence that one could make the other a liar or ignorant.
This is the key move: the possibility of mutual negation proves incompatibility with divinity.
4
Reflect on the final analogy
Maturidi concludes that even the most foolish person would not empower someone to overturn their authority, so how could God do so? This reinforces the impossibility.
This drives home the point that dualism is rationally untenable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم فى اثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذى له أبطل القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفى ما يريد الآخر اثباته، أو يسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر، فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن لا يكون وعلى أن يجعله كاذبا فيما أخبر به، وعلى أن يتلف ما أراد الله إبقاءه قدر على تسفيه الله وتجهيله وخلفه في الوعد، ومن ذلك وصفه ليس بإله، وبمثله نفوا قول الثنوية. مع ما في هذا أمر عجيب أن يكون الله يقوى أحدا على نقض ربوبيته؛ إذ ملك تصييره كاذبا وقدر على جعله جاهلا، وعن وفاء ما وعده عاجزا. وهذا النوع من الأقدار لا يفعله أسفه السفهاء، فكيف أحكم الحاكمين، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then, in establishing power (qudra) is the verification of the meaning by which the statement of dualism (al-qawl bi-ithnayn) is invalidated. That is, that each of the two would be able to negate what the other wishes to affirm, or one of them would conceal what the other's knowledge does not reach. Thus, whoever enables the servant to do what Allah does not know will not be, and to make Him a liar in what He has informed, and to destroy what Allah wishes to preserve, that one has power to make Allah foolish, ignorant, and to break His promise. From that, describing Him as not being God—by such they refute the statement of the dualists (al-thunawiyya). Along with this, there is a wondrous matter: that Allah would empower anyone to overturn His lordship, for he would have the power to make Him a liar, the power to make Him ignorant, and to make Him incapable of fulfilling His promise. This type of empowerment is not done by the most foolish of fools, so how [could it be done] by the Most Just of judges? And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 858

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of dualism (the belief in two creators). Maturidi states that establishing God's power (qudra) provides the meaning that invalidates the dualist position. The key point: if there were two independent beings with power, each could negate the other's will—one could affirm what the other denies, or one could conceal something from the other's knowledge. Maturidi then reduces the dualist position to absurdity: if a created servant were given power over things that God does not will or know, that servant could make God a liar in His promises, destroy what God wants to preserve, and thereby accuse God of foolishness and ignorance. Such a description would mean that being is not God. Thus, dualism is refuted. Maturidi emphasizes the absurdity: God would never empower anyone to overturn His lordship, for that would mean empowering someone to make God a liar, ignorant, and incapable. Even the most foolish of humans would not do such a thing, so how could it be attributed to the All-Wise?

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra)
ثنوية (thunawiyya)
ربوبية (rububiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism is only refuted by scriptural proofs, not rational argument.
Correction: Maturidi provides a rational argument based on the nature of power, showing that even without scripture, dualism is logically impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the absurd consequence Maturidi uses to refute dualism?
A) Two gods would have to share power
B) Each would have power to negate the other's will, leading to imperfection
C) They would create the same things
D) They would not need each other

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes dualism by showing that two independent powers would conflict, leading to absurdities that cannot be attributed to any true deity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where your plans clash with what Allah has decreed, do you resent His lordship or submit to His wisdom? Where in your life have you been arrogantly trying to 'overturn' His will?
?
Maturidi argues that even the most foolish person would not empower someone to make him a liar. Do you trust Allah's promises with the same certainty that you trust a friend's word? What promise of Allah do you find hardest to rely on?
?
If the concept of power itself disproves any partner with Allah, then why do you sometimes act as if your own power (or the power of others) can achieve things without His permission? Commit today to acknowledging His exclusive power in one specific fear you carry.

Interpreting Capacity and Refuting a False View
Maturidi interprets capacity verse and refutes a false view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's interpretation of the verse on capacity and his refutation of a view that would make God's obligation exceed human capacity.

Core Idea
God never obligates beyond what a person can bear; justice requires alignment of obligation and capacity.

Maturidi begins by reaffirming the correct interpretation of a key Quranic verse. He then explicitly rejects a view that would nullify obligation at the time of the act, which would effectively burden a soul beyond its capacity. This sets the foundation for a deeper discussion on divine justice and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic and its literal translation to grasp Maturidi's concise style.
Notice how he uses 'qabih' (ugly) to describe the refuted view.
2
Identify the two parts of the passage
The passage has two main components: the interpretation of the verse and the refutation of a false opinion. Locate each.
The refutation is indicated by 'wa bayyana qubha qawlihi'.
3
Understand why the refuted view is ugly
Maturidi argues that dropping obligation at the time of act and negating power makes the obligated person beyond capacity, which contradicts divine justice.
This connects to the broader principle that God does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.
4
Reflect on the relevance
Consider how this refutation upholds the balance between divine decree and human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا تأويل قوله: لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا، وبينا قبح قوله في إسقاط التكليف وقت الفعل وإبطال القدرة عليه، فيصير في التحصيل المكلف على غير الوسع. على أنه يقال : كيف لو كان في علم لا يفعل، أو في علمه أنه يريد الفعل في الوقت الذي يتلوه، ومن قولكم إن من أراد الفعل في الوقت الذي يتلوه إنه يفعله لا محالة، إلا أن يمنع أن يفعله، أيمنع أو يفعل ضده؟ فإن قال : يفعل ضده أبطل قوله في كون الإرادة قبل الفعل وألزم نفسه الأمر معه والقدرة معه وبطل قولهم في الإرادة الموجبة، وإن قال : يمنع، فقد ألزم من فى علم الله أنه لا يفعل التكليف بقوة تمنع عن الفعل، وهو في التحقيق تكليف العاجز الممنوع، وإن كان برفع الكلفة أبطل أن يكون أحد ممن في علم الله أنه لا يعطيه مما تضمنته المحنة ولزمه الأمر والنهي، وذلك غاية ما ينتهى إليه القول في القبح. وعلى ذلك أمر الإرادة، إن الله إذ يمنعه عن الفعل الذي في حكمه أنه لا يفعله لا بد أن يمنعه كالإرادة، وفى ذلك منع عن الطاعة إذ يمنعه عن الفعل الذى فى علمه أنه لا يفعله لا بد أن يمنعه بالإرادة، وفى ذلك منع عن الطاعة عنده والخير. ثم يقال : المروى عن الذي روى أنه سنل سيفه على رسول الله فمنعه الله بقبض يده، أكان ذلك المنع أصلح له في الدين وأخير له أو الإطلاق ؟ فإن قال : الإطلاق، فقد أقرّ بأن الله قد يفعل بعباده.
And we have explained the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not charge a soul except [within] its capacity' (2:286). And we have explained the ugliness of his saying in dropping obligation at the time of act and nullifying power upon it, so that in actuality the obligated is beyond capacity. Moreover, it is said: How if it is in [His] knowledge that he will not act, or in His knowledge that he intends the act at the time that follows, and your saying that whoever intends the act at the time that follows, he will do it necessarily, unless prevented from doing it? Does He prevent or does He make him do its opposite? If he says: He makes him do its opposite, he nullifies his saying that will is before the act, and imposes upon himself that command and ability are with it, and their saying about the necessitating will is invalid. And if he says: He prevents, then he imposes upon one whom God knows will not act, the obligation with a power that prevents from the act, and that is in reality an obligation upon the incapable prevented one. And if it is by raising the burden, he nullifies that anyone about whom God knows that He will not give him from what the trial entails, and the command and prohibition become necessary for him. And that is the utmost extent of the saying about ugliness. And upon that is the matter of will. Indeed, when God prevents him from the act which in His judgment he will not do, He must prevent him, such as by will. And in that is prevention from obedience, as He prevents him from the act which in His knowledge he will not do, He must prevent him by will. And in that is prevention from obedience and good in his view. Then it is said: The narrated [story] about the one who drew his sword upon the Messenger of Allah, and Allah prevented him by grasping his hand: Was that prevention better for him in religion and more beneficial for him, or the letting go? If he says: The letting go, then he has affirmed that Allah may do to His servants...
Source pages p. 868

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about divine justice and human capacity. Maturidi interprets the Quranic verse (2:286) that God does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. He refutes a view that nullifies obligation (taklif) at the time of action and invalidates power (qudra) upon it, which would effectively obligate beyond capacity. Then he engages in a dialectical analysis: If God knows a person will not perform an act, or knows he intends it at a future time, then according to the opponent's own principle, the person will necessarily do it unless prevented. Maturidi examines two possibilities: God either makes him do the opposite or prevents him. Both lead to contradictions. The first nullifies the opponent's claim that will precedes the act; the second imposes obligation on one who is incapable (because prevented). This shows that God's knowledge and will do not conflict with justice. Then he uses the story of a man who drew his sword on the Prophet and was prevented by God. The question: was that prevention better for him in religion or releasing him? This tests the opponent's view about God's actions being for the best (al-aslah). The implication is that God's actions are wise even if they appear to prevent good.

Key Terms
التكليف
الوسع
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God might obligate a person to do something they are incapable of.
Correction: Maturidi shows that such a view is 'qabih' (ugly) because the verse explicitly states that God's obligation is within capacity; any opinion suggesting otherwise is a misinterpretation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what happens if obligation is dropped at the time of the act and power is nullified?
A) The person becomes excused.
B) The person is obligated beyond capacity.
C) The person is still obligated.
D) The person has free will.

Key Takeaway
Divine obligation always aligns with human capacity; any view that suggests otherwise is both incorrect and morally objectionable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult religious obligation, do you ever doubt that you have the capacity to fulfill it? How does this verse challenge that doubt?
?
Reflect on a time you felt that an obligation was too heavy for you. In light of this lesson, what might you have been misunderstanding about God's justice and your own capacity?
?
Are there areas in your life where you have dropped an obligation, thinking it was beyond you, without considering that the power to act comes at the moment of action? What will you do about it starting today?

Dialectical Analysis of Knowledge, Will, and Prevention
Maturidi presents a dialectical argument on knowledge and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's dialectical argument showing that God's knowledge and will do not conflict with justice, and how two possibilities both lead to contradictions for the opponent.

Core Idea
God's foreknowledge and will do not impose injustice; the opponent's own principles lead to absurdities.

Maturidi now engages in a sophisticated dialectical exchange with the opponent. He examines two scenarios based on God's knowledge and the opponent's claim about the necessity of action when will exists. By exploring the outcomes of prevention versus causing the opposite, he demonstrates that the opponent's position collapses into self-contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read carefully to follow the conditional reasoning and the two branches of the argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'aiman'a aw yaf'alu diddahu?' (Does He prevent or make him do its opposite?).
2
Trace the first possibility: causing the opposite
If God makes the person do the opposite of the intended act, the opponent's claim that will precedes the act is nullified. Also, it implies that command and ability coincide with the act, invalidating the idea of a necessitating will.
3
Trace the second possibility: prevention
If God prevents the act, then the obligation is placed on someone who is incapable due to prevention, which is an obligation on the incapable and thus unjust.
Maturidi calls this 'taklif al-'ajiz al-mamnu'' (obligation of the prevented incapable).
4
Understand the final conclusion
Both branches lead to absurdities, showing the opponent's position on God's will and human action is untenable.
Maturidi concludes this section by stating that this is the utmost extent of the saying about ugliness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا تأويل قوله: لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا، وبينا قبح قوله في إسقاط التكليف وقت الفعل وإبطال القدرة عليه، فيصير في التحصيل المكلف على غير الوسع. على أنه يقال : كيف لو كان في علم لا يفعل، أو في علمه أنه يريد الفعل في الوقت الذي يتلوه، ومن قولكم إن من أراد الفعل في الوقت الذي يتلوه إنه يفعله لا محالة، إلا أن يمنع أن يفعله، أيمنع أو يفعل ضده؟ فإن قال : يفعل ضده أبطل قوله في كون الإرادة قبل الفعل وألزم نفسه الأمر معه والقدرة معه وبطل قولهم في الإرادة الموجبة، وإن قال : يمنع، فقد ألزم من فى علم الله أنه لا يفعل التكليف بقوة تمنع عن الفعل، وهو في التحقيق تكليف العاجز الممنوع، وإن كان برفع الكلفة أبطل أن يكون أحد ممن في علم الله أنه لا يعطيه مما تضمنته المحنة ولزمه الأمر والنهي، وذلك غاية ما ينتهى إليه القول في القبح. وعلى ذلك أمر الإرادة، إن الله إذ يمنعه عن الفعل الذي في حكمه أنه لا يفعله لا بد أن يمنعه كالإرادة، وفى ذلك منع عن الطاعة إذ يمنعه عن الفعل الذى فى علمه أنه لا يفعله لا بد أن يمنعه بالإرادة، وفى ذلك منع عن الطاعة عنده والخير. ثم يقال : المروى عن الذي روى أنه سنل سيفه على رسول الله فمنعه الله بقبض يده، أكان ذلك المنع أصلح له في الدين وأخير له أو الإطلاق ؟ فإن قال : الإطلاق، فقد أقرّ بأن الله قد يفعل بعباده.
And we have explained the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not charge a soul except [within] its capacity' (2:286). And we have explained the ugliness of his saying in dropping obligation at the time of act and nullifying power upon it, so that in actuality the obligated is beyond capacity. Moreover, it is said: How if it is in [His] knowledge that he will not act, or in His knowledge that he intends the act at the time that follows, and your saying that whoever intends the act at the time that follows, he will do it necessarily, unless prevented from doing it? Does He prevent or does He make him do its opposite? If he says: He makes him do its opposite, he nullifies his saying that will is before the act, and imposes upon himself that command and ability are with it, and their saying about the necessitating will is invalid. And if he says: He prevents, then he imposes upon one whom God knows will not act, the obligation with a power that prevents from the act, and that is in reality an obligation upon the incapable prevented one. And if it is by raising the burden, he nullifies that anyone about whom God knows that He will not give him from what the trial entails, and the command and prohibition become necessary for him. And that is the utmost extent of the saying about ugliness. And upon that is the matter of will. Indeed, when God prevents him from the act which in His judgment he will not do, He must prevent him, such as by will. And in that is prevention from obedience, as He prevents him from the act which in His knowledge he will not do, He must prevent him by will. And in that is prevention from obedience and good in his view. Then it is said: The narrated [story] about the one who drew his sword upon the Messenger of Allah, and Allah prevented him by grasping his hand: Was that prevention better for him in religion and more beneficial for him, or the letting go? If he says: The letting go, then he has affirmed that Allah may do to His servants...
Source pages p. 868

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about divine justice and human capacity. Maturidi interprets the Quranic verse (2:286) that God does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. He refutes a view that nullifies obligation (taklif) at the time of action and invalidates power (qudra) upon it, which would effectively obligate beyond capacity. Then he engages in a dialectical analysis: If God knows a person will not perform an act, or knows he intends it at a future time, then according to the opponent's own principle, the person will necessarily do it unless prevented. Maturidi examines two possibilities: God either makes him do the opposite or prevents him. Both lead to contradictions. The first nullifies the opponent's claim that will precedes the act; the second imposes obligation on one who is incapable (because prevented). This shows that God's knowledge and will do not conflict with justice. Then he uses the story of a man who drew his sword on the Prophet and was prevented by God. The question: was that prevention better for him in religion or releasing him? This tests the opponent's view about God's actions being for the best (al-aslah). The implication is that God's actions are wise even if they appear to prevent good.

Key Terms
العلم
الإرادة
المنع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's foreknowledge forces actions and removes human responsibility.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this alleged forcing leads to contradictions; instead, divine knowledge and justice are compatible with human capacity.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the consequence of saying God causes the opposite of the intended act?
A) It affirms divine mercy.
B) It nullifies the opponent's claim that will precedes the act.
C) It proves human free will.
D) It justifies God's prevention.

Key Takeaway
Both logical outcomes of the opponent's view lead to absurdity, demonstrating that God's will and knowledge do not violate justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself blaming God for your failures, thinking 'He knew I would sin, so it was out of my control'? How does Maturidi's argument challenge that excuse? Will you stop using God's foreknowledge as a shield and instead take full responsibility for your choices starting today?
?
The opponent in this passage assumed that if God prevents an act, it would be unjust. But what about your own heart? Are there areas where you feel God has 'prevented' you from doing good, leaving you feeling unjustly treated? How will you respond to that feeling with the truth that God's justice is perfect and that He never obligates you beyond your capacity?
?
If both 'God causes the opposite' and 'God prevents' lead to absurdity, then God's knowledge and will are perfectly compatible with your free choices. How will this truth change the way you approach your next difficult decision? Will you act with confidence that your efforts are meaningful and that God's will does not crush your responsibility?

Prevention, Will, and the Story of the Sword
Maturidi discusses prevention by will and uses a story to challenge al-aslah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that God's prevention by will is coherent, and his use of a historical example to challenge the doctrine of al-aslah (the best).

Core Idea
God's prevention by will is part of divine wisdom; even prevention can be better than letting an act occur.

Maturidi continues by connecting prevention to divine will. He argues that when God prevents an act He knows will not occur, the prevention must be by His will. This prevention, though it appears to hinder obedience, is part of divine justice. He then invokes a concrete historical example: a man who drew his sword on the Prophet Muhammad and was prevented by God. This story serves to test the opponent's doctrine that God always does what is most beneficial (al-aslah).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the whole passage to see how Maturidi links prevention to will and to the story.
Notice the shift from abstract argument to concrete example.
2
Understand the role of will in prevention
Maturidi asserts that God's prevention is necessarily by will, and this prevention includes preventing obedience and good from that person's perspective.
This counters the idea that God's will always leads to good for the person.
3
Analyze the story of the sword
The story asks: was the prevention (grasping the hand) better for that man in religion or the letting go (allowing him to strike) better? If the opponent says letting go is better, then he admits God may not do the most beneficial for His servants, undermining his own doctrine.
4
Draw the implication
Maturidi uses this to show that God's actions are not bound by what humans consider 'best'; divine wisdom may involve prevention that appears contrary to benefit.

?

?
